# Mode B: Settlement maps (hamlets, villages, towns, provincial cities)

This file is the Mode B half of the /diagram skill: settlement maps built by the parametric generator ([`settlement.py`](settlement.py)) and gated by the validator ([`check_village.py`](check_village.py)).  Read [`SKILL.md`](SKILL.md) first for everything shared (principles, workflow, labeling, style conventions, render pipeline, output convention); this file adds the settlement vocabulary, the spec → validator → persona workflow, and the historical grounding behind the realism checks.

Settlement maps are landscape plans - a hamlet, village, or town sitting in its fields - not interior building plans. They reuse every shared convention in [`SKILL.md`](SKILL.md) and add the vocabulary and workflow below.

### Architecture: a shared library + thin per-settlement specs

The common machinery lives in [`settlement.py`](settlement.py) (the `Settlement` class). A specific settlement is a **thin spec** that imports it, declares its fields/water/shrine/houses, and calls `finish()`. Worked examples, smallest to largest:

- [`pool/hamlets/moritono.gen.py`](pool/hamlets/moritono.gen.py) - a **hamlet** (no headman/shrine/tax-free), three small fields fed by a cascading stream, plus two features beyond the usual vocabulary: a **forest** (`s.forest(west_edge, ...)`) filling the east, and the county magistrate's **walled manor** (`s.manor(...)`, a hunting lodge - a Mode A compound shown as a feature, a samurai estate adjacent to but not part of the hamlet).
- [`pool/villages/kikuta.gen.py`](pool/villages/kikuta.gen.py) - an average **village**, **pond-fed**, ONE contiguous comb-fan field, nucleated cluster + communal fengshui windbreak, a Shrine to Benten reached by a **7-torii approach avenue on flat ground** (no hill), the burial ground in the same precinct. Rebuilt on the water-first engine.
- [`pool/villages/hikari-no-sato.gen.py`](pool/villages/hikari-no-sato.gen.py) - an average **village**, **stream-fed** (no pond), ONE great V-shaped common field with an internal fallow patch (no abandonment), a ring of small fields fed field-to-field, a modest 2-torii Benten shrine at the southern torii gateway (NOT on a hill), and a second Bishamon shrine in the southwest.
- [`pool/towns/hoshizora.gen.py`](pool/towns/hoshizora.gen.py) - an **unwalled town** (county seat, ~1,200 people). Imperial Road spine; a stream crossing the map obliquely to the road with the land falling SSW along both (`downhill`/`down_deg=115`); the farm zone is a **water-first comb wedged between stream and road** - sluice ON the stream bank (a weir), delivery ditches down-slope, the drain collector emptying into a small **drainage tameike** at the low road-bend corner (`pond_role="drainage"`) - plus a second comb running off the east edge (its own brook in, drain discharging off-map); a dense urban core (merchants/laborers/servants aligned to the road), a town **monastery** with a torii, the magistrate's walled manor + samurai houses, a segregated burakumin quarter, a theater stage by the monastery, **hayfield/grazing pastures** ringing barns, and a small forest - terrain features (forest, pasture, one field) run OFF the map edge. Town comb grain: at 1 ft/px `plot_across=58`, `row_step=(52,72)` (~0.08-acre bunded paddies, mid premodern; the old 66px quilt figure would put build_comb's 2x-plot_across offtake floor above the short town canals and starve the delivery net - the "why" lives in the gen docstring). **Town farmsteads run the NUCLEATED to-scale homestead bundle** (`toscale=True, nucleated=True` + `s._nucleated=True`, the same placement algorithm as the villages: house + strictly-south threshing yard + adaptive sunny garden + reserved north kura, footprint-tested against the paddies) - the legacy house-first path center-tested fields (+14px) and let a 44px town house sink a corner into the crop (GM, 2026-07). No per-farm groves (a nucleus shelters itself): the greenery is a communal `village_grove` windbreak on the windward upland + leafy copse scatter through the rows. **Windbreak COMPOSITION rule (GM 2026-07, now AUTOMATED as `village_windbreak_embraces_cluster`): the belt must NESTLE against each farm cluster's windward fringe**, a band wide enough to reach open ground (clumps drawn only over the packed rows thin to scatter - a band must bridge from the rows INTO clear ground to take). Corner forest masses alone are decoration, not a wind wall; a multi-cluster town needs a hugging band per cluster, merging into the corner masses where they meet. *Why this is NOT an automated check*: only `village_windbreak_present` + `village_windbreak_on_windward_side` are automated (presence + centroid direction). A windward-canopy-within-R shelter metric was calibrated across every nucleated map (2026-07) and CANNOT separate approved forms from bad ones - Kikuta's approved ribbon-form belt scores 4-18% while corner-blob layouts score 29-45% - so the embrace property is automated via the FORM-AWARE adjacency metric instead: at least one substantial windbreak grove (>= 12 clumps) within 150px of a farmhouse (approved maps nestle at 37-131px; maps whose wood is a real M['forest'] are exempt - Moritono nestles against the forest itself). The in-field paddy flourishes (pocket pond / rock / grave island) are gated OFF at town+city scale - at the 1 ft/px grain the GM read them as a pond and an ossuary standing in the rice.
- [`pool/towns/hirameki.gen.py`](pool/towns/hirameki.gen.py) - a **walled town**. The rampart is an irregular hill-anchored arc (`s.wall(...)`) whose two ends **climb partway up the hill flanks**; the **north flank is a steep hachured hill** (`s.hill(..., steep=True)`) carrying the magistrate's manor, so the slope defends that side instead of a wall; a front gate with guard station + guardtower; and a **chrysanthemum field** (`s.flower_field(...)`, the Imperial flower) kept INSIDE the walls, abutting the inner face (the wall bulges out around it). Its FIVE fields are water-first combs showing every legal water topology at once: own feeder brooks off the north edge fully diverted at the sluice (w1/e1, the akagahara pattern), a brook in from the west edge (w2, off-edge field), a **field-to-field CASCADE** (e2 fed by a drawn `frm=drain -> to=field` connector carrying e1's collector surplus - the check-side cascade-reuse source clause + the engine's `source={"kind":"cascade"}`), and a stream diverted bodily into an irrigation head (s1 swallows the west stream's lower course). Collector culverts return runoff to the streams; each drain gets a `toe_block()` no-build band so nudged farmsteads can never end below the collector.
- [`pool/provincial-cities/tango.gen.py`](pool/provincial-cities/tango.gen.py) - a **walled provincial city** (the city scale). A closed `s.city_wall(...)` ring with N and S gates, an `s.moat(...)` fed by an off-map stream, the Imperial road straight through gate-to-gate with a guard house + inspection station + tower at each gate, `s.governor_mansion(...)` + six `s.ministry(...)` offices (Rites in the temple neighborhood), a crossing-grid street network of dense neighborhoods (~600 buildings - tight rows packed in the blocks), quartered districts (NW agricultural + in-wall burakumin, NE laborers, SW merchants + temple, SE government + samurai), and a few dispersed samurai estates (the nearest 1-3 shown) outside to the SE, the rest off-map.

**What is COMMON (lives in `settlement.py`, do not duplicate per village):** the palette and SVG defs; organic field outlines (bbox-based OR an arbitrary base polygon like a V) with non-uniform crop basins and per-plot angled rows; the south-facing pitched-roof house glyph; size-aware, corridor-aware, field-blocking house placement; hills + summit shrines + torii; ponds, off-map streams, and winding channels; tax-free plot picking (interior-validated); the manifest emission. When you need a NEW shared capability (a new field shape, a new building type), add it to the library, not to one village.

**What is SETTLEMENT-SPECIFIC (declared in the thin spec + echoed into `manifest["meta"]`):** field count/shape/placement; the irrigation **source** (pond vs stream vs field-to-field) - water *must exist*, but the kind varies by region (a pond/*tameike* suits a dry locale; a stream diversion suits a river valley - not every village had a pond); torii count; whether the main shrine sits on a hill or stands central on flat ground; whether blight left abandoned houses (a knob; no current map uses it); additional shrines; the settlement scale and (for towns) the holding clan, walls, slope, and monastery dedications. The validator reads `meta` and each channel's `frm`/`to` anchors, so it adapts per settlement instead of assuming one layout - see the knob reference next.

### Settlement `meta()` and the per-settlement knobs

A settlement's identity and the rules the gate applies to it are declared with `s.meta(...)` (echoed into `manifest["meta"]`) plus two `Settlement` attributes. **This is also the persistence mechanism:** the knobs live in the `.gen.py` source, so every regeneration re-applies them and the gate fails loudly if a pass ever drops one - which is why these maps survive dozens of re-generation passes without losing their identity. Annotate non-obvious knobs with a comment explaining *why* (a changed-hands town, an intentional single monastery), so the reasoning travels with the data.

- `name=` - the place name (the title block).
- `scale=` - `"hamlet"` | `"village"` | `"town"`. Drives nearly everything downstream: headman/shrine presence, the house-count band, the religious tier, and which town rules switch on.
- **The headman is a FARMSTEAD, not an exception** (GM 2026-07-21, caught on Hikari no Sato): `s.headman(x, y)` routes through the standard homestead bundle in BOTH settlement styles (nucleated AND dispersed), so the grandest house in the village gets its threshing yard + dooryard garden like every other farm - capped to an ORDINARY farm's appurtenance sizes in both paths (a big house does not mean a field-sized saien; `garden_area_within_norms` holds). In the dispersed style the bundle brings the per-house grove too when room allows, and the solver drops it gracefully in a dense cluster (neighbor tree cover shelters the house - the grove is the one optional part). `harvest_yards_present` and `gardens_present` no longer exempt `role=="headman"` - that carve-out was written around the old lone-house headman bug. **And the headman ALWAYS has an attached fireproof kura** (`headman_has_kura`, GM 2026-07-21): the shoya/nanushi is by definition among the village's most prosperous farmers, and the office functionally needs one - tax ledgers, land registers, and tax rice awaiting collection are exactly what fireproof storage is for. The ~30% kura roll is for ORDINARY plains (the kura keeps meaning wealth because most farms lack one); the headman sits at the top of that distribution by construction, so `role=="headman"` forces `shed=True`. Watch the knock-on when retrofitting: the headman's larger bundle reservation re-rolls the whole packing sequence, so expect to re-seed the house scatter (Hikari went `SEED + 1` -> `SEED + 4`) or re-order a fixed-coordinate set-apart feature to before the crop (the kura repack shifted Hoshigaoka's west extent and clipped its graveyard).
- **A village/hamlet shrine has a VILLAGE-scale footprint** (`village_shrine_footprint_within_norms`, GM 2026-07-21, caught on Hikari no Sato): the ordinary earth-god/water-mouth hall is ~275 m^2 (30x24 px at 2 ft/px - Ueda, Hoshigaoka), a showcase primary (Kikuta's 7-torii Benten, Hikari's gateway Benten) runs to ~490 m^2 (44x30 px), and the check's ceiling is 600 m^2 - the monastery/temple tier (1,000+ m^2) belongs to towns and cities per the temple-density canon. Hikari's two halls had survived from before these norms at 192x128 / 236x164 ft (small-monastery footprints), which is also why its correctly-sized graveyard read tiny beside the Bishamon hall. `religious_matches_scale` gates the TYPE per tier; this gates the SIZE. Note `s.shrine_well(cx, cy)` takes the HALL CENTER (the ring search finds the nearest clear spot beside it) - Hikari's legacy offset-coordinate calls only passed `remote_shrine_has_own_well` while the halls were oversized.
- `households=N` / `target_houses=N` - village sizing (occupied houses ≈ 0.7 per household, or an explicit count band).
- `walled=True` - a town has a rampart (turns on the wall / gate / main-street / theater-stage-inside checks).
- `torii_expected=N` - exact TOTAL torii count drawn (a blunt map-level assertion; prefer the per-hall `shrine_hall(torii_count=N)` pin, which is what `torii_match_roll` gates - Hirameki and Hoshizora dropped their `torii_expected` pins at the 2026-07-23 re-roll so the per-temple rolls govern).
- `shrine_on_hill=True` - the village shrine sits on the summit, reached by a torii ascent.
- `fallow_implies_abandoned=True` - fallow fields are ringed by abandoned houses (post-blight).
- `downhill=<cardinal name | [dx,dy]>` - the land's slope (so channels can be gated to run downhill); tag it when the gradient is clear (a hill on one side).
- `clan="<Great Clan>"` - the holding clan; sets the town's two default monastery dedications. **ASK the GM if not given.**
- `monastery_fortunes=[...]` - override the monastery dedications (a town that changed hands, or one with a single monastery).
- `theater_stage=False | "outside"` - omit the town theater stage, or allow it outside a walled town.
- `gate_market=False` - suppress the extramural gate market a walled town has by default (a purely military fort, or a depopulated / suppressed gate). See `walled_town_has_gate_market`.
- `fire_tower=False` - omit the fire-watch tower(s) a WALLED town or a city has by default (`walled_town_has_fire_tower` / `city_has_fire_towers`). An open road-town has none either way (see below).
- `windward="NW"` - the compass quarter the prevailing cold wind blows FROM, setting which side each farmstead's homestead grove (*yashikirin*) shelters. Default `"NW"` (the East Asian winter monsoon); override per map (`"N"`/`"NE"`/.../`"NW"`) when local geography - a sea, a mountain wall, the western Burning Sands - sets a different exposure. See `groves_on_windward_side` and "Homestead groves".
- `grove_prevalence=1.0` - the fraction of farmhouses that are homestead-grove candidates (UNIVERSAL by default - a grove is drawn on every farm with windward room). Lower it for a sheltered/atypical microclimate where fewer farms planted a windbreak. `groves_where_possible` honors the knob.
- `inwall_groves=False` - whether farms INSIDE a city wall get groves. Off by default (an intramural plot is sheltered by the urban fabric and on land too precious for a tree belt; `no_groves_inside_walls` enforces it). Set `True` only for an unusual in-wall homestead district.
- `granary=True` - mark a rice-TRANSIT town and require a distinct granary (`s.granary(...)`, gated by `town_has_granary`). OFF by default - a standard county seat's grain sits inside the magistrate's yamen, not drawn separately.
- `flophouses=N` - how many market-day flophouses a town must show (`town_has_flophouse`). Defaults to **1** (default-on); set higher for a busy market hub, or `0` to opt out.
- canvas is `Settlement(W, H, seed=...)` (echoed to `meta.W/H`); **`s.bscale`** (`= 1/ftpx`, set by `meta()`: town 1.0, city ~0.33 - the old hand-tuned 0.82/0.42 values predate the ft/px scale ladder and are gone) shrinks the urban glyphs so every building draws its TRUE feet at the map's scale. **Farmhouses share the same grain** - `s.ring(...)`/`try_place` scale the outside-the-walls farmhouse footprint by `bscale` too, so a peasant farmhouse never renders LARGER than the samurai/merchant houses inside the walls. Because smaller footprints pack the field rings more easily, dropping `bscale` may raise the farmhouse count - at TOWN scale farmhouses count toward `population_consistent_with_housing`, so thin the rings if it overshoots (a CITY excludes farmhouses from its population entirely, so ring freely there).

### Village variation knobs (feature 005) - the roll engine, the Family-A catalog, the twin-detector

Two villages with the SAME water direction (`down_deg`) used to come out near-identical (Kikuta was a copy of Hoshigaoka down to the headman's house position), because the generator fixed one value on every layout axis. Feature 005 replaces those hidden constants with **historically-typed, seed-rolled knobs**, and adds a pool-level check that mechanically guards against re-twinning.

**The roll engine** (`settlement.py`: `Knob`, `knob_rng`, `register_knob`, `resolve_knob`, and the `Settlement.pin_knob`/`resolve`/`knob_context` surface). A spec MAY **pin** any knob; every unpinned knob is resolved by an **independent, deterministic roll off the map seed** (`knob_rng` derives a per-knob sub-seed with SHA-256 - Python's `hash()` is per-process salted, so it can't give cross-run determinism), filtered by the knob's **typing rule**. Resolution order is **pinned → rolled → default**; a pinned value that is out of its value space or violates its typing rule is a loud error, never silently drawn. *Why independent per knob, not preset "village-type" bundles (research.md D3):* independent draws give the widest variety and make "pin one knob, roll the rest" natural, while the per-knob typing rules - not a bundle - keep a combination historically coherent.

**The Family-A catalog** (registered at import; China-first value spaces + typing rules, per research.md D2). The typing rules read the village's stated geography from the context (`water_kind`, `field_origin`, `scale`, ...) so a roll respects it:
- `cluster_position` (high_margin / flank / mid_margin / valley_mouth / valley_head / on_rise) - villages sat on whatever non-arable higher/drier ground existed; 背山面水 ("back to the hill, face the water") orients the back to high ground and the face to water, but which corner that is depends on the valley, so the "high windward margin" is one common case, not the only one.
- `cluster_shape` (round / elongated / crescent / split) - cluster shape followed the available dry ground: a knoll gives a round blob, a levee a linear string, a field-edge a crescent, two flanking patches a 2-hamlet split. *Typing:* `split` needs room for two hamlets to read separately (a village/town, not a hamlet).
- `lane_skeleton` (spine / T / Y / cross / waterside) - a nucleated village's lanes followed its site: a spine along a ridge, a T where a spur met the field track, a Y where two approaches merged, a cross at a small market node (草市), a waterside lane in a stream village. The headman compound and the primary-shrine gateway are **derived from the skeleton's focal points** (`skeleton_layout` / `Settlement.lane_skeleton`), never a fixed pixel offset - which is precisely why two same-water villages stop sharing a headman position. *Typing:* `waterside` needs water running ALONG the cluster (a stream/canal beside it), so it is excluded for a pond-fed valley whose only water is a valley-head reservoir uphill.
- `water_source_position` (pond: corner_{NW,NE,SW,SE} / mid_margin / chain; stream: edge_{N,E,S,W}) - a *tameike* sat wherever the catchment delivered water above the command area (not always the NW corner); small villages often had a chain of little ponds rather than one big reservoir; a stream diversion entered from whichever edge the valley fed. *Typing:* the `edge_*` entries need a stream source and the pond positions need a pond; gravity feed (source uphill of the intake) is enforced at placement, not as a value exclusion.
- `plot_size` (small_irregular / medium / large_block / strip) + `plot_regularity` (organic / grid) - plot size and regularity varied with land-division history: tiny hand-shaped plots in old organically-grown fields, rectilinear blocks under a survey/allotment system (the 条里 *jōri* grid in Japan; well-field/allotment remnants in China), long strips under strip tenancy. *Typing:* a `grid` bund pattern implies a planned/surveyed field, so it is excluded unless `field_origin="planned"`.
- `grain_drift` (degrees off the fall-line) - real valleys let the paddy grain drift rather than holding one rigid angle; this resolves the "uniform 45° grain" residual flagged under Fields. Always allowed. Wired through `build_comb(..., grain_drift=)` (offsets the dry-plot contour heading, so the recorded `theta` - and the twin-detector's `grain_orient` - shift without moving any plot polygon).

Generator surface for the shipped knobs: `s.lane_skeleton(kind, cx, cy, ex, ey)` lays the lanes and returns the DERIVED `headman`/`gateway` focal points; `s.cluster_seeds(shape, cx, cy, ex, ey, n, rng)` yields shape-aware house seeds (round / elongated / crescent / split) to feed `try_place`; `s.line_seeds(p0, p1, n, half_band, rng)` yields a LINEAR ribbon of seeds strung along a road/margin/dike (the `settlement_form="linear"` archetype - houses front a line instead of clustering in a blob; per research.md D5 the cheapest big structural difference between two same-region villages, and the reason Kikuta now reads as a ribbon village against Hoshigaoka's nucleated blob); `s.scatter_seeds(cx, cy, rx, ry, n, rng)` yields an EVEN scatter over a broad area (the `settlement_form="dispersed"` archetype - the kainyo strewn-farmstead pattern; pair it with `s._nucleated = False` so each farm draws its OWN yashikirin grove instead of a communal windbreak). **Sizing caveat for dispersed (grounding):** a dispersed hamlet needs roughly TWICE the margin room per farm as a nucleated one - each homestead carries its own grove and keeps its own spacing (no tight packing), and the bundle solver hugs them all to the field edge into a single-file frontage - so a settlement declared at the nucleated-pack household count will not fit that many dispersed farms in the same margin. Demonstrate `dispersed` on a roomier field (a full village) or declare fewer households, not on a hamlet sized for a nucleated cluster. **Focal-feature catalog** (the optional foci the `focal_set` axis reads): dedicated glyph methods `s.crescent_pond(cx, cy, r, facing_deg)` (半月塘, drawn in the shared water block, reserved as a keep-out; **it labels itself "geomantic pond"** - GM 2026-07-21, the banyuetang is culturally specific and does not read by itself (the one deliberate exception to don't-label-the-obvious), and "geomantic" is the GM's chosen term. *What it is (recorded because the GM asked)*: GEOMANTIC, not religious - no deity, no rites; cosmological engineering like orienting a house south. The village wants "mountain behind, water in front" (背山面水): the hill + fengshui grove are the back half, and where no river obliges the village DIGS the front half - still water gathers and holds qi/wealth where flowing water carries it away, and the HALF shape leaves the lineage room to grow (complete things can only wane). Grove-arc behind + water-arc in front cradle the village as one system; practically it is the rain-fed runoff basin (deliberately UNCONNECTED to irrigation), fire water, fish/duck/washing water, with the flat-side bank as the open threshing/ceremony forecourt. The shrine is where religion happens; the pond is how a well-sited village should be shaped. And **no vegetation touches its water**: the grove placement keeps a full-disk canopy keep-out (the flat-side band doubles as the pond's open forecourt, historically the settlement's ceremony/work ground) and the scrub/reed scatter skips the water like any other water body; gated by `trees_clear_of_fengshui_ponds` + `crescent_pond_labeled`) and `s.mill(x, y, wheel_side)` (水磨, a mill house + waterwheel beside a watercourse); the composition-based foci (a secondary earth-god shrine via `shrine_hall(primary=False)`, an ancestral hall, a market clearing at a lane junction) are recorded with `s.note_focal(kind)` so they read on the manifest without a bespoke glyph. Every focal feature is placed by the same overlap / set-back invariants as hand-authored content and is classified in `check_village`'s overlap system (`crescent_ponds`, `mills`).

**Knob resolvers + the roll-from-seed entrypoint (US2/US3/US4).** Every registered knob now has a geometry *driver*, so a knob is a real lever and not just a recorded label:
- `s.cluster_anchor(position, field_bbox, down_deg)` resolves `cluster_position` (6 dry-margin seats: high_margin / valley_head / mid_margin / flank / valley_mouth / on_rise) into a cluster anchor + margin-oriented extents; off the paddy, off the flood toe. *Grounding (research.md D2):* a village took the best DRY ground beside its paddy (背山面水), and which dry ground was available - the high back, a head terrace, a side levee, a valley-mouth shoulder, a knoll - is the variation.
- `s.water_source_anchor(position, field_bbox, down_deg)` + `s.water_sources_for(down_deg, water_kind)` resolve `water_source_position` into the sluice/stream-entry point on the field's UPHILL margin, and REJECT a downhill (gravity-impossible) source; the roll picks from the legal set. *Grounding:* Chinese canal doctrine feeds a comb from its high end; the varied high-side entry is the knob.
- `s.plot_texture(plot_size, plot_regularity)` maps those two knobs onto `build_comb`'s `(plot_across, row_step)` so the paddy grain actually changes (small = many small paddies, large_block = few big, strip = narrow-long; `grid` tightens the row-step spread into a surveyed look). Sizes are picked in REAL FEET via `waterfields.paddy_grain` (see **Paddy cell size** below), not raw px, so the same knob means the same real paddy at every scale.

##### Paddy cell size (the real-feet calibration; GM 2026-07-22)

Every DRAWN paddy plot is one leveled, diked cell - and because a paddy must hold water at an EVEN depth, that cell is physically small. `plot_across`/`row_step` used to be hand-set in PIXELS per map, so an identical px grain read as ~4x different real area between a 1 ft/px hamlet and a 2 ft/px village, and the villages drifted to ~0.13 acre (bigger than history allows for a single cell). `waterfields.paddy_grain(ftpx, target_acres=PADDY_CELL_ACRES)` now derives `(plot_across, row_step)` from a real-feet target ÷ ftpx, so the paddy is the same real size at every scale.

- **Target = 0.05 acre (~200 m2, ~47 ft square).** *Research (China-first, Japan corroborating; GM asked before choosing):* Francesca Bray, *The Rice Economies* - a leveled paddy "twenty yards square [~0.083 ac / 335 m2] would be considered large," the CEILING for one cell, typical valley cells smaller. J.L. Buck, *Land Utilization in China* (16,786 farms, 1929-33) - avg ~0.06 ha (0.15 ac) OWNERSHIP plots, but a plot subdivides into several leveled cells on any slope, so the cell sits below it. Japanese *se* (畝) = 100 m2 (0.025 ac) is the small-paddy unit (floor); the *tan* (段, ~0.245 ac) is a TAX/allotment unit, not one leveled field. 0.05 ac sits mid-band, above the *se* floor and well under Bray's ceiling, and keeps a drawn plot ~1.7x the 46x28 ft farmhouse glyph so a paddy still visibly outsizes a farmhouse.
- **What changed:** only VILLAGES (were ~0.13 ac, over the ceiling) and CITIES (~0.08 ac, at it) were pulled down; HAMLETS (~0.034) and TOWNS (~0.036-0.057) already sat in-band and were left untouched. `plot_texture`'s size knobs bracket the target (`small_irregular` 0.72x, `medium` 1.0x, `large_block` 1.35x, `strip` = target area but long-and-narrow), so a rolled village (e.g. Kikuta's `small_irregular`) legitimately runs a touch smaller.
- **The population/household invariant is UNTOUCHED (the reason this was safe):** shrinking the CELL subdivides the SAME field envelope into more, smaller cells - total paddy area, the field outline, the farmhouse rings (which key off the envelope), and the household count are all unchanged. A village keeps its farmhouses and population; only the bund grid gets finer. (Verified: Hoshigaoka's field stays 53.7-ac envelope / ~45-ac planted / 70 farmhouses whether cells are 0.12 or 0.05 ac.) `population_consistent_with_housing` counts dwellings, never paddy area, so it never moved.
- **Grain fidelity for ft/px=1 maps:** a map at 1 ft/px should pass `grain=2/ftpx=2` to `build_comb` (the carve's minimum-size thresholds are tuned at the 2 ft/px village grain); cities correctly pass `2/3` and villages default to `1.0`, but the ft/px=1 hamlets/towns historically passed nothing (`grain=1`). That under-fill is why a town's nominal 0.083-ac cell rendered at ~0.04 - which happens to land in-band, so it is left as-is rather than "fixed" into oversize.
- **The leveled-cell principle is UNIVERSAL - it also governs the HILL-RICE archetypes (GM 2026-07-22).** A terrace paddy and a valley-floor ribbon paddy are leveled cells like any comb paddy (water held even), so they are the same ~0.05 ac, not field-wide bands. Both engines used to draw each terrace STEP / ribbon BAND as one plot spanning the full width (~1.4 ac terraces, ~0.5 ac ribbon cells - far over the leveled-cell size); now `build_terraces` splits each step ALONG the contour and `build_ribbon` splits each band ACROSS the valley into ~`PADDY_CELL_ACRES` cells (derived at the map's `ftpx`), and `n_terraces`/`n_bands` are raised so the step depth stays shallow enough that a cell reads wider-than-deep. *Grounding (China-first):* at Longsheng the LARGEST terrace is 0.62 mu (~0.10 acre) and most are far smaller (some hold three rice plants), 15,862 terraces in one village - terraces are SMALL. (This does NOT touch the `polder_grid` / `mulberry_dike_fishpond` archetypes: those parcels are DELIBERATELY larger and already grounded true-scale - Buck's ~1 mu polder parcel, 0.4-0.6 ha ponds - see the polder-parcels note below.)
- **Ratchet:** `test_settlement.py::test_paddy_grain_hits_the_real_feet_target` (the pure derivation) + `test_villages.py` asserts every valley-paddy village/city AND the two hill-rice archetype demos (`contour_terraces` Tanada, `ribbon_valley` Yatsuda) render a typical cell in the calibrated 0.03-0.072-ac band (catching a regression back to the old 0.13-ac villages or the old field-wide terrace/ribbon bands). Not a manifest gate check (villages do not record `plot_polys`), so it lives in the SVG-measuring test tier, same as the ditch z-order audit.
- `s.roll_village(name, households, down_deg, water_kind, field_fall)` **rolls every unpinned knob and builds a complete gate-passing map with ZERO hand-placed coordinates** (SC-004): water source → sluice, plot_texture → grain, cluster_position/shape → homestead cloud (seated constructively on the field's actual drawn edge, biased clear of the intake so it always abuts + rings the field on any fan shape), lane_skeleton → lanes, plus wells / windbreak / bridges / hinterland. Same seed → byte-identical; different seeds → different combinations (`pool/hamlets/shimizu` seed 7, `pool/hamlets/honda` seed 8). It shares `s.draw_comb_field(net, name, source)`, the ~50-line comb-drawing + water-topology helper. *Current scope:* a nucleated hamlet/village; ~1/3 of arbitrary seeds pass the full gate today (the constructive placement is robustened over time), so a shipped rolled map is a chosen passing seed.
- **Completed focal catalog** (T020): beyond `crescent_pond` + `mill`, dedicated glyph methods `s.ancestral_hall` (祠堂), `s.water_mouth` (水口), `s.market` (墟/市), and `s.secondary_shrine` each draw, record, reserve a keep-out, and `note_focal(kind)`.
- **Archetype knobs (US4).** `field_archetype` (valley_paddy / contour_terraces / polder_grid / ribbon_valley / mulberry_dike_fishpond) and `land_use_overlay` (none / mulberry_fishpond / lotus / tea_fringe) are registered with **terrain typing** (research.md D4: terraces need hill ground, polder/dike-pond need low reclaimed ground, tea needs a hill fringe). `s.apply_land_use(net, overlay, rng)` is implemented in full - it recolors a fraction of paddy plots (or a hill-tea fringe) as the overlay crop, gated by the `land_use_overlay_drawn` check (a declared overlay must actually be drawn). **Every overlay value is a PERMANENT use, never a rotation** (GM, 2026-07): an overlay recolors some plots while the rest stay standing rice, so it may only hold crops that coexist with rice in the same season - a dike-pond, a lotus paddy and a hill tea garden are given over all year, so the plot next door can be rice. **RAPE (油菜) was tried and removed**: rice and rape are the two halves of one rotation in the SAME plot (rice May-Oct; rape sown into the drained stubble Oct-Nov, flowering Mar-Apr), so they are never both standing - mixing them at any fraction depicts two seasons at once, and the real spring picture is yellow rape against BARE stubble, not against green rice. Rape belongs on a future SEASONAL axis (a whole-field state), not this per-plot one.

  **LAND-USE OVERLAYS ARE SITED BY TOPOGRAPHY, NOT BY CHANCE (feature 010, `specs/010-land-use-overlay-grounding/research.md`).** The rape failure exposed a second defect that survived it: the overlay picked its plots with a uniform random sample. The corrected rule, which governs every value:

  > **Topography sets which plots are ELIGIBLE; economy decides how many of the eligible plots CONVERT.**

  The old code had only the economic term (`fraction`) and no topographic filter at all, so it drew ponds and lotus on ordinary upper-field rice ground. Eligibility is now the plots the field builders flag `low` (comb = the bottom two levels of each sector, terraces = the lowest 3, polder = the lowest 2 rows, ribbon = the lowest 3 bands). Zero eligible plots means the overlay honestly draws NOTHING rather than falling back to random placement.

  **`low` (topography) is NOT `FLOODED` (the picture) - do not re-conflate them.** `FLOODED` tints a random 45% of the comb's bottom level blue for visual texture, so keying eligibility off the fill made it an accident of RENDERING. The two are now separate fields on the plot record.

  **`fraction` is a share of the ELIGIBLE set, not of the whole field.** As a share of the field it was inert - the eligible set is always smaller, so every village converted 100% of its low ground and the economic term decided nothing. As a share of eligible the two terms vary independently, which is exactly what the evidence demands: Shunde was ~5% dike-pond county-wide while containing townships past 50% the same year, on identical terrain.

  **A CALIBRATED LIBERTY is recorded here** (constitution XII, GM 2026-07-19): the low band is the bottom TWO levels rather than the single hem on the drain. How wide a valley bottom's wet backswamp ran is unrecorded, and the researched extent for a lotus-growing village (a few percent to ~10-15% of field area) is itself interpolated from a national average that includes regions growing none. The single-hem reading put lotus at ~2% - inside the range, but so sparse the knob stopped making villages look distinct, which is the reason it exists. We chose the upper part of a plausible range for a stated non-historical reason (legibility) and disclosed it. What this does NOT do is invent a range: lotus stays strictly on genuinely low ground and cannot touch the upper field. Gated by `overlays_on_wet_ground_only`, whose teeth come from `wet_plots` being written by the FIELD pass while `land_use[].plots` is written by the OVERLAY pass - two independent records, so the check cannot be satisfied by a self-report.

  Per value:

  - **`mulberry_fishpond` (桑基魚塘)** - dug out of 低洼易有洪患之处, the low flood-prone hollows, as a flood adaptation that drained the hollow while raising the dike. **This value was nearly DELETED on a false premise** - that the dike-pond system was only ever a wholesale landscape conversion, so a scatter among rice never existed. The research refuted that outright: the scatter was the system's NORMAL state. Shunde county was ~4.6% dike-pond in 1581 (while containing townships already over 50% the same year); a 1980s survey of the heartland still found rice at 35%, the same share as the fishponds; and at Lake Tai mulberry sat on the *tang* banks with rice remaining the polder's main crop permanently. Gazetteers found *total* absence of rice remarkable enough to record. The wall-to-wall landscape is the rare end state of a ~300-year plot-by-plot process (挖塘培基 - dig one low plot into a pond, pile the spoil into a dike; a one-household, one-dry-season job), which is what the `mulberry_dike_fishpond` ARCHETYPE is for. **The archetype and the overlay are two SCALES of one system, not duplicates - do not delete either.** The archetype opts out of the topographic filter by name (`eligible="all"`), since at that scale the ponds really had engulfed the ordinary ground too. *Negative result worth keeping:* the outer-delta 沙田 *shatian* were equally low and equally wet and **stayed in rice** - low ground is necessary but not sufficient; the dike-pond zone also had smallholder tenure inside an established polder and water access to Canton.
  - **`lotus` (藕田)** - models **deep-water lotus** (深水藕, 30-50cm, tolerating ~1m) against paddy rice's ~5-9cm optimum, so it physically cannot sit on high ground. **Shallow-water lotus** (浅水藕, 10-20cm) in ordinary paddy is equally real but is deliberately NOT modeled: it is an economic choice rotating with rice (稻藕轮作), driven by a layer the generator does not have, and drawing it would be visually indistinguishable from the uniform-random bug this replaced. Read research.md D1 before "restoring" it. *Honest limitation:* the agronomy is solid but pre-modern village-scale practice is not directly sourced - the clearest conversions in the record (Kasumigaura 1970s, contemporary Vietnam) are modern and policy-driven. Extent where present is a few percent up to maybe 10-15% of field area; that range is interpolation, not a sourced figure.
  - **`tea_fringe` (茶)** - already correct, unchanged in code. But the prose describing it as the "upper slope" was WRONG: tea took the **lower-to-mid FERTILE hillside**, never the low lands and never the barren upper slope (Robert Fortune, eyewitness, 1843: "always situated on the lower and most fertile sides of the hills, and never on the low lands"; the upper slopes were forest, sweet potato and peanut). The boundary rule states itself - **the line is the highest irrigation ditch** - which is exactly what `net['dry_plots']` already is. Form is smallholder: recognizable rows in acre-scale patches, several per household, dotted across a hillside, not one contiguous block. **Two anachronism traps:** neat contour-TERRACED tea is post-1949 (a state program; terrace the paddy, not the tea), and bund-margin tea (畦畔茶) is a JAPANESE practice with no Chinese equivalent - do not project it westward.

  **A check was written and then REMOVED for having no teeth** (`dikeponds_are_clustered`). Household-by-household conversion really did spread as patches, and `_pick_overlay_plots` models it - but it is not independently observable, because the eligible set is always a thin contiguous strip of low ground, and every subset of a strip is "clustered" by any nearest-neighbor-vs-span metric. An even random scatter of the same count passed the check, so it would have been a check that cannot fail - worse than no check. It becomes testable if a future archetype ever yields a genuinely 2-D eligible region. ALL FIVE field-GEOMETRY archetypes are now DRAWN: the `valley_paddy` comb (`build_comb`), **`contour_terraces`** (`waterfields.build_terraces` - stacked contour terrace bands stepping down a hillside from the high catchment, a flank supply channel cascading terrace-to-terrace to a foot drain; each step is split ALONG the contour into ~0.05-ac leveled cells - see 'Paddy cell size' - so a step reads as a ROW of small paddies, not one band; demo `pool/hamlets/tanada.gen.py` 棚田, validator `contour_terraces_are_stepped_bands` = >=8 cross-slope retaining bunds, which reads `terrace_bunds` not the cells so the split is transparent to it). *Grounding (research.md D4):* the south-China / SE-Asia rice terrace (Yuanyang 元陽, Longsheng 龍勝) is THE field archetype for HILL ground where valley-bottom paddy is impossible - the defining alternative to the comb. and **`polder_grid`** (`build_polder` - a rectilinear wei-tian 圩田 block of paddies inside a perimeter dike on LOW reclaimed ground; demo `pool/hamlets/enokida.gen.py`, validators `polder_fills_its_bbox` + `polder_parcels_vary`). **`mulberry_dike_fishpond`** (polder geometry + a full mulberry_fishpond overlay = a reclaimed block of dike-ponds, demo `kuwabata.gen.py`, validators `dikepond_is_ponds_in_a_block` + `polder_parcels_vary`), and **`ribbon_valley`** (`build_ribbon` - a long narrow paddy MEANDERING down a confined valley floor, the brook down the center; the valley floor steps down in cross-bunds AND splits across its width into ~0.05-ac leveled cells - see 'Paddy cell size' - so it reads as a chain of small paddies, not one long sheet; demo `yatsuda.gen.py`, validator `ribbon_is_long_and_narrow` checks the field OUTLINE so the split is transparent to it). Each archetype has terrain typing (terraces=hill, polder/dike-pond=low, ribbon=narrow_valley), an archetype-specific validator with a negative fixture, and China-first grounding (research.md D4). A roll with no declared terrain resolves to `valley_paddy`; a declared terrain unlocks its archetype.

  **The polder's PARCEL fabric is a patchwork, never identical cells** (`polder_parcels_vary`; researched + source-verified 2026-07-21; full grounding in `build_polder`'s docstring). The original `build_polder` drew every cell as one identical `cell x cell` square (Kuwabata/Enokida: 66 identical 150-ft squares - the GM flagged it as "not the organically developed farms I'm used to seeing"). The research upheld the instinct: the surveyed rectilinear chessboard of the Taihu *tangpu* 塘浦 system was the CANAL grid at kilometer scale, while the parcels inside it were a private-tenure patchwork - mid-Qing Jiangnan farms averaged ~10 mu scattered over several parcels; Buck's pre-mechanization survey (1929-33) found a mean parcel of ~1 mu, rectangular only where it fronted a straight ditch; dike-ponds accreted household-by-household (挖塘培基, research.md D2), so 66 identical ponds contradict the map's own backstory. Uniform machine-sized rectangles are a 20th-century consolidation look (Japan's 1963 *hojo seibi* 30m x 100m standard; PRC consolidation campaigns). The rework keeps the interior ditch-grid module lines straight (that part was genuinely surveyed - see the `Perimeter dike` note below for the outer dike, which is NOT straight) while most module bays split into 2-3 oblong strips, a few merge into double-bay parcels (along the fall only), and interior bund nodes jitter ~6 px. **Parcels are TRUE SCALE** (GM directive 2026-07-21 - no legibility inflation on to-scale maps): rice polders run a ~110 ft module so parcels average ~1 mu (Buck's mean; whole bays ~1.9 mu, halves ~0.9, thirds ~0.6), and dike-pond blocks run a ~160 ft module with a merge-heavy `parcel_mix` so most ponds are ~160x320 ft (~0.48 ha - traditional ponds were 0.4-0.6 ha oblongs; earliest attested sizes are 20th-century surveys of the traditional landscape, flagged in `build_polder`'s docstring) behind ~22 ft (~6.7 m, attested 6-10 m) mulberry dikes via the `gap` knob.

  **Perimeter dike: an irregular earthwork band following the natural water edge** (`polder_dike_is_earthwork`, `s.perimeter_dike`; GM 2026-07-22, researched + source-verified). The GM noticed the perimeter dike was drawn as a single uniform-width, perfectly straight, right-angled tan line and asked whether a hand-built earthwork would really look like that. It would not. *What the research found:* a wei-tian 圩田 / dike-pond dike was dredged pond-mud heaped and packed (the 挖塘培基 dig-and-pile cycle that also formed the ponds), trapezoidal in section, PLANTED with mulberry/willow/crops that bind the soil, walked and lived on, and constantly breached-and-repaired - so it read as a mottled, vegetated green-brown band of VARYING width, not a uniform stroke. Crucially, the *plan form splits*: the surveyed interior ditch/paddy grid was genuinely rectilinear, but the OUTER perimeter dike **followed the natural water edge** (lake / creek / marsh) in gentle curves and non-square bends - the "fish-scale polder" (鱼鳞圩) form named for exactly those irregular overlapping outlines. The dead-straight right-angled rectangle is a **post-1949 industrial** shape (heritage scholars: "the organic forms of polders were replaced by standardized rectangular patterns"), so it is the one genuinely anachronistic thing on the old render. *The decision:* `s.perimeter_dike(inner_env, ...)` takes the rectilinear grid boundary as the dike's INNER face and draws the OUTER face as an organic curve bulging outward by a varying amount (broad shoreline-following bulges + finer pinch-and-repair variation, ~14-40 ft wide - a perimeter dike ran wider than the ~6.7 m inter-pond mulberry dikes it rings, so it is drawn to TRUE width, not the old under-scale 4.4 px line), corners rounded not square, filled as a mottled earthwork with scattered soil-binding mulberry/willow crowns. The interior grid stays rectilinear (the surveyed part that IS historically correct). *Departure:* specific dike base/crest/height figures are not attested for pre-modern polders, so the ~14-40 ft band width is a plausible low-earthwork assumption, not canon; the width VARIATION and organic outer form are the well-attested parts. The dike is LABELED (the GM asked for it named - a polder dike is a real diegetic feature, not an "obvious" one exempt under the don't-label-the-obvious rule). Both polder demos (`kuwabata.gen.py` dike-pond, `enokida.gen.py` rice polder) call it; the check requires the recorded band's width to vary (`w_max >= 1.4x w_min`), so a reverted uniform-width or missing dike fires (negative fixture: `pool/regressions/polder_dike_is_earthwork_fires_on_a_ruled_uniform_dike.json`).

  **Perimeter dike planting: rows with a purpose, not a scatter** (GM 2026-07-24, researched - accuracy pass on the dike greenery). *Why dikes were planted at all:* a bare bank of heaped dredge-mud is a liability - rain gullies it, wave wash gnaws the waterside toe, and a slump becomes a breach - so planting the dike was the standard remedy wherever these earthworks existed: the roots bind the packed mud. The species split by role: WILLOW on the water face (thrives with wet feet; its root mat armors the bank against wave wash; pollarded for withies - willow-fascine bank protection is an ancient Chinese technique, in use by the last century BC), and in sericulture districts MULBERRY on the crest/inner face - the dike was elevated, well-drained, annually re-fertilized by the dredge cycle, i.e. prime planting ground in a landscape that is otherwise water (Lake Tai mulberry sat on the *tang* banks). A dike that looks bare and cleanly engineered is the modern-concrete-era tell. *What the numbers rest on:* dike planting was ROW planting along the alignment, not scatter. The closest attested in-row figure is the Qing Willow Palisade statute - willow whips planted every 5 chi (~1.67 m ~ 5.5 ft) in rows on an embankment - corroborated by modern willow-fascine practice descending from the same mechanics (rows 1-1.5 m apart on erosive soil, 1.5-2 m on cohesive). A polder-dike-specific statute was NOT found; the Willow Palisade figure is an ANALOG from a border embankment, recorded here as such, not as polder canon. *The decision:* the old uncalibrated random crown scatter is replaced by two planted rows that follow each band run (skipping the sluice notches): a willow row at ~3/4 of the band width toward the water face (larger pollard crowns, r 3.5-5.5 px, in-row 8.5 px - drawn at the loose end of the attested ~5.5 ft for the touching-crown read, the pond-bank legibility precedent) and a mulberry row on the inner face (coppice form and 4.4 px spacing identical to the pond banks). The earth mottle stays SCATTERED deliberately - patch-repairs, unlike planting, are haphazard. Both polders inherit this (a rice polder's dike was equally willow-armored, and Lake Tai attests mulberry on rice-polder banks). *Why the dike willows do NOT replace the village windbreak* (GM 2026-07-24, asked and answered - do not "simplify" one away): a windbreak's sheltered zone runs ~10-20x barrier HEIGHT, and the homestead belt is full-height dense planting for exactly that reason, while dike willows are POLLARDED low because the withies are the harvest - a single porous row at rooftop height shelters almost nothing at the houses' distance. Worse, willow and mulberry are DECIDUOUS: bare sticks during the NW winter monsoon, the one season shelter matters, which is why homestead windbreaks ran dense/multi-row/evergreen-heavy (the igune of the flat Sendai plain persisted amid abundant field-edge trees for the same reason). And an east-dike village sits downwind of the whole pond sheet - open water is the smoothest fetch there is, so the wind reaches the dike at full strength. Utility rows on the dike and a dense grove at the homestead are DIFFERENT plants doing DIFFERENT jobs; real polder landscapes carried both.

  **Polder ring canal: the trunk runs on the INNER TOE of the dike, not buried in it** (`polder_channels_clear_of_dike`; GM 2026-07-22, researched + source-verified). Once the dike became a wide earthwork band, the GM caught that the perimeter feeder - which `build_polder` ran at `s = +-12` px, OUTSIDE the field envelope - now sat buried in the dike, and asked where the channel really belonged and whether it too should be a little "watery". *What the research found:* the polder's trunk distribution+collection canal rings the block on the INSIDE toe of the perimeter dike, on the FIELD side (Jiangnan shorthand **一河围田, "one river surrounds the field"**; cross-section outside->in: wild water -> dike -> inner ring canal 圩内河 -> field ditches 浜 -> paddies). Outside the dike is the wild lake/creek the dike holds back, so NO irrigation channel runs out there; water crosses the dike ONLY through gated **sluices** (斗门/水閘/涵洞) cut at discrete points (the inlet + outfall), never as an open cut over the dike body. And the trunk line is *organized-but-organic*: long runs that read straight-ish but GENTLY WAVY (a surveyed dug canal wavers with terrain and repair; crescent 月样 / bow 弓样 trunk forms are attested named options), with rounded corners rather than hard 90-degree turns - the finer laterals are visibly crookeder. *The decision:* `build_polder` now reserves the ~14 px `RING` corridor inside the dike on ALL FOUR sides (was two) and runs the feeder / drain / two side toe-ditches as a connected ring canal in it, at `RING*0.5` just inside the envelope, gently wavy (`waver`); the header pond sits OUTSIDE the dike as the wild-water source, and only the pond inlet + the brook outfall cross the dike (the two sluices). The dike's inner face wobbles OUTWARD only, so it never intrudes over the ring canal. The check counts field-ditch vertices inside the recorded dike band and fires above 4 (the sluice-crossing allowance); negative fixture `pool/regressions/polder_channels_clear_of_dike_fires_on_a_canal_in_the_dike.json` intrudes the dike over the canal to trip it.

  **Polder ring canal, second pass** (GM 2026-07-22, researched): the GM then made eight more observations about the reworked Kuwabata, each answered here. (1) **Filleted corners** (`build_polder` `cr` fillets): a hard 90-degree ring-canal corner scours the outer bank and silts the inner - FAO sets an earthen-canal minimum bend radius of tens of times the width - so every ring corner is a quadratic-bezier FILLET, never a right angle (the finer laterals stay crookeder). (2) **Clean lateral/ring joins**: the laterals now START on the feeder inner-toe line and END on the drain inner-toe line, and the rounded corners removed the old feeder-meets-toe overlaps. (3) **The pond visibly charges the ring**: the dike is drawn FIRST (a ground layer) so the fields + ring canal + the two sluice crossings draw ON TOP of it; the feeder is recorded NW-end-last and extended with a short INLET STUB up through the dike to the pond rim, so the pond plainly feeds the ring at the north sluice. (4) **The south drainage exits**: the drain (bottom ring side, cross-slope) taps at mid-south into the brook, which runs off-map SOUTH through the dike (the outfall sluice) - water has somewhere to go. (5) **Structures + windbreak keep OFF the dike** (`structures_clear_of_dike`): `perimeter_dike` registers its band as a placement keep-out and `village_grove` skips clumps on it, so no farmhouse or windbreak clump sits on the earthwork bank (it carries only its own soil-binding trees; negative fixture `pool/regressions/structures_clear_of_dike_fires_on_a_house_on_the_dike.json`). (6) **The windbreak wraps the WINDWARD (NW) fringe, not just the north**: the cold winter monsoon blows from the NW, so the belt is an L covering the cluster's north end AND its west side. Because an east-dike village abutting the ponds has open water to its west, the gen reserves a windward no-build gap over the cluster's north third (the north houses shift east; the south houses still hug the field for `field_ringed`) and runs the west arm down that gap - the only way to fit a west windbreak against a pond-facing village. (7) **Footbridges cluster on the SETTLEMENT side** (research: crossings concentrate at the dike->field transition where people live, ~one per field-access lane; the unsettled sides are walked on the dike crest and crossed - if at all - at a sluice/culvert, not a plank; most real crossings were earthen culvert-causeways, a few plank spans): each ring side carries a `seg` tag and `channel_footbridges(seg_caps=...)` caps planks per side (east toe several, laterals sparse, feeder/far-toe/drain none) - Kuwabata dropped from 41 planks to 8. `long_ditches_have_a_footbridge` exempts the unsettled ring segs. (8) **The three green rectangles are correct**: the `mulberry_dike_fishpond` archetype converts ~90% of parcels to fish ponds (`fraction=0.9`), leaving a few (Kuwabata: ~4 of 43) as standing rice - the historically-attested mixed dike-pond district (mulberry sat on the tang banks with rice remaining the polder's crop permanently), NOT wall-to-wall ponds. (Fourth pass: those leftovers now draw as textured standing rice with no bund outline - see 'Polder fourth pass' below.)

  **Polder third pass: edge wander, sluice gaps, and inset rounded fish ponds** (GM 2026-07-22, researched). Looking at the reworked Kuwabata the GM flagged five more things, each an "it's too machine-perfect / the water does the impossible" note, and each is now both a placement fix and (where the manifest can carry teeth) an automated check. (1) **The dikes WANDER** (`polder_edges_wander`; `build_polder` `edge_wander` knob): a hand-dug wei-tian dike followed the old water edge, so it runs at a slight angle and gently changes direction with the ground (the fish-scale-polder read); a dead-straight axis-aligned block is the post-1949 consolidation shape. `edge_wander` drives a SEPARABLE low-frequency warp of the whole `(s, t)` grid - `cwarp(s)` shifts every contour-row in the cross direction (so all N-S dikes AND every interior column line share it and stay parallel while the block bends), `fwarp(t)` shifts every column in the fall direction (E-W dikes + row lines). Because every point - envelope, parcels, ring canal, laterals, and the dike that follows the envelope - is placed through `grid()`, the whole polder warps as ONE coherent piece and each field edge stays parallel to its dike section (exactly the GM's "the edges would be parallel to each section of dike"). A linear term is the overall tilt, the sines are the topology-following bends; phases come from a separate rng so every `edge_wander=0` map stays byte-identical. Both polders now pass `edge_wander=0.4`. The check requires >=30% of the field outline to run off-axis in the down-frame (a pure rectangle scores 0). (2) **Water crosses the dike through a DUG GAP, not over the top** (`polder_dike_gapped_at_sluices`; `perimeter_dike(gaps=...)`): the old inlet + outfall ran the channel OVER the unbroken earthwork band (it read as the pond water running uphill onto the dike and back down). `build_polder` now returns `dike_sluices` (the inlet + outfall crossing points) and `perimeter_dike` NOTCHES the band there - it splits the earthwork into the runs BETWEEN the gaps and draws each as its own capped strip, so the sluice channel passes through a dug notch. The check finds every THROUGH-CROSSER (a water line with a point inside the dike band AND a vertex outside the field outline - it genuinely runs field -> through dike -> off-map) and requires a recorded gap within ~26 px; incidental ring-canal clipping of the inner toe at a concave bend never leaves the field, so it is not a crosser and is not required to have a gap. (3) **The fish-pond water is INSET within its mulberry banks** (`dikepond_water_within_banks`): the old overlay filled the whole parcel with teal to its very edge, so the pond "ran off the green interior". A 桑基魚塘 unit is a raised mulberry dike (基, drawn green) surrounding an inset pond (塘, water), so `apply_land_use` now fills the parcel green and draws the water homothetically inset inside it (`Settlement._rounded_pond`), recorded as `M['dikeponds']` (parcel + water polygon per pond); the check requires every pond's water polygon to lie inside its parcel. (4) **The pond corners are ROUNDED** (`dikepond_corners_rounded`): a premodern dug earthen pond erodes to rounded corners - it had no way to hold a poured-concrete right angle - so `_rounded_pond` fillets every corner with a quadratic bezier of slightly irregular reach (erosion is uneven); the check requires the recorded water polygons to carry the rounding as many sampled vertices (>=10), where a sharp quad has 4. (5) **The laterals FEED the ring, they do not overshoot it** (a rendering fix, no manifest teeth): the old laterals left a little stub poking past the feeder into the dike corridor. This was a draw-order artifact (the ring's gentle waver plus widest-drawn-first left the lateral's top segment uncovered), not a geometry error - the endpoint sits on the ring line in both the before and after manifests, so there is nothing for a manifest check to separate. The fix is to draw the polder RING trunk (feeder / drain / toe collectors) LAST, ON TOP of the laterals, so every lateral-to-trunk junction is a clean T covered by the trunk (comb nets set no `seg`, so their widest-first order is unchanged and byte-identical); the laterals are also snapped exactly onto the feeder/drain centerlines. `field_ditches_terminate` still guards termination; the clean junction itself is verified visually. *Village hug:* the east-edge wander pulled the field away from the straight house line, so Kuwabata's cluster was moved ~30 px closer to the dike to keep >=5 houses ringing the field (`field_ringed`). Negative fixtures: the pre-fix manifests of both polders are frozen - `pool/regressions/dikepond_and_polder_wander_gaps_fire_on_prefix_kuwabata.json` (fires all four new checks) and `pool/regressions/polder_wander_and_sluice_gaps_fire_on_prefix_enokida.json` (the rice-polder variant, fires the two dike checks). (6) **The green floor IS the ring-canal interior** (`polder_floor_is_ring_interior`; GM 2026-07-22 follow-up): the field greenery (`comb_base_fill`) was drawn to the dike-boundary ENVELOPE, a separate rectangle that - once the ring canal wavers under `edge_wander` - drifts in and out of the outermost channels (sometimes green spills past the ring toward the dike, sometimes it falls short). `build_polder` now returns `floor` = the four ring sides concatenated into the closed inner-toe loop, and `comb_base_fill` fills THAT (the ring canal draws on top), so the greenery is bounded exactly by the outermost irrigated channels. The check requires every recorded field-floor vertex to lie within ~8 px of a ring channel centerline; the pre-fix envelope floor sat ~9-22 px out at the dike boundary and fires (negative fixture `pool/regressions/polder_floor_is_ring_interior_fires_on_an_envelope_floor.json`).

  **Polder mosaic vs grid: a tunable knob for two historically-real looks** (`build_polder` `mosaic`; GM 2026-07-22, researched). The GM asked whether real dike-ponds were the neat rectangular grid the maps drew, or something rougher. *What the research found (web-sourced, cited in the session):* the answer is BOTH, and it splits by system. The individual ponds genuinely WERE rectangular oblongs - hand-dug from marsh (挖塘培基: dig the pond, pile the spoil into the dike), the recurring descriptor a "chessboard" of "rectangular-shaped dikes... with water in between" - because you dig a pond in whatever packs the space and straight dikes are easiest to pile, walk, and plant mulberry on. So all-rectangular ponds are correct; this is the rare farm landscape that does NOT grow organically around the terrain, because the farmers MADE the terrain. BUT the *arrangement* differed by system. The lower-Yangtze **圩田 (wei-tian)** was a SURVEYED rectilinear grid - the Song-era 塘浦 *tangpu* lattice, deliberately engineered - so a clean grid is historically right for it. The Pearl-delta **桑基魚塘 (dike-pond)** instead accreted household-by-household into a MOSAIC; the landscape-ecology literature describes the historical delta not as a uniform chessboard but as "mosaic-like constructed ponds with meandering natural river systems, [with] the boundary between constructed and natural blurred" - rectangles, yes, but of varied sizes at varied local orientations fitted around winding interior creeks (the perfectly-uniform grid is closer to the MODERN consolidated look, which the same sources note eroded the ~20 m dikes to under 4 m). *The decision:* since both are accurate AND two same-type polders that look different multiply map variety, `mosaic` is a tunable knob (0 = the surveyed grid, the default). It displaces the INTERIOR bund-node lattice by a smooth CORRELATED field tapered to 0 at the pinned perimeter (so the envelope + dike stay put and parcels never leave the block): neighbouring nodes move together, so the lattice lines stay continuous but BEND - the interior laterals become meandering creeks and the parcels skew to trapezoids, while the individual ponds stay 4-sided (matching the research: the mosaic is in the ARRANGEMENT, not in ponds being triangular). Displacement draws from a separate rng, so every `mosaic=0` map stays byte-identical. Enokida stays the **grid** (its 圩田 identity); Kuwabata now runs **mosaic=0.5** (its 桑基魚塘 identity), and declares `meta(pond_layout="mosaic")`. *Testing (and why no gate check):* the knob is verified by an ENGINE unit test (`test_build_polder_mosaic_knob`: byte-stable at 0, deterministic, and the parcels measurably more trapezoidal at 0.5) plus the existing gate, which already passes on the mosaic map. A per-map manifest CHECK was deliberately NOT added: the mosaic signature lives in the RELATIVE bending of neighbouring lattice lines, but every aggregate manifest metric tried (lateral straight-line deviation, quadratic-fit residual, parcel-area cv) overlaps heavily with the smooth `edge_wander` bend, and the full parcel polygons are not recorded - so a manifest check would be theater, not teeth. Instead the variety is made to COUNT structurally: `pond_layout` is a 9th `twin_axes` axis (grid vs mosaic), so the twin-detector reads a grid polder and a mosaic polder of the same water direction as genuinely distinct places.

  **Polder fourth pass: the dike-pond reads as what it is - planted banks, textured rice, no floating outlines** (GM 2026-07-23, researched). Looking at Kuwabata the GM asked three questions, each answered here. (1) *What are the orange outlines?* The base polder draws every parcel flat rice-green with a tan bund stroke; the ~10% of parcels the wholesale conversion left as rice (item 8 of the second pass) kept that rendering, and with no surface texture and a fill near the floor green they read as floating tan outlines around nothing - and the one FLOODED leftover read as "a pond with no mulberry dike". *Decision:* under `eligible="all"` (the archetype's wholesale case ONLY - a partial overlay's unconverted plots are ordinary textured comb paddies already), `apply_land_use` repaints every leftover parcel as textured standing rice (`_paddy_surface` transplant mottle; a flooded leftover keeps its flood tint + sheen, and - GM follow-up, same day - its waterline draws ROUNDED and slightly irregular via `_rounded_pond` at a small inset with no edge stroke, because bund corners silt round and a hand-piled bund toe wanders; the missing stroke and missing mulberry bank are what keep it reading as a wet field, not dug infrastructure) and erases the bund outline with a same-color covering stroke - inside a dike-pond block the neighbors' raised banks are what bound a rice parcel, so its own drawn bund was noise. Enokida (the rice polder) is deliberately untouched: its tiled bund grid is the established look and the GM has not yet interrogated it. The repaint records `leftover_plots` centroids in the `land_use` manifest entry. (2) *Are the mulberry bands really that thin next to ponds that big?* Yes - the drawn geometry hits the attested ratio. The classic dike-pond prescription was an explicit area ratio of 6 parts water to 4 parts dike (some districts 7:3); measured from the Kuwabata manifest, water is 76% of each parcel (bank 24%) and 50% of the whole block once the shared 22 ft dikes and canal corridors count - bracketing 6:4. The band is not marginal ground: each pond's ~6,300 sq ft (~0.14 ac) bank was the SILK side of the loop (leaf -> silkworm -> frass -> fish -> dredged pond mud -> dike fertility), and the ratio existed because too much water starves the silkworms and too much dike starves the fish. (3) *Should the band be actual trees?* Silkworm mulberry was not grown as trees: it was COPPICED into low bushes (crowns ~4-6 ft) so the leaf could be stripped several times a year, planted in dense rows on the dike at roughly one bush per 10-20 sq ft - i.e. 300-600 bushes per pond, tens of thousands across the map. At 1 px = 1 ft a crown is a 2-4 px dot and adjacent crowns nearly touch, so drawing the actual trees at honest density IS a packed dot band; individually distinguishable tree glyphs would mean 3-5x crown inflation, forbidden on to-scale maps. No berries either: leaf-stripped coppice barely fruits, and a mulberry fruit is sub-pixel at this scale - crown color carries the read. *Decision:* the flat dark-green band is replaced by the perimeter dike's own treatment (`_mulberry_rows`) - a mottled earthen bank carrying two planted ROWS of true-scale crown dots (r 2.2-3.6 px at ~6 px in-row spacing, the loose end of the attested 3-5 ft, for pixel separation). *Quantified (GM 2026-07-23 follow-ups):* attested density is ~1 bush per 10-20 sq ft with 4-6 ft crowns at 3-5 ft in-row spacing - which means real adjacent crowns TOUCH, and a fully honest-density row is a fused continuous hedge line (exactly the solid band this pass replaced). The GM then asked for the touching-crown read without the fusion (`oo`, not `o o` and not concentric): in-row step went 6 px -> 4.4 px, so crowns touch in runs with bank tan showing through the notches, measuring ~1 per 23 sq ft (Kuwabata: 10,613 crowns over ~243k sq ft; the 6 px draft sat at ~1/31). Still shy of the attested low end because only 2 rows fit the band legibly - the remaining gap is the price of the crowns reading as separate plants at all - with crown sizes honest (4.4-7.2 ft drawn vs 4-6 ft real) - and the bank's corners ease with small erosion fillets while KEEPING the rectangular character, because straight rectangular dikes are attested (see 'Polder mosaic' above: the mosaic is in the arrangement, never in the pond shape). The bank sits at the TRUE parcel line; the base parcel's tan bund stroke is erased by a floor-color underlay (floor, base parcels, and cover all share `_RICE_GREEN`, so it vanishes into both, and the corner fillets expose that cover as floor). An earlier draft EXPANDED the bank +5 px to cover the stroke directly - `mulberry_banks_clear_of_channels` (next entry) caught it putting banks over the wavering laterals in 72 places, which is exactly the check doing its job. Rendering-level decisions (rows, mottle, crown dots) are deliberately NOT manifest-checked - `M['dikeponds']` still records parcel + water exactly as before, so `dikepond_water_within_banks` / `dikepond_corners_rounded` keep their teeth unchanged.

  **Mulberry bushes keep clear of the canals** (`mulberry_banks_clear_of_channels`; GM 2026-07-23). The bank planting is coppiced BUSHES standing on the dike, not canopy trees arching over water, so a crown drawn across the ring canal or a lateral would be a bush growing in open dug water - impossible. *Placement (refined GM 2026-07-24):* `_mulberry_rows` keeps the bush TRUNK off the canal - any crown whose CENTER lies within 3.5 px of a channel centerline is dropped - but the crown EDGE may overhang the water, and the crown groups draw AFTER the late-water anchor, so the channel strokes render UNDER the canopies: an overhanging leaf edge covers part of the channel, never the channel slicing across a crown (the canal runs between the bushes at ground level; the original clearance rule was crown-circle-clear at r + 3 px, which kept canopies artificially pulled back from the water). The earth mottle and all ground FILLS stay beneath the channels as before. *Teeth:* recording thousands of decorative crown dots would bloat the manifest, so instead each pond records its `bank` outline - the planted band's outer edge, which the crowns fill - and the check requires (a) every recorded pond to carry the `bank` record, so silently dropping it cannot disable the check, and (b) no densified field-ditch centerline to penetrate more than 2 px inside any bank. Edge-GRAZING passes deliberately: the canal genuinely runs along the dike toe, where earth meets water, and the mosaic-bent laterals graze parcel edges by up to ~1.5 px - that is the toe line clipping the bank rim, not a canal through the dike. *The check earned its keep on day one:* the first bank rendering expanded the band +5 px past the parcel (to cover the base bund stroke), and the check fired on the real Kuwabata with 72 penetrations up to 6.5 px deep - the fix moved the bank to the true parcel line with a floor-color underlay doing the stroke-covering (see the fourth pass above). That pre-fix manifest is frozen as a real-map negative fixture alongside the synthetic ones from `make_regressions.py`.

  **Dike-pond sluices: every pond is FED and DRAINED, downhill** (`dikeponds_fed_and_drained`; GM 2026-07-22 -> 07-23, researched). The GM first noticed the fish ponds did not connect to the irrigation canals at all, then - once they did - that a single connector was not enough: for water to move through a pond it has to enter high and leave low. *What the research found:* a 桑基魚塘 pond is NOT a sealed basin - each connects to the creek/canal network through a SLUICE GATE, "a protected opening in the pond dike that can be easily closed with wooden boards to regulate water level" and, by pulling the boards, drain the pond at harvest. And a pond on a slope is plumbed INLET-HIGH, OUTLET-LOW so water flows downhill through it (the whole dike-pond net runs in series from a high intake to a low outfall). So the channels do not "irrigate" the ponds paddy-style; they are the conveyance-and-drainage network the ponds exchange water with. *The decision:* `apply_land_use` gives every pond TWO gates - a FEEDER `<line>` culvert from its uphill corner to an UPHILL point on the creek network (water runs down IN) and a separate DRAIN from its downhill corner to a DOWNHILL point (water runs down OUT), each connecting to the nearest channel OR neighbour pond in the right fall direction (`<line>`, so the z-order audit ignores it). Recorded as `M['dikepond_sluices']` (`{a: pond-end, b: network-end, kind: feed|drain}`). The check works in the down-slope frame: every pond must have a feed AND a drain on its water, a feed's network-end must sit UPHILL of its pond-end and a drain's DOWNHILL, every sluice's far end must reach a channel or another pond, and a pond's feed + drain segments must not cross - so sealed, one-way, uphill-draining, or crossing ponds all fire (negative fixture `pool/regressions/dikeponds_fed_and_drained_fires_on_sealed_ponds.json`). Note the `apply_land_use` late-water re-anchor (above) means the trunk canals draw OVER the pond banks, so a sluice reads as the creek reaching in through the dike. (The channels themselves are still tagged with the rice-polder roles `feeder`/`lateral`/`drain` - inherited from the 圩田 engine Kuwabata is built on - but for an all-ponds district they are really the conveyance/creek network, not paddy irrigation.)

  **The polder water network is CONNECTED, and every parcel fronts a ditch** (`polder_parcels_front_water`; GM-flagged 2026-07-21: the original Kuwabata's feeder dipped into the block, touched one paddy and stopped, while the ponds and the drain floated with no connection). The jingbang 泾浜 polder interior was a two-tier creek-and-ditch net (jing 泾 creeks, bang 浜 field ditches) behind a sluiced perimeter dike, in which every basin fronted water - qualitatively well-attested; the exact lateral spacing is a REASONED RECONSTRUCTION (one lateral per module line). `build_polder` now draws the head feeder straight along the high dike, a `role="lateral"` ditch down every interior column line (following its jittered bund-node line, so laterals waver gently), and the collecting drain along the low edge to the outfall - one connected system the existing topology checks (`field_ditches_terminate`, `field_ditches_reach_source_and_sink`) validate, while the new frontage check requires every parcel centroid within ~0.62x its longer span of a supply/drain ditch. Straight lines and right angles are CORRECT for a surveyed polder - the defect was the disconnection, never the geometry. `draw_comb_field` records per-plot `[along, cross, cx, cy]` on the field's manifest entry so both parcel checks measure drawn geometry, not a builder self-report; the pre-fix Kuwabata manifest is frozen as the negative fixture for both (`pool/regressions/polder_parcels_vary_fires_on_kuwabatas_uniform_squares.json`).

  **Polder siting Q&A: the ring is complete, the outside is fluctuating water, the village sits on the landward margin** (GM 2026-07-24, researched - an UNDERSTANDING pass, no render or code changes; open items below are flagged for a future GM decision, not fixed). The GM asked three siting questions about Enokida, answered here so the reasoning is on record. (1) *Does the dike really surround the paddies completely?* Yes - full enclosure IS the defining feature, not a drawing convenience. A weitian is wetland "enclosed with dykes to be hydrologically separated from the surrounding fluctuating water and then drained" (the character 圩 means the enclosing embankment); Shen Kuo (Northern Song, Illustrated Records of Wanchun Polder) describes "dikes and dams... built along the rivers to enclose the farmland, which is called a polder." The enclosed floor sits at or below the surrounding FLOOD stage, so on a flat lake plain there is no safe side to leave open - any gap re-floods the whole block at the next high water, which is why water crosses only at the two gated sluices. The scale is attested too: fragmented small polders were each "cultivated by a group of 10-20 households" behind dikes ~1.5 m high - Enokida's 16 households are exactly this unit. (2) *Should there be marsh/wetland on all sides then?* The outside is "fluctuating water," but that means neither open lake on every side nor water year-round. Attested surroundings: the lake/creek network the polder was dug from; reed marsh and mudflat where reclamation had not yet reached; NEIGHBOR polders across a shared creek (the mature Taihu landscape was "islet-like" fish-scale polders packed into the water net); and - at the district margin - the natural shore, because reclamation advanced FROM the shore ("mudflats along rivers and lakes were transformed"). The water also FLUCTUATES seasonally: at low stage much of the outside is exposed mudflat and reed, at flood it is sheet water - the dike is built against the flood stage, not the average day. Both pool polders are drawn as the landward-margin case: wild header pond NW (the source), reed marsh at the low south outfall side, village on naturally dry ground east. **RESOLVED (GM 2026-07-24, same day):** the WEST flank's outside used to draw as the same dry scrub as the landward east, so nothing communicated that the west dike held anything back; both polders now carry a `waterside` reed fringe along the west and declare `meta.waterward`, gated by `polder_waterward_flanks_wet` - see 'Polder waterward fringe + dike-top housing' below. (3) *Should the farmhouses be INSIDE the dike?* Both siting patterns are attested, split by what dry ground exists. Where the polder abuts the natural shore, the village sits on the landward dry ground at the dike's shoulder - the current renders' configuration, and the natural one for a margin polder (nobody lives on a flood-fighting earthwork when real dry ground is a few steps east). In the DEEP-water landscape with no natural dry ground, settlement used the polder's own raised earth instead: linear villages ON the dikes (canal-dike settlement "taking advantage of the elevated typology" is attested from the 8th century on) or houses inside the polder along its interior streams (Fei Xiaotong's Kaixiangong / the Xichang polder layout). So Enokida and Kuwabata are correct AS margin polders - but an "islet" polder map, water-ringed on all sides, would REQUIRE dike-top or interior housing, and `structures_clear_of_dike` (which keeps all structures off the dike band) would need a carve-out for that settlement form. **RESOLVED (GM 2026-07-24, same day):** dike-top housing is now a real engine capability (`s.dike_top_houses`, `settlement_form="dike_top"`, the carve-out + its honesty check) implemented as a KNOB for future variety - the GM explicitly chose NOT to convert any existing settlement; no pool map uses it yet. See 'Polder waterward fringe + dike-top housing' below. One more confirmation from the same research: the polder community IS its dike-maintenance community ("sustaining a polder necessitated a close-knit community," often one extended family, which named its polder) - so a polder village always sits hard against its own block, which is what `field_ringed` and the cluster-hug behavior already enforce.

  **Polder waterward fringe + dike-top housing** (GM 2026-07-24, implementing the two resolved items of the siting Q&A above). (1) *The waterward flanks read WET.* New marsh role `waterside` (`s.marsh(role="waterside")`): the un-reclaimed fluctuating wild outside a polder's dike - reed marsh / mudflat at low stage, sheet water at flood - drawn as the standard wet-palette reed scatter hugging the band's outer face (the dike + field keep-outs shape it automatically; the thin bare strip at the outer toe reads as the drawdown mudflat line, which is honest). It is EXEMPT from `marsh_on_low_ground`, because that check encodes the valley-toe logic (wet ground = downhill of the paddy) while a polder floor sits BELOW the outside water level, so its wet fringe surrounds the dike regardless of the fall direction.
