- **A magistrate's manor sits at the EDGE of its settlement, and its gate faces what it fronts** (`manor_gate_faces_town`, hamlet + town): the town/hamlet it administers (the dwelling centroid) OR the Imperial road it sits beside. **There is no fixed default direction** - it depends on where the town is - so pass `s.manor(..., gate_dir=...)` intentionally; **`s.manor`'s fallback is `"south"`** (the auspicious/formal orientation), NOT a blind `"west"`. Moritono faces **west** (the hamlet is west of the forest-edge lodge); Hirameki faces **south** (down its hill to the town); **Hoshizora is TILTED** - `s.manor(..., gate_dir="north", rot=-30)` so its front wall runs **parallel to the diagonal Imperial Road** it fronts, gate opening onto the road. `s.manor(..., rot=<deg>)` physically tilts the whole compound (and its overlap footprint rotates with it). One caveat: a tilt changes the manor's footprint/block, which reshuffles a dense settlement's **seeded packs** and can knock the population off its mark - the fix is to **pick a seed that lands it back in band** (each of the dense towns/city carries a hand-picked seed for exactly this), which is cleaner than whack-a-mole on individual pack counts.
- **Pastures and large terrain** - hayfields/grazing (`s.pasture(...)`), forests (`s.forest_patch(...)`): a large area feature near an edge must **cross** that edge rather than sitting wholly on the map (`edge_features_run_off_map`). Barns sit within the grazing.
- **Streams stay between fields, never through them** (`streams_avoid_fields`): run a stream parallel to the road between field pairs. **Every fully-on-map field must SHOW a water source** (`fields_show_water_source`) - a channel ending inside it, or the field directly abutting a stream/pond. Being merely *near* water with no visible connection does not count, so tap the stream with a channel (`s.channel(stream_pt, field_pt, {"kind":"stream"}, {"kind":"field","name":...})`). Fields that run off the map edge are exempt (their water may be off-map too).
- **Nothing overlaps the manor, road, stream, or irrigation channel** (`no_structure_on_manor` / `_road` / `_stream` / `_channel`): the manor blocks a rect expanded by 36; roads, streams, and channels are corridors tested by the full rotated-rect footprint. Fields stay clear of the road (`fields_clear_of_road`). The "structures" every overlap check tests are houses + urban buildings **+ the standalone civic buildings** (the flophouse and granary *kura*) - those are real buildings and must not sit on a road / stream / wall / street / channel either. The one exclusion is the **merchant storehouses**, which are drawn as annexes *deliberately* abutting their shop, so they are not in the overlap set (they would trip the structure-overlap test by design).

**Walled towns** (`meta(walled=True)`) add a rampart:

- `s.wall(pts, gate=(gx,gy))` draws an irregular thick polyline (a wide no-build corridor - clearance ~46, so even a large building's corner stays off the rampart) with a gate gap, flanking posts, a guard station, and a guardtower. The gate records to the manifest. The wall must be **irregular** - `wall_sections_irregular` requires **>= 5 sections and a section-length coefficient of variation >= 0.25** (a spread test, so a wall may hug a feature with several short segments while a lazy near-regular polygon still fails); `walled_town_has_wall` requires both a wall and a gate. No structure may overlap the rampart stroke (`no_structure_on_wall`).
- A wall need not enclose a full ring. It can be an **open arc anchored to a steep hill**: the hill's back/sides defend that flank, so the rampart ties into the slope. Draw the hill with `s.hill(..., steep=True)` (emphasized hachures on the steep north back/upper flanks), and **run the wall's two ends partway UP the hill flanks** so the slope, not a blunt wall-end, closes each side. The magistrate's manor sits on the summit.
- A **chrysanthemum field** (`s.flower_field(...)`, the Imperial flower - "Heaven with the defenders") is kept INSIDE the walls, abutting the rampart. A field may **abut** the wall but must never cross it (`fields_clear_of_wall`). To make it read as genuinely flush (not a thin tan sliver): flatten the abutting edge with `flower_field(..., flat_west=True)` and run a **straight wall segment** right along it - center the wall ~5px outside the field's flat edge so the rampart's inner stroke (half-width ~5) lands flush on the field boundary. A wavy field edge against a straight wall always leaves a visible gap; flatten one, straighten the other, and they touch.
- **The whole urban core lives INSIDE the wall** (historical: a Chinese walled county seat / Japanese *jokamachi* enclosed its townspeople; the *graph* for "city," 城, means "wall"). Inside, zoned around the magistrate's hilltop citadel: samurai by the manor, then the merchant/shop streets, then the **laborers and servants in back-lane blocks** off the commercial avenue, plus the monastery - and open ground the surrounding farmers retreat into during a raid. **Outside the wall, only:** the farmland and farmhouses, the **segregated burakumin quarter** (outcasts on marginal land - historically correct), and a *small* **gate market** (*guan-xiang*) of a few shophouses along the road just outside the gate. The gate market is a **default, not an option**: a walled town is gated to have a few businesses (shops/merchants) outside the wall near the gate (`walled_town_has_gate_market`, >= 3 within ~420px). **The why is TRAFFIC, not taxes (GM 2026-07-24, correcting the rationale ported from the city tier):** towns levy NO import tariffs - budgets.md puts the entire tariff apparatus (the Yasuki Taka gate collection, the tariff-audit yoriki) at provincial-city and capital gates only, ~2,700 manageable collection points instead of an impossible ~14,400 town gates - and the county magistrate's jurisdiction is the whole COUNTY, so standing outside the gate crosses no tax or regulatory line at all. The honest drivers are the ones the city-tier research (flophouse-research.md) validated: through-road travelers (carters, peddlers) buying services without detouring inside, the market-day chokepoint where the rural catchment trades, and late arrivals who find the gate shut at dusk. A town's gate market therefore scales with its **gate traffic, not its population**: **typically ~4-8 permanent premises** (the check floor stays >= 3) - the documented "smaller guanxiang" end of the researched 10-40-per-trafficked-city-gate band - and it is a **SLICE like the farmland**. At CITY scale that slice shows as run-off-frame truncation: string the stalls along the approach road and let the outermost run off the frame, the cut itself saying "more beyond the map" (the convention the cities adopted 2026-07-24 - a city canvas extends past its cropped view, so a stall can straddle the frame). A TOWN canvas IS the view and `_fits` keeps buildings ~26px clear of the frame edge, so a town's market sits whole inside the frame and the approach road running off the edge carries the continuation signal by itself (Hirameki: 4 premises at FIXED coordinates placed before the street frontage scans - an exact-count documented feature is never left to a grid scan, whose spots re-roll with every upstream RNG shift - with the s1 paddy comb honestly pinching the rest). Premises beyond the ~24 merchant DWELLINGS are `shop` glyphs - business premises, not household-gated, housing no one - so growing the gate market never perturbs the population math (the merchant dwellings that do stand at the gate count inside the 24 like any others; the town tier counts all dwellings regardless of the wall). Suppress it only for a real exception with `meta(gate_market=False)` (a purely military fort, a depopulated or suppressed gate). Do NOT push the laborers/servants outside to save room - that inverts the real pattern.
- **Notice board (kosatsuba) - the state's standing law at the settlement's busiest point** (`town_has_kosatsuba` default-on for every town, walled or not; `kosatsuba_by_the_road` sites it within ~60 ft of a road/main street; `s.kosatsuba(x, y, rot)`; opt out with `meta(kosatsuba=False)` for a suppressed or backwater seat). Every Edo town AND village kept the official edict board - standing shogunal/domain law, porter and packhorse rate tables, currency regulations, ban edicts - and its siting was a TRAFFIC decision, not an administrative one: busy street corners, checkpoints, bridgeheads, the gate or center of the settlement, "in a prominent position alongside the main highway". Edo's principal board stood at Nihonbashi (the bridgehead where the five highways began), post towns' mid-shuku by the transport office - not at the government office. **The TWO boards are distinct institutions and coexist** (multiple boards per settlement were normal): the settlement kosatsuba posts the state's standing law where everyone passes, deliberately imposing (like the execution ground, it was designed to represent the strength of authority); the magistrate's manor-gate board (part of the Mode A compound program - buildings.md "Notice board") posts the bench's OUTPUT - verdicts, edicts of the court, bounties - for the people who come TO the court (litigants, petitioners, bounty hunters). Because the manor deliberately sits at the settlement EDGE (`manor_gate_faces_town`), defaulting the town board to the manor's gate would put it exactly where the fewest feet pass - the inversion the siting check exists to prevent. Placement: an unwalled road-town puts it on the highway frontage at a busy node of the core (Hoshizora: the SW arrival stretch by the theater/flophouse - the packed merchant frontage upstream has no verge, which is honest); a walled town on the main street just inside the front gate (Hirameki). Drawn at TRUE size (~12x5 ft roofed frame over the 7x3 ft board, the Mode A size); the label carries the read. **Cities port the institution UP, not away** (`city_has_kosatsuba` + `city_kosatsuba_per_gate`, same siting check with the limit in REAL feet - 60 ft is 20 px at the 3 ft/px city grain; GM 2026-07-24): a real city posted MANY boards - Edo kept the principal high-board at Nihonbashi plus subsidiary boards at its gates and bridge approaches - so a city **draws the SET and labels ONE** (GM decision 2026-07-24, superseding the initial one-board-stands-for-the-set depiction): a board on every main gate's approach corridor (`city_kosatsuba_per_gate`, within ~800 real ft of each gate - the corridor, not the furnished throat), with only one representative board labeled, the same one-label convention as the fire towers and gate markets. An UNLABELED board also fits the tight gate verges a labeled one cannot - Tango's busier south gate could not hold the label box but takes the bare board fine. Current placements: Tango labeled below the north gate's guard/inspection throat + unlabeled inside the south gate; Nagahara labeled at the east-avenue crossroads (clear of the caravan stable's animal-yard disc) + unlabeled inside the north gate - a single drawn board standing in for the set exactly like the drum tower and the per-quarter fire watch. At city grain the true ~12x5 ft frame draws ~4x2 px and the label carries the read; if that proves too small to see, the documented escape is well-style LOCATION-MARKER status - a GM call, never a silent inflation. Villages and hamlets historically had boards too - whether the village tier depicts them is a future decision, recorded here so the scope choice is deliberate.
- **Fire defense - a WALLED town gets a fire-watch tower (an OPEN town gets none).** The packed wooden core of a *walled* town is where fire is catastrophic, and the rampart that keeps raiders out also traps a blaze in, so a walled town draws one (an open town - a road-town strung along the highway, or an unwalled county seat like Hoshizora at detached village grain - has field-gaps for natural breaks and gets none; a 2026-07 audit briefly widened the requirement to every town, reverted 2026-07-24 after research - see the "Fire towers" grounding). Place a **fire-watch tower** with `s.fire_tower(x, y)` - a *hinomi-yagura*, an open braced-timber tower with an alarm bell, the magistrate's watch - among the **laborer/merchant blocks** (`walled_town_has_fire_tower`; `fire_tower_in_commoner_quarter` keeps it in the dense commoner warren, not the samurai quarter, and it is an overlap-checked struct so it must stand clear of the wall - distinct from the guard towers ON the rampart). Place it **LAST, after the packs and `farmsteads()`**, on a cleared seam the finished map actually has, so it perturbs no placement. Suppress with `meta(fire_tower=False)`. See the "Fire towers" historical grounding below.
- **Town scale ≠ village scale.** A town is ~1,200 people vs a village's ~350, so it needs a genuinely larger drawing: a bigger canvas (Hirameki is `Settlement(2600, 1820, ...)`) AND a finer building grain - set `s.bscale ≈ 0.82` so the urban glyphs pack denser (town buildings are smaller dots than village houses; the `bscale` factor only applies where set, so an unwalled town like Hoshizora can keep `1.0`). Sizing the wall like a village's is what forces the population outside - give the rampart room for the whole core.
- **Streets carve the interior into blocks.** Draw `s.street(pts, width=26, main=True, label="main street")` for the **gate-to-yamen axis** (extend it *through* the gate so the gate market frontage outside is on the same avenue) and `s.street(pts, width=20)` for one or two market cross-streets - *before* the frontage/packs. `walled_town_has_main_street` requires a `main=True` street running inward from the gate; `no_structure_on_street` keeps buildings off the bed. Then line the streets with `s.frontage(...)` (businesses, two-deep, facing the street; `face_streets=True` packs skip deep spots so commerce only lines frontage) and fill the laborer/servant **back-lane blocks** with `s.pack(..., face_streets="fill")` - the `"fill"` mode faces buildings near a street but still fills the deep block cores (tenement housing, which is `>92px` from any street and therefore exempt from the facing check). Give the laborer quarters their own back-lanes off the avenue so their dwellings front a *non-main* street (`housing_off_main_street` only bars them from the main commercial frontage). Because `frontage()` sits *against* the street it fronts (it skips that street's corridor), several streets no longer starve each other the way plain `pack()`-into-blocks did - a main axis plus a couple of cross-streets and back-lanes is fine.
- **No "street to nowhere": every street earns its existence by the buildings along it** (`streets_have_buildings` - no inside-the-walls stretch longer than ~130px may be empty of buildings that **front this street**). The rigor that matters: a building counts toward a street only if that street is the one it actually **fronts** (its nearest street, the one it was rotated to face) - a building sitting beside a north-south lane but fronting the east-west cross-street it is nearer to does NOT keep the lane alive. (An earlier, looser version counted any building within proximity and so missed lanes that dead-ended past their last real frontage.) **A building walled off from a street cannot front it either:** if a ward fence (`s.ward`) or the city wall lies between a building and the point it would front, that building serves its own side, not this street. (This was the Tango government-avenue bug - the gap-band laborers NORTH of the samurai ward fence appeared to "serve" the avenue SOUTH of the fence, papering over a 150px bare approach between the ward gate and the first ministry; the avenue had literally zero houses on either side. The fix lined the avenue's west end by fronting the Temple of Bishamon onto it. The threshold was a red herring - the check was counting frontage across a fence; excluding it surfaced the real 150px gap.) The *why* is historical: a street is **access infrastructure for the buildings it serves**, and it is paved or worn into the ground by the foot traffic to and from them - Beijing's *hutong* alleys "emerged as access routes lined by contiguous courtyard residences," and a desire path forms only between real destinations. A planned grid line that never gets built up simply **isn't drawn** (an undeveloped block). Note the asymmetry: **buildings with no street are fine** (the poor can't afford street frontage - they sit in the deep block cores), but **a street with no buildings is not**. When the check fails, fix it by **building demand**: (1) if there are buildings the lane could serve - dwellings sitting off in the cores, or documented households still owed - **route the lane to them or move them onto it** (lower-status dwellings readily line lesser back-lanes); (2) if the population is already fully housed (all the `town_caste_count` bands are met), the street has no reason to exist - **trim it back to its last building, or remove it** (this is what Hirameki's redundant lower cross-lane got: deleted, with no loss of laborer capacity since `face_streets="fill"` had already seated them in the cores). Don't add a street first and hope buildings find it; add streets where the buildings (or the demand for them) already are.

- **The wall must HUG the built town - don't wall in empty space** (`wall_hugs_the_town` - no contiguous stretch of rampart longer than ~280px may run more than ~140px from the nearest building, feature, or terrain). The *why* is pure economics: a rampart is the single most expensive thing a town builds (rammed earth or stone, maintained for centuries), and its cost scales with its **length**, so a town walls in exactly what it must defend and no more - the line is drawn to skirt the built-up area, not to inscribe a tidy circle around a lot of empty ground. Historically this is why town walls are *irregular*: they kink in to exclude a gully and bulge out around a quarter, following the settlement's actual footprint (and the terrain). Two kinds of slack are legitimate and the check allows for them: (1) **terrain** - a wall climbs or skirts a hill rather than leveling it, so the hill counts as filled "occupancy" (Hirameki's north rampart rides up the citadel hill and is exempt there); (2) a **modest gate forecourt** - the open *masugata* assembly/defensive square just inside the gate is real, so a short open dip at the gate is fine. What is NOT fine is a long empty margin along a whole face (Hirameki's first town-scale draft enclosed empty ground at three of its four quadrant edges - the east rampart ran ~260px from anything). When the check fails, the fix is almost always to **pull that face of the wall inward** to ride just outside the last buildings (this is what Hirameki's S/SE/E faces got - and the cross-street and east quarter were drawn in to match, since a tighter wall means a smaller interior); only rarely do you instead **fill the margin** with displaced buildings. Note this composes with `streets_have_buildings`: streets earn their length from buildings, and the wall earns *its* length from the whole built area - both reject infrastructure drawn around emptiness.

### Provincial cities (`meta(scale="city")`)

A provincial city is the next tier up from a county town - a provincial governor's seat, ~3,000 inside the walls. Like towns, some are walled and some unwalled; the worked example **Tango** (`pool/provincial-cities/tango.gen.py`) is walled. The drawing vocabulary adds a few city-only methods; the gate adds a city block of checks. (Since the budget-first wall sizing of feature 009, dwelling counts are a near-census: the budget targets the full ~600 households and the gate holds the map to its floor - see Scale and density above.)

- **The wall is a CLOSED ring with multiple gates.** Draw it with `s.city_wall(pts, gates=[...])` - a full loop (not the town's open hill-anchored arc), with a gap at each gate where the wall runs ~horizontal. Records `M["wall"]` (the ring), `M["gates"]` (all), and `M["gate"]` (the first, for checks shared with towns). The town-walled checks (`wall_sections_irregular`, `streets_have_buildings`, `wall_hugs_the_town`, the gate market, the monastery torii avenue) are **town-only** and do NOT apply to a city - a city's wall is a regular defensive ring with deliberate open ground inside (drill grounds, refuge space), not a cost-minimized skirt. `walled_city_has_wall_and_gates` requires a closed wall + **>= 2 gates**.
- **PLANNED / NOT YET BUILT - a tunable SALLY / POSTERN gate knob** (GM idea 2026-07-22; captured here per the "deferred note" convention). A secondary defensive gate distinct from the main road/river gates, present or absent as a **defensive-posture** choice (a city expecting war "shores up its defenses" by constructing/reconstituting one; a long-peaceful city may have none or a bricked-up one). **Historical framing to resolve first (needs its own research pass):** a dedicated European-style "sally port" riddling the curtain wall is NOT the China-first form - the Chinese walled seat concentrated defense in a *few grand gates*, each with a **barbican (瓮城 *wengcheng*)** that WAS the sortie-point, plus the wall and moat; it did not pepper the curtain with small posterns. The apt China-first / Japan-second equivalents are a **secondary / rear gate** (Japanese 搦手門 *karamete-mon*, the lesser gate opposite the main 大手 approach), a small **postern** (埋門 *umon*), or a **water gate** (水門 - which Nagahara's river gate already is). So the grounded knob is likely a *rear/postern gate*, not multiple sally ports - confirm the form + count with research before building. **Design sketch:** `meta(postern_gates=N)` or explicit positions, or a `meta(war_footing=...)`-style posture flag that adds one; it draws a SMALL, plain gate in a wall stretch clear of the main gates and mural towers, opening onto **empty field** (no road through it, so no *guan-xiang*). **It is traffic-free, so it is EXEMPT from the gate-market, flophouse, and caravan-cluster rules** - store its gates SEPARATELY from `M["gates"]` (which holds only main road/river gates) so `city_has_gate_market` / `city_flophouse_outside_each_gate` / `city_gate_caravan_facilities` skip them automatically (this is exactly why those checks were scoped to "every MAIN-ROAD gate," 2026-07-22). Furniture is minimal (a plain gate, maybe a small guard post; NO inspection station - nothing to inspect). Its own checks would gate: on the wall, clear of main gates/towers, opening onto field not a road, and the posture-knob's presence logic. When built, add a `specs/NNN-*/` feature via spec-kit (feature work, per CLAUDE.md).
- **A MOAT rings the wall, fed from off-map.** `s.moat(wall_ring, gap=...)` draws the wall ring pushed outward - water all the way around. `city_moat_surrounds_wall` requires every wall point inside the moat ring; `city_moat_fed_offmap` requires a **stream from a map edge** reaching the moat (the off-map source). **That feeder must be as WIDE as the moat** (`city_moat_feeder_matches_width`): a trickle cannot keep a full moat supplied, so a stream reaching the moat must match its width within ~25% - pass `s.stream(..., width=<moat width>)` (the moat's `width`, default 26, is recorded in `M["moat_width"]`; `s.stream` records each stream's `w`). Cities with moats **often** irrigate their outside farmland by tapping the moat (optional, not gated). A stream may legitimately terminate at the moat (the `stream_runs_off_edge` check now allows a moat terminus, as it already allowed a pond). (Waterways - streams, the moat, the pond feeder - render as solid water with a lighter mid-current sheen, **no dashed centerline**: a dash denotes a road's lane, which makes no sense on water.)
- **The Imperial road runs straight N-S through the city, gate to gate** (`city_imperial_road_through` - the road must run off both the top and bottom edges). It quarters the interior together with the implied E-W axis. The **`"Imperial Road"` label must sit OUTSIDE a gate** (`city_road_label_outside_walls`): inside the walls the same roadway is a *city street* the city maintains, not an Imperial responsibility, so pass `s.road(..., label_xy=(x, y))` a point beyond a gate (the default label anchor is the polyline midpoint, which for a city is the center - inside the walls).
- **A city ON the Imperial road LINES that road with commerce** (`city_imperial_road_has_commerce`). The through-road is the city's prime frontage: caravans and travelers pass along it, so it carries a **commercial ribbon** of shops + traveler services (inns), not bare housing-backs or empty ground. This is a **general rule for ANY city with an Imperial road, walled OR not** (a city *without* a road skips it, its commerce staying in the market district). The check measures the road's portion running *through* the city - bounded by the **wall** if there is one, else by the **urban footprint** (the bounding box of the city's buildings) - and wants commercial buildings (`shop`/`merchant`/`inn`) fronting it at roughly **>= 1 per 130px** of that length - a floor that catches a bare spine. Build it as a true **two-sided market street**: `s.frontage(<road sub-segment>, ["shop", ...], skip=<the road poly>, both=False, rows=2)` for the west side and a second call (a north-running sub-segment) for the east, plus a `s.pack(...)` to deepen a road-market block and a `s.inn(...)` or two for travelers. Capture the road polyline in a variable so you can pass it as `skip=` (a frontage row sits *against* the corridor it fronts). The dead frontage to watch for is the stretch between two quarters that both turn their backs to the road (Tango's was the band between the burakumin quarter and the merchant avenue) - fill it. Place the ribbon LAST in the gen (after every quarter's pack) so it flows into the gaps and perturbs no RNG-seeded placement. **General guidance on commercial intensity:** a provincial city's merchant/artisan caste is ~25% of households (~150 of 600, the highest commercial share of any tier), so a healthy commercial face is roughly **1 storefront per ~25-30 residents** (Tango ~3,000 -> ~105 `shop`+`merchant`+`inn` frontages); a road-city sits at the denser end of that band, with the increment concentrated as the road ribbon. (Domain capitals, all of which have an Imperial road, always carry this ribbon.)
- **Each gate has a GUARD HOUSE + attached INSPECTION STATION + GUARD TOWER**, drawn automatically by `s.city_wall(...)` (top layer, so the road passes under). Caravans entering submit cargo to inspection and pay the Ministry of Revenue's import tariff (the "Yasuki Taka system"), audited by the Imperial yoriki sub-station. Gated by `city_inspection_station_at_each_gate` (an inspection station within ~160px of each gate) and `city_gate_has_guardhouse` (>= 2 gate structures - the guard house + tower - within ~180px). Like the towers, the guard house + inspection station sit **SQUARE TO THE WALL / ring road** they line - rotated to follow it, not axis-aligned (`city_gate_furniture_aligned`). Each piece is WALKED along the curving wall from the gate (`_wall_walk`) so it picks up the wall's **LOCAL** tangent *where it actually sits* - NOT the gate vertex's tangent, which has already curved away by then (Tango's gates are on ~8 deg wall stretches, not the flat top/bottom, so getting this wrong leaves the road slicing diagonally across a flat box) - then pulled in radially to the **ring road centerline** (inset matching `s.ring_road`), so the patrol road runs lengthwise *through* each building. `s.city_wall(...)` records each piece's `rot` and `kind` (`"guardhouse"` / `"inspection"` / `"tower"`) in `M["gate_structs"]`; the check compares the furniture's `rot` to the nearest wall edge's angle **mod 180** (these are rectangles whose long axis runs along the wall, so a 180 deg flip is the same but a 90 deg turn stands them across the road the wrong way), within **6 deg** - tighter than the towers' 15 deg, because the furniture is set from the exact local edge angle (not the towers' chord-through-neighbors approximation), so it matches near-exactly and a 15 deg window would wave through the shallow ~8 deg gate slope. The angle is folded to (-90, 90] so the two gates render alike whichever way the wall runs through them.
- **The wall is TOWERED for INTERLOCKING flanking fire - density set by the city's DEFENSE TIER** (`city_wall_towers_spaced` for the coarse "not just at the gates" floor, `city_wall_tower_coverage` for the real curtain-coverage invariant). A fortified city spaced its mural (horse-face / 马面) towers so their fields of fire OVERLAP - an attacker at the wall base is under arrow fire from **2 towers at once** (the 侧射 "flanking shot" principle; Shen Kuo's 11th-c. 矢石相及, "arrows and stones reach each other," describes adjacent bastions covering the curtain between them). Towers are a function of the **wall's defensive geometry, not the interior street grid**, and they also housed the stairs up to the parapet. The **required density is TUNABLE per city** via `meta(wall_defense=...)`, because a city's history sets how hard it was fortified (see "Historical grounding: wall-tower coverage" below):
  - **`"siege"`** - a border city that has had to **repel sieges**: `>= 2` towers cover every curtain point within **aimed-lethal bowshot (60 m / 197 ft)**, so towers sit a bowshot apart (~66px at 3 ft/px). The Pingyao standard. **Tango and Nagahara both use this** (border location + siege history).
  - **`"garrison"`** (the DEFAULT) - a garrisoned interior city: `>= 2` towers within **full war-bow reach (100 m / 328 ft)**, a looser ring.
  - **`"peaceful"`** - a city long at peace: only `>= 1` flanking tower within aimed-lethal range everywhere (curtain midpoints still get 2). The sparser Xi'an spacing (~120 m / 394 ft between towers).
  - `settlement.wall_tower_spacing_px(px_per_ft, tier)` returns the max spacing; `WALL_DEFENSE` holds the `(range_ft, min_coverage)` table. `s.city_wall(...)` reads the tier and **densifies automatically**: it anchors on the gate towers, fills each arc so no sub-gap exceeds the tier spacing, then runs a coverage-remediation sweep that drops an extra mural into any run still short of the tier's min-coverage (a slide off a kido can leave a neighbor gap just over range). All recorded in `M["wall_towers"]`.
  - `city_wall_tower_coverage` samples every curtain point (~every 18px) and requires the tier's min-count of towers within the tier's arrow range **+12px** (a mamian's half-footprint - an archer shoots from the tower's parapet span, not its center point). The gate **barbican** is exempt (gate + guard house + inspection form a defended complex, not open curtain): points within 130px of a gate or 55px of its guard furniture are skipped, as are points within 45px of a **water gate** (a fortified shuimen opening flanked by its own two towers). These check keep-outs deliberately MIRROR the placement keep-outs - a point the placement code structurally will not tower (inside a barbican, on a water-gate opening) must not be demanded by the check, or the map can never pass. The older `city_wall_towers_spaced` (>= 6 towers, no bare arc wider than ~75 deg) remains as a coarse floor beneath the coverage invariant. Two additions from the doubled-tower incident (GM 2026-07-23, Tango's east curtain ran ...54, 76, 32, 54...): **(1)** points within `KIDO_TOWER_KEEPCLEAR` (62px) of a recorded ward-fence junction (`M['wall_tower_keepclears']`, the gens' `tower_skip` spots) are exempt too - the kido ward-gate is a manned chokepoint placement refuses to tower, and demanding 2-coverage of its band is exactly what forced the remediation pass to seat a SECOND tower 32px from a 55px-rhythm neighbor; **(2)** `wall_towers_evenly_spaced` gates the rhythm itself - mamian stand at regular flanking intervals, so no open-curtain mural gap may fall under **0.7x the map's median gap** (gate/water-gate flanking pairs exempt; calibration: the three defective pairs sat at 0.58-0.60x, every legitimate pool gap at >= 0.87x). Placement enforces the same rhythm from its side: mural min-separation floors at 0.75x the tier's spacing cap (was a flat 28px), strictly tighter than the check since the median never exceeds the cap - a rejected remediation seat slides to the local span midpoint instead of doubling up.
  - The towers also sit **SQUARE TO THE WALL** (`city_wall_towers_aligned`): each is rotated to the wall's tangent there - a tower on a 30 deg stretch slants 30 deg, not an axis-aligned box - recorded as `rot` in `M["wall_towers"]`. The check compares each tower's `rot` to the nearest wall edge's angle, mod 90 (a square reads the same every quarter-turn), within ~15 deg.
- **A RING ROAD hugs the inside of the wall** (`city_has_ring_road`) - the Chinese "follow-the-wall street" (順城街), the wall-clear patrol zone a fortified city keeps for moving troops along the rampart. Call **`RING = s.ring_road(WALL, inset=34)`** right after `s.city_wall(...)`, then **`s.bound = RING`** so the quarters pack INSIDE the ring (off the wall), leaving the clear zone. It is deliberately NOT a `town_street`: a fortification road is exempt from the must-be-built-up rule (its wall side is bare, and stretches run behind fields/compounds). Pulling the bound in off the wall costs ~one perimeter row of buildings (~8% area), so re-check the population/caste bands after adding it - usually a small density bump on one or two packs. **Streets AND ALLEYS MEET the through-lanes cleanly at a T-junction** (`city_streets_meet_through_lanes`): a street OR a gravel alley running toward the **Imperial road OR the ring road** must reach the lane's bed and END there - neither a sliver SHORT of it (an undershoot: the lane appears to dead-end in open ground; note `city_streets_connected` is satisfied by merely touching the lane's outer *edge*, so a lane can be "connected" yet visibly stop short of the bed) nor a sliver PAST it (an overshoot: a stub poking through to the far side instead of stopping at the junction). It covers alleys as well as paved streets (the laborer warren's east E-W alley once stopped ~15px shy of the east ring road - an alley heading straight at a through-lane must reach it too). A genuine 4-way crossroads, where the street truly continues well past, is fine. The fix is to extend an undershoot to the lane's centerline (mind clipping a nearby civic compound - extend a street ALONG ITS OWN axis to the lane, not diagonally to the nearest point) and trim an overshoot back to just inside it. This applies to ALL streets, the government quarter's included - the ring road runs inside the ward too (its SE stretch along the wall), so the gov avenue gives onto its own stretch of the patrol road. That works because **where the ring road crosses a ward fence it is GATED** (a kido at each crossing), sealing the ward's patrol stretch from the commoners' - so the ring road is part of `city_samurai_ward_sealed`'s netlines (find the ring x fence crossings and add a kido at each via `s.ward(..., gates=[...])`). **And the ring road stays CLEAR** (`ring_road_kept_clear`): the whole point of a patrol road is an unobstructed lap of the rampart, so NO building, civic compound (ministry, the governor's yamen, temple), or field footprint may sit on its bed. The wall furniture that SHOULD line it - the gate guard houses, inspection stations, and mural towers - is exempt (those records aren't in the building/civic/field lists), and a ward fence may cross it (gated, per above). The engine keeps the packs off automatically: `s.ring_road` lays a no-build corridor `width/2 + 17` wide along the loop, so even a large or rotated footprint's nearest corner stays well off the bed (Tango's closest dwelling clears it by ~14px). The check fires if any footprint's corner falls within the bed half-width (~4.5px) of the ring centerline or the ring crosses it - the failure mode it caught on Tango was 2 ministry offices and an in-wall farm field straddling the loop; move them inward off the ring (mind that nudging a ministry can land it on the gov avenue - clear both). If you ever shrink the corridor or hand-place a compound near the wall, this is the backstop.
- **The provincial government is in the interior** (every provincial city, walled or not): the **governor's mansion** (`s.governor_mansion(...)`, a grand walled compound; `city_has_governor_mansion`), the **six provincial ministry offices** (`s.ministry(x, y, name)`; `city_has_six_ministries` - Rites, Revenue, Retainers, War, Works, Justice), and a **samurai neighborhood** (`city_has_samurai_neighborhood`). **The Ministry of Rites sits in the temple neighborhood** (`city_has_ministry_of_rites`, exactly one) because it oversees temples and shrines; religious buildings at city scale are **temples** (`religious_matches_scale`, all of `kind="temple"`), and a city can have **several**. Where a **city street runs straight UP TO a temple** (a street that terminates at its front, within ~28px), a **torii arch must stand on that street just in front of the temple** (`city_temple_approach_has_torii`) - pass `s.shrine_hall(..., torii=[(tx, ty)])` a point on the approach (the `torii=` param both draws the arch and reserves a no-build block around it). Torii render in the TOP layer, so the street passes *beneath* the arch (`city_torii_over_streets`); each torii records its draw-z in `M["torii"]` as `[x, y, z]`. Temples set back from the grid (no street running up) need no torii - Tango has a Temple of Benten and a Temple of Daikoku in the SW temple neighborhood and a Temple of Bishamon among the SE samurai (the warrior fortune). **A temple's torii COUNT is its per-temple ROLL, not the remaining street room** (`city_temple_torii_fill_approach` RETIRED 2026-07-24, superseded by the seeded roll - a rolled 1 beside an open street is a hall with one patron gate, not an unfinished avenue; `torii_match_roll` gates drawn == rolled/pinned instead). The gen authors the avenue GEOMETRY to fit its ground: Nagahara's Ebisu rolled the full 7 and takes a COMPRESSED ~19px (57 ft) stride sando ending short of the samurai ward fence - the donation-row look - because the naive 44px extension marched arches across the fence onto the Ministry of War. The torii block reserves only the arch's own footprint (`bm=20`, kept *smaller* than a street corridor) so adding arches along a street doesn't shove the frontage houses off it. **A temple NEIGHBORHOOD (>= 2 temples clustered within ~400px) should be dotted with a smattering of small wayside SHRINES** (`s.small_shrine(x, y)` - a vermilion-roofed shed with a little torii, non-residential, recorded in `M["religious"]` as `kind="small_shrine"`: it is not a dwelling, needs no torii avenue, and is exempt from `religious_matches_scale`). `city_temple_neighborhood_has_shrines` wants >= 3 of them near the clustered temples; a LONE temple among houses (the Bishamon temple in the samurai quarter) is not a neighborhood and needs none. Place the shrines BEFORE the packs (they reserve a no-build block) and clear of the temples/wall/streets. The merchant district and laborer neighborhoods are checked for presence too (`city_has_merchant_district`, `city_has_laborer_neighborhoods`). **The samurai neighborhood must be SIZED to the cohort**: a provincial city is ~10% samurai (~300 of ~3,000, budgets.md) = ~60 households, most housed here as individual houses (the governor's compound + extramural estates hold the rest), so `city_samurai_housing_sufficient` wants >= ~65% of the expected household count (~`0.10 x pop / 5`) drawn as samurai houses - a token cluster of a couple dozen is far too few. Pack them with `face_streets="fill"` (NOT `"core"`: the samurai quarter is laced with government streets, and "core" skips the near-street band, leaving almost everything unbuilt). And unlike the poor, **samurai LINE their streets** - `city_samurai_partly_front_streets` wants at least a third of samurai houses within ~90px of a lane (deeper lots sit behind, but the quarter fronts its streets). **In-city samurai houses VARY IN SIZE by rank, and NONE are walled** (`city_samurai_housing_varied`): budgets.md's provincial-city rank table splits the resident cohort roughly ~25% senior (R5-7) / ~75% junior (R1-4), so the neighborhood mixes a **minority of large senior houses** (`kind="samurai_large"`, the bigger urban dwelling) among **many small junior houses** (`kind="samurai"`). Interleave them in the pack (e.g. `["samurai"] * 4 + ["samurai_large"]` repeated) so the large ones front streets prominently. The check wants >= 3 large houses, the small houses a strict majority, **and NO `s.manor(...)` inside the wall ring** - samurai walled ESTATES sit OUTSIDE the walls (see below); the only walled samurai compound within the city is the governor's mansion. **The inverse also holds: NO free-standing samurai HOUSE stands outside the wall** (`city_samurai_houses_inside_walls`, hard-zero) - the only extramural samurai residences are those walled country estates; an unwalled lone samurai house beyond the rampart is defenseless and has no anchor. The commoner inside-walls check exempts samurai *because of the estates*, which is exactly the gap this closes - and placement code must apply the stay-inside-the-wall test to samurai house glyphs like any other dwelling, exempting only the hand-placed `s.manor` estates (validated instance: Tango's SE gap-fill sweep - a rectangular region poking past the round wall arc, run after the ring bound was cleared - leaked 14 samurai houses into the moat berm, 2026-07-20; Nagahara's SW arc leaked 1 the same way). The **governor's mansion is legitimately LARGE** - the historical provincial *yamen* / governor's compound was a whole city block (main hall, residence, retinue quarters, jail, granary, gardens - dozens of buildings), drawn here walls-only with the interior implied; so its size is correct (`city_governor_mansion_large` enforces that it is the grandest compound - a city block at least as large as any estate and >= 3x any ministry), but like the ministries and temples it must sit INSIDE the rampart, clear of the wall stroke and moat (`city_government_clear_of_wall_moat`). **The five other ministries cluster AROUND the governor's yamen** (the government district, threading into the samurai quarter - as in a Chinese provincial seat / Japanese castle town), not strewn about (`city_ministries_cluster_at_government`, within ~480px of the governor); only Rites sits apart, with the temples it oversees. In a *planned* city the offices are not scattered: the yamen sat where the main streets crossed and the bureaus LINED the avenues around it (the Chinese 'official street'; the jokamachi grid where compounds align tightly along the streets), so **every ministry must FRONT a city street** (`city_ministries_front_a_street`, within ~85px of one) - lay a short government avenue (an L wrapping the yamen works well) and seat the ministries along it. A street fronted by ministries counts as served (the `streets_have_buildings` helper now credits civic buildings - ministries, the governor's yamen, temples, flophouses - as frontage, not just houses and shops). **A government office stands in its OWN ground** (`city_government_offices_dont_abut`): a ministry or the governor's yamen is a large, important compound and must keep a clear gap (~14px) from every other building/compound - ordinary city houses may touch each other, but these may not abut a neighbor (this caught the Ministry of Works touching the Ministry of Justice, and the Ministry of Rites touching the Temple of Daikoku). When two offices are too close, separate them - and mind the knock-on (the Rites/Daikoku fix needed the SE caravan inn nudged east to make room, since Rites is wedged against the ring road). The **internal streets** must likewise stay inside the wall (`city_streets_clear_of_wall_moat`) - the elliptical wall is a *polygon* whose chords cut *inside* the smooth ellipse, so size streets/compounds against the actual wall points (or just inset them), not the ideal ellipse.
- **A walled provincial city must keep >= 1 burakumin neighborhood INSIDE the walls** (`walled_city_has_burakumin_inside`): a city under siege cannot be without its burakumin (corpse-handling, leather, sandals, executions), so however many live outside, a neighborhood always sits within. Not all burakumin need be inside.
- **City streets form a crossing GRID of blocks** (`city_streets_have_buildings`, the same "no street to nowhere" rule as towns). Per quarter, draw a few crossing `s.street(...)` lines (2 N-S x 2 E-W = nine blocks is a good unit), then fill the whole quarter with **one dense `s.pack(bbox, [...], face_streets="fill")`**: the pack faces near-street buildings toward the streets (so every street is lined) and packs the block interiors with tight rows, while respecting the street corridors (so nothing sits on a street). **Density is what lines the grid** - the failure mode is a *sparse* pack leaving a street stretch empty, so pack to the real per-caste counts. Two rules of thumb learned building Tango: (1) don't draw two streets on the same line (a doubled corridor pushes buildings out of fronting range); (2) the big footprints (merchant 54x36, samurai 56x40) need `step >= ~0.8 x footprint` or they collide and place *fewer* - a larger step paradoxically packs more. (`s.frontage(street, [...], rows=N)` - front row plus tight rows behind - also works and is good for a single avenue, but multi-row frontages collide at grid intersections, so prefer dense `pack` for a true crossing grid.) **A larger city street must be LINED with buildings close to it** (`city_larger_streets_lined`): roadside land on a commercial/residential through-street is prime real estate, so no long stretch (>~140px) may run with the nearest building more than ~58px off it - stricter than `city_streets_have_buildings` (which tolerates a building up to ~105px away and so misses a street with a wide bare margin). Narrow gravel ALLEYS are exempt (the "small streets" threading block interiors need no frontage), and so is the GOVERNMENT avenue (its frontage is the spaced ministry compounds, governed by `city_ministries_front_a_street`, not shops/houses - the check exempts a street fronted by >= 2 ministries / the yamen). **Frontage `skip`-object GOTCHA** (this caused the very bug the check now guards): `s.frontage(street, ...)` sits tight against the street by *skipping that street's own corridor*, but it matches the corridor by **object identity** (`poly is skip`). If you pass `s.street(...)` one list literal and `front(...)` a *fresh* literal of the same coordinates, the skip will NOT match the registered corridor, the frontage gets blocked off the street by its own corridor, and the storefronts silently fail to place - leaving a bare avenue. **Capture the street in ONE variable and pass that same object to both** `s.street(AVENUE, ...)` and the frontage call. The grid must also be **one connected network wired to the Imperial road** (`city_streets_connected`) - run at least one street per quarter so its paved bed actually OVERLAPS the road's or another street's. Connectivity is **width-aware**: two lanes count as joined only when their centerline gap is less than the sum of their half-widths (the beds physically touch, so you can walk between them) - a street that stops even a roadbed short of the next reads as a *separate* network and fires (this caught the laborer grid ending 40px shy of the road). Extend the road-facing street of each quarter until it MEETS the road (to its centerline). Kido ward gates do not break connectivity - the street centerline runs on under the gate. Streets must also never come ALMOST together without meeting (`city_streets_no_near_miss`): a pair that closes to within ~2-30px but does not cross reads as a mistake (the classic case is a grid corner where a cross-street stops a sliver short of the through-street) - make the streets actually CROSS (extend one past the other) or pull them clearly apart, never leave a sliver gap. The mirror-image fault is a **stub** (`city_streets_no_intersection_stub`): a street that crosses another and then STOPS a sliver (~3-50px) past it. Fine to cross and run on (to the next block or the edge), or to terminate AT the junction (a clean L/T corner), but not to overshoot it by a little - so at a grid's outer corner, end the two outermost streets at their shared corner point rather than extending each past the other. **A related, more general rule covers ALLEYS too** (`city_lanes_meet_when_aligned`): if two lanes - streets OR alleys - are **heading straight at each other and stop just short**, with a CLEAR path between (no building, ward fence, or wall in the gap), they should simply **connect**. Unlike `city_streets_no_near_miss` (which only compares street-vs-street segment *proximity*), this fires on an *aligned endpoint* - a lane end whose outward direction points within ~37 deg at another lane within ~80px - so it catches collinear lanes that resume a sliver further on (the classic case: a quarter's vertical lane and a continuation lane in the adjacent strip, ending 10-56px apart on the same line). The fix is to extend one lane to meet the other (mind any check that scales to lane length, like `alleys_serve_buildings` - if extending a lane tips its served/length ratio, close the gap from the *other* lane's side instead). A gap that a building/fence/wall genuinely blocks is exempt (the lane is correctly routing around it). The rule is generic to any city with lanes, walled or not. **Lane RENDER LAYERING is enforced** (`city_lanes_layered_by_width`): where two linear features cross, the WIDER renders on top - the Imperial road over the city streets it crosses, streets over the alleys. The engine handles this automatically (`s.street`/`s.alley`/`s.road` defer to one ground layer flushed in width order, so a narrow lane never paints over a wider one); the check guards it via each feature's recorded draw-z. **And lanes meet as clean CROSSROADS** (`intersections_are_crossroads`): the engine flushes the ground block in three sub-layers - all EDGE strokes (the dark curb-borders), then all BED strokes (paved surfaces), then all center-marks - so every edge sits below every bed and the beds merge into a continuous junction. Without this, one lane's edge-border paints a line across the other's mouth where they meet (a street looks like it dead-ends at the road instead of flowing into it). The check guards the invariant: `M["ground_edge_zmax"] < M["ground_bed_zmin"]`. **WALLS render OVER the ground lanes** (`city_lane_under_wall`, `city_lanes_under_ward_fences`): a road/street/alley that runs INTO a wall - the exterior city/town rampart OR an internal neighborhood (ward) fence - must pass **under** it, not paint over it. The engine draws ramparts in a dedicated **wall layer** (`s.add_wall`, recorded `wall_z`) above the ground block and below the TOP layer, so this holds by construction; the city wall (and town arc) are drawn with a **genuine gap** at each gate (`_gapped_ring`) rather than a land rect painted over the stroke - so the wall can sit on top yet the road still shows THROUGH the opening (a painted-over rect would erase the road once the wall is on top). A lane only breaches a wall at a gate, where there is no stroke to render over, so touches/crossings within ~50px of a gate are exempt. The checks fire if any lane that meets a wall has a draw-z >= the wall's (i.e. it would render over it) - so if you ever draw a rampart with plain `s.add` instead of `s.add_wall`, or a lane ends up in the wall layer, it is caught.
- **Shops front the streets; poor housing fills the block INTERIOR, reached by alleys** (`businesses_front_streets` - almost every `shop`/`merchant` within ~85px of a street; `poor_housing_mostly_interior` - most `laborer`/`burakumin` are NOT). The historical pattern: a street grid divides a quarter into blocks, businesses line the paved streets (`s.frontage(street, ["shop", ...])`), and the residential majority jams the deep interior (`s.pack(bbox, ["laborer", ...], face_streets="core")` - "core" leaves the street-facing band for the shop frontage and packs dwellings only DEEP, off the street). **The more mercantile a quarter, the more streets**, but **merchant HOUSING is varied and roomy - the deliberate contrast to the laborers** (uniform, small, jammed tight). Behind the storefronts the homes mix by wealth band (`city_merchant_housing_varied`; budgets.md provincial-city merchants, of ~600 households: very rich 8% -> **walled estates** via `s.merchant_estate(x, y)`, a fenced court with a large house inside, recorded in `M["merchant_estates"]` NOT `M["manors"]`; rich 12% -> **large houses** `kind="merchant_large"`; poor+other 80% -> **small houses** `kind="merchant_house"`). And they are **SPREAD OUT** - `city_merchant_housing_spread` wants the merchant homes' median neighbor gap >= 1.3x the laborers' (pack with a bigger `step`; a few denser blocks are fine, the median is robust). Walled estates need DEEP block cores, so do NOT over-street the merchant quarter into shallow strips: a couple of N-S streets off the avenue leave top-to-bottom blocks the estates and roomy homes fit into. **The estate COURT (the fenced rect, not just the house inside it) is checked for clearance** like any compound: it must sit clear of the wall and moat (`city_merchant_estates_clear_of_wall_moat`) and not overlap any other building - temple, compound, house, or another estate (`city_merchant_estates_clear_of_buildings`; the estate's own inner house, centered in the court, is exempt). So keep estates in the block CORES, well inside the rampart and clear of the temple neighborhood - not jammed against the west wall or sitting on a temple. It IS fine (and historically common) for an estate WALL to abut a neighboring building, but then its **GATE must open onto open ground, never into that building** (`city_merchant_estate_gate_clear`): pass `s.merchant_estate(x, y, gate_dir=...)` the side facing clear space (the estate abutting the Temple of Benten opens NORTH, not south into the temple). The gate point + direction are recorded in `M["merchant_estates"][i]`, and the check rejects a gate whose threshold fronts a compound (temple, ministry, the yamen, or another estate court). A laborer quarter, by contrast, has only a couple of through-streets and very deep blocks. Those deep blocks are subdivided by **unpaved gravel/plank ALLEYS** (`s.alley(pts)` - thinner than a street, a pale speckled lane, a narrow no-build corridor so the dense core leaves a gap), the lanes the interior housing is actually reached by. **An alley is checked like a street** - it must not run over a building (`no_structure_on_street` covers alleys too), nor cross the wall or moat (`city_streets_clear_of_wall`, `city_streets_clear_of_moat`); place alleys BEFORE the frontage so no building sits on a lane, and clip them inside the wall (the elliptical rampart curves in). **No GIANT cluster may be cut off from circulation** (`no_isolated_dwelling_cluster`): housing packs deep, but a big contiguous block of dwellings with no street OR alley within ~95px has no way in or out - lace every deep block (including any space-filling band, like Tango's strip between the laborer and government quarters) with alleys so every dwelling is reachable. Small deep cores are fine; the check flags only a large (>30) isolated cluster. And an alley must EARN its length by UNIQUELY serving dwellings (`alleys_serve_buildings`): each building is credited to its NEAREST lane only (the one it actually fronts), exactly as `streets_have_buildings` scores streets, so a lane counts only what no other lane already reaches. This catches BOTH a lane running off into a half-empty corner (a lane to nowhere) AND a **redundant** lane - one laid beside or across another that already serves the same block. The rule of thumb is **one lane per block**: a block's interior needs a single spine to reach it, so don't add a perpendicular cross-arm the spine already reaches (Tango's west laborer blocks share one continuous vertical spine at x1810 and carry no horizontal cross-alley; only the east block keeps its own L), and don't shadow a street with a parallel alley a few tens of px away (the street already fronts those dwellings). The threshold scales to the buildings (~1 uniquely-served dwelling per 30px of the alley's own length), so it bites at the city's dense small-footprint grain rather than relying on a fixed town pixel-gap. **Exception: a gate-access spur.** An alley that runs out to a **ward kido gate** past its last building is providing gate access, not block-service, so that terminal stretch (from the gate to the nearest building the alley fronts) is subtracted from its length before the ratio - extend a commoner alley to its ward gate freely without tripping this check. Why nearest-lane and not raw proximity: a redundant alley still sits *near* plenty of buildings (raw proximity is fooled into passing it), but those buildings are nearer the spine or street that truly serves them, so the redundant lane's UNIQUE tally collapses toward zero and it fails. Samurai (not poor) may front their streets; merchants front as businesses AND count as dwellings (dual-use). **Laborer HOUSING varies by wealth too** (`city_laborer_housing_varied`): like the samurai (senior/junior) and merchant (estate/large/small) tiers, the hinin are not uniform - budgets.md's provincial-city laborer cohort is ~12.5% **"master" (rich) laborers**, the rest standard. So a clear minority get **larger homes** (`kind="laborer_large"`, ~50x34) among the overwhelming majority of small standard `laborer` dwellings (~34x24). Place the large ones on the **prime back-street FRONTAGE** (the wealthier laborers take the roadside lots, with room around them) via `s.frontage(...)`, and keep the standard poor laborers jamming the deep interior cores (`face_streets="core"` packs). The check wants `laborer_large` at roughly **6-20%** of laborers (a generous band around the 12.5% target, since the big homes are room-limited to street frontage) and a strict standard-laborer majority; `laborer_large` is exempt from `poor_housing_mostly_interior` (it is the wealthy tier, so it *should* line streets).
- **`s.bound` makes placement fill the wall's SHAPE.** Set `s.bound = [list(p) for p in WALL]` after drawing the wall; every `pack`/`ring`/`frontage` then rejects positions outside it, so a dense pack over a generous bbox fills the elliptical ring cleanly (partial blocks at the rampart) instead of a rectangle with empty corners. Reset `s.bound = None` before placing anything OUTSIDE the wall (the estates, off-map fields).
- **A small city GATES its samurai/government ward; it does not WALL every neighborhood** (`city_samurai_quarter_gated`, `city_samurai_ward_sealed`). The walled-ward (Chinese *fang*) system - a continuous internal wall around every quarter - was a great-capital, Tang-era feature (Chang'an's wards were 30-80 hectares each, one outsizing a whole provincial city) and was torn down by the Song. At provincial-city scale the samurai/government quarter is **sealed by a light earthwork/palisade fence** (`s.ward(name, boundary, gates)`) whose ends abut the city wall, pierced ONLY at **kido** wooden ward gates (`s.kido`) where a street crosses it - so the gates can't simply be walked around and the road network has no ungated samurai<->commoner path. The gen must run the quarter's access streets THROUGH the fence line (extend them to the road) so each crossing is a gate. The check wants a ward declared, >= 2 kido near the yamen, every street/road/**ring road**/alley crossing the fence gated within ~32px, and both fence ends within ~45px of the wall. (The ring road is a closed loop near the wall, so it crosses the fence at the two points where the fence ends approach the rampart - gate both.) Keep commoner packs/alleys OUTSIDE the fence. **A commoner lane that APPROACHES the ward fence must reach it and END AT A KIDO GATE** (`city_lanes_reach_ward_gates`) - laborers come in to work in the samurai quarter, so the lanes they use pull right up to a gate rather than stopping a sliver short. (`city_samurai_ward_sealed` only catches lanes that *cross* the fence ungated; this catches lanes that stop *short* of it.) A lane endpoint within ~60px of a ward fence, heading at it (within ~37 deg) with a clear path (no building or the main wall between), must sit on the fence (within ~6px) AND have a kido within ~34px, else it fires. Two important distinctions: (1) **the MAIN city wall is exempt** - a lane may stop short of the outer rampart (that is the city's own edge, not a neighborhood boundary); only internal ward fences pull a lane in. (2) **Interior ward lanes are exempt** - a government/samurai lane near the fence from the INSIDE is not an entry; the check uses an interior anchor (the governor's yamen, else the fence centroid) and skips any endpoint on the same side as it. When you extend an alley to a gate, the run-out *past its last building* is a legitimate **gate-access spur** and does not count against `alleys_serve_buildings` (that check now subtracts the spur for an alley ending at a kido). Add the gates via `s.ward(..., gates=[(x, y, horizontal), ...])` - `horizontal=False` for an N-S lane crossing an E-W fence leg. **The fence ends must MEET SOLID wall** (`city_ward_fence_meets_wall`): not merely near the wall *polygon* (a point can be 40px inside the rampart yet read as on it, since `poly_dist` is 0 for interior points - use `edge_dist`), and NOT landing in a **gate opening** (where the wall is cut, so the fence meets nothing and the ward can be walked around) - extend the fence to solid rampart, jogging clear of the gate if need be. **And the wall renders ON TOP of the fence** at the junction (`city_ward_fence_under_wall`): the fence runs UNDER the rampart, not painting over it - `s.ward` lays a short wall cap (recorded with the fence's z AND its polyline `pts` in `M["wards"][i]["wall_caps"]`) over each end so the rampart wins. **That cap must lie FLUSH along the wall** (`city_ward_cap_flush_to_wall`): it FOLLOWS the rampart - walking the wall +/-16px through any vertex in the span - rather than being a single straight tangent. A straight cap laid where the fence abuts AT a wall CORNER cannot follow the bend, so it juts past the corner and reads as **two wall sections overlapping instead of one bent wall** (the Nagahara SW corner, GM 2026-07). The check samples each cap vertex against the wall polyline and fires if any sits > 4px off it. (Full walled wards become plausible only at the future capital-city tier, ~12,000.)
- **Crop the frame to the CONTENT so the image is only as big as what it shows** (`s.crop_to_content(margin=30)`; a nonstandard image size is fine and expected). This is the GENERAL village-layout step (the city's tight-to-the-walls crop below is the same mechanism, hand-sized). WHY: a fixed canvas leaves dead margins - a village's paddy runs off to one side, the settlement sits in a corner - so `crop_to_content` computes the bounding box of the **HARD** features + `margin` and `set_view`s to it, tight to `margin` on every side. The frame is set ONLY by hard content: `_CROP_HARD` + the fields' **visible** extent + the pond. The fields use a recorded `vis_bbox` (the drawn plots), NOT the house-blocking envelope polygon - that envelope can have an invisible tail past the last plot, and framing to it re-introduces dead space (a real bug: the south margin was once ~210px too low by the envelope's tail).
  - **Everything else clips at the frame; it never extends it.** The **commons** scrub AND the linear/off-map **runners** (streams, channels, lanes) are drawn and simply CUT at the crop edge, trailing off as "more wild ground / more map this way". We used to *extend* the frame to preserve ~2/3 of a trailing commons ("bleed"), but that repeatedly held the frame open on empty back-slope grazing - past the graveyard on the west, ~130px past the lone pond on the east - which is exactly the dead space the crop is meant to remove. So the commons now clips like the marsh: **the frame hugs the real settlement (houses, fields, pond, groves, graveyard), never the scrub around it.** (If a map ever *wants* a wilderness feature to widen the frame, add it to `_CROP_HARD`, don't reach for a bleed rule.)
  - **The communal windbreak does NOT set the frame** (GM 2026-07-20): `crop_to_content` no longer counts `village_groves` - the belt CLIPS at the view edge, and a partially visible belt reads as "the wood continues". Prefer the SMALLER crop: a larger frame whose only extra content is more of the same grove is wasted image (this held Kikuta's north edge ~300px open). Two checks gate the rule: **`crop_hugs_content`** (each view edge within 56px of the outermost frame-setting content - crop margins run 30-44, so a conforming crop passes with a little slack while a grove-held edge fires) and `hard_features_within_frame`, which for `village_groves` now demands partial visibility instead of containment (a belt entirely OUTSIDE the view is still a lost feature and fires). Homestead `groves` still set the frame (each hugs its own farmhouse, so it never drags it). Fixing this exposed a latent crop bug: wells record `{x, y, r}` and the crop's poly/w-h reader silently ignored them - the grove band had been covering for the wellheads; the crop now reads the `r` form too.
  - **Call order matters for SET-APART hard features.** Anything the frame must CONTAIN has to be placed BEFORE `crop_to_content`: the large features (water, fields, houses, groves) and also any **outlying** hard feature that sits beyond the cluster - a back-slope **graveyard**, an outlying **shrine** - or the tight crop will clip it (this bit Ueda: its west-set graveyard, placed after the crop, got sliced once the frame stopped being padded by scrub). Only features that DROP INTO the framed space (wells among the houses, monk plots) and the **title** go AFTER the crop - the title is placed last so it lands inside the window (there is no compass - see the label note above). **`hard_features_within_frame` gates this** (village/hamlet): every hard feature - houses, groves, the graveyard, the shrine, wells, the torii - must lie INSIDE the cropped `meta["view"]`, so a deferred feature that lands off-frame and gets silently clipped is caught rather than only spotted by eye.
  - Linear / off-map **RUNNERS** (streams, channels, the connector lane) are ignored - they clip at the frame, and their off-edge checks already read the crop (`meta["view"]`) as the map edge, so a connector/feeder/brook that ran to the old canvas edge still "runs off" the new one.
  - **Crop advisory (SOFT default, `crop_relocatable_singletons` / the `ADVISORY crop_could_tighten` line):** unlike the hard invariants, this NEVER fails the gate - it prints a hint. It flags the case where a SINGLE, freely-relocatable feature is the ONLY thing holding a crop edge out, and there is EMPTY space to move it into - so moving that one feature crops the image significantly smaller without disturbing anything else. Fires only when ALL hold: (1) a village/hamlet that crops to content (a city/town frames bespoke); (2) removing the feature pulls an edge in by **>= 150px** (it is the unique extreme, big slack); (3) the feature is not **hydrologically or terrain anchored** - a **pond that sources a field** (a channel `frm=pond -> to=field`) is a valley-head reservoir that belongs uphill of the field, and a shrine whose center sits on `M["hill"]` can't move to flat ground; both are exempt automatically; (4) an equal-size EMPTY landing, clear of all SOLID occupancy (buildings, fields, groves, forest, marsh, hill - **but not the sparse commons scrub, which a pond can simply replace**), fits INSIDE the tighter frame. Because the field-sourcing-pond exemption covers every irrigation pond, the *singleton* form fires on **no** pool map - it stays a general detector for a genuinely free feature (a standalone/decorative pond, a mis-sited cemetery). A map that still WANTS to silence a fire on an intentional placement can set `meta(crop_advisory=False)`. Not a manifest-recorded check, so no regression fixture - covered by `test_checks` unit tests.
    - **A candidate can be a GROUP, not just a lone feature (`_shrine_group`, `members > 1`).** A village SHRINE and the churchyard GRAVEYARD it is responsible for (plus its ablution well and torii) form ONE sacred precinct - you relocate the whole precinct, not the altar alone. The single-feature detector is BLIND to this: remove the shrine alone and the graveyard still pins the same crop corner (and vice versa), so each reads as "not the unique extreme" and neither fires. So the advisory also builds **group candidates**: for each shrine, gather the cemetery within ~300px, the well within ~150px, the torii within ~140px, **and the shrine's own `shrines`/`religious` mirror record** (the same shrine is stored under both keys, and both are crop-drivers - miss the mirror and the copy left behind pins the edge). A group is only a candidate when a **real companion** (a graveyard/well/torii) attaches - a bare shrine plus its mirror is still just the singleton. The whole group's COMBINED bbox is what must find an empty, DRY (marsh is solid occupancy here), appropriate landing inside the tighter frame; it moves as one rigid unit. **Why it exists:** Hikari-no-Sato's Bishamon shrine + its graveyard sat together at the far SW, holding the S crop edge out ~198px with a lot of empty dry ground higher up - a tighter crop was available but no single-thing move could see it. The group form "realizes" the shrine and graveyard can both move together. Hikari is the driving test case (`test_crop_advisory_realizes_the_bishamon_group_on_the_real_hikari_map`). This is a HINT, not an auto-move: the generator still places the precinct by hand; the advisory just flags when relocating it as a unit would pay off.
    - **The valley-head pond, and the NUDGE (the right way to reclaim a pond's poke).** The check now *auto-exempts* a field-sourcing pond (above), because moving it into the frame would drop it downhill of the field's water-entry - backwards for a gravity feed. So you do **not** relocate it. **But you can still reclaim the cheap part of the slack with a small NUDGE.** A pond only needs to *contain its sluice* to feed the field, so draw it decoupled from the `build_comb` anchor (keep `POND`/`SLUICE`/`build_comb`/feed-anchor untouched - the field is unchanged - and draw at a separate `POND_DRAW`), sliding it a little so its far edge sits **flush with the field/dry-plots** instead of poking past. The sluice stays inside the drawn ellipse, so the `frm=pond` topology still anchors. Ueda's pond is nudged ~157px W (E edge flush with the dry-field strip, ~9% smaller image); its remaining N poke is the irreducible valley-head cost and is simply accepted. Re-orienting the whole field to dodge the poke is **not** worth it: a pure mirror (NE-high -> NW-high) just flips which side the pond pokes and erases the deliberate variance between sibling villages.
    - **Where a nudged pond's channels meet it, they must JOIN at the RIM, not overlap the water.** Nudging the pond so it *contains* the sluice means the head-race would otherwise be drawn starting *inside* the pond (over the water). Clip each channel's in-pond vertices to the pond boundary before drawing (Ueda's `_clip_pond`) so it emerges cleanly from the rim - the same "join, don't overlap" rule roads/streams already follow. Clip the DRAWN geometry only; the recorded channel keeps its sluice endpoint so `frm=pond` still anchors. (An inflow brook drawn *before* the pond is already covered by the water, so it needs no clip.)
- **A city map crops TIGHT to the walls** (`s.set_view(ox, oy, w, h)` directly, rather than `crop_to_content` - a city is framed to its WALL, not its scattered outside estates). A town map is as much about its surroundings as the town; a **city** map is about the city - the countryside around it matters little, so the rendered window should *just barely encompass the walled city* (wall + moat + a ~50px margin for the title), zooming the city itself as large as the canvas allows. Compute it from the wall: `s.set_view(CX-RX-52-M, CY-RY-52-M, 2*(RX+52+M), 2*(RY+52+M))` (52 ≈ moat gap + wall stroke, `M` ≈ 50). Placement still uses the full coordinate space, so the estates, outside farmland, and the far rows of the gate market simply **run off the cropped edge** - they need not be fully rendered. Crucially, the **checks read `meta["view"]` and treat the crop, not the full canvas, as the map edge**: "runs off the edge" (road, moat-feeder stream, off-map fields) means off the *view*. So size the view to clear the moat but let the estates fall outside it. The title sits top-left *inside* the view (it follows automatically). The off-wall estates remain recorded (`s.manor`), so the estate checks (1-3 shown, dispersed, SE, no-overlap) still pass even though most estates are off-map entirely.
- **Size the wall to HOLD the city - no large empty swaths inside** (`city_no_large_empty_space`, ported from the town's `wall_hugs_the_town`). A wall encloses what it must defend; an oversized ring with a big empty perimeter would not have been built. The fix is the inverse of the town's: rather than pulling a wall in around a fixed built area, **size the ring to the ~600 households and fill it densely** (the city's 3 ft/px grain - `bscale = 1/3` - keeps the true-size footprints small enough to pack ~600 into a hugging wall). A city keeps SOME open ground, but every deliberate open is CLAIMED by a feature record (a right-of-way, a field, a working yard); ground claimed by NOTHING, sitting on wall-protected premium land, would not have been left bare. *Detection (REBUILT footprint-aware, GM 2026-07-23):* the GM caught a ~230x95px bare pocket (~600x330 real ft, ~1.6 ac) just inside Tango's north gate that the original detector passed - that pass sampled an 80px grid and called a cell "used" within 120px of any building CENTER, a radius so wide a single house sanitized a 240px disc, so only vast voids could ever fire. The rebuilt detector counts every claiming feature at its real FOOTPRINT (building/compound/grove rects, field and ground polys, well / stable-yard / torii discs, road / street / alley / ring-road / water rights-of-way, ward fences, the rampart + patrol strip, the pond), marks 32px-grid cells >= 20px clear of ALL of them as dead ground, and fails any contiguous dead cluster >= 4,000 px2 of core. *Calibration (pool-wide dry-run, 2026-07-23):* Tango's pocket measures 6,144 px2 of core; the largest legitimate opens anywhere else measure 2,048 (Tango) / 1,024 (Nagahara) - the threshold sits between with ~2x headroom both ways (pre-fix Tango is frozen in `pool/regressions/` so the check keeps teeth). *Remedies, in preference order:* fill the ground (extend a quarter / drop in a neighborhood), or claim it as deliberate working ground - the standing EASY option is **`s.animal_ground(cx, cy, r, label=...)`**, a standalone stable-yard scatter (beaten earth, hitching rails, tethered oxen, cart litter; it auto-avoids roads, fields, water, the rampart, and every footprint, and records `M['stable_yards']`, which the detector counts as claimed). Extra animal space is the natural claim when the pocket adjoins a gate or the stables: first applied to Tango's north gate, where Phoenix-border caravan traffic wants marshalling room (the north gate serves trains coming down from, or departing toward, Phoenix lands).
- **Civic amenities port up from the town tier** (a city is a bigger version of the same market center): merchant houses keep fireproof *kura* (`s.merchant_storehouses(...)`, `city_has_merchant_storehouses` >= 5), there is market-day lodging (`s.flophouse(...)`, `city_has_flophouse`) - one INSIDE the walls (`city_flophouse_inside_walls`) AND one just OUTSIDE EVERY gate (`city_flophouse_outside_each_gate`, within ~520px): **convenience lodging at the busy market gate** for peasants, carters, and peddlers arriving from either direction (see the WHY below - this replaces the old "stranded by the dusk gate-curfew" rationale, which the research found is a *Tang* artifact that had relaxed by the Song/Ming rice-south period we model; the outside-gate placement itself is well-grounded in the extramural gate-suburb/*guanxiang* clustering pattern). **WHY the count (`flophouse-research.md`, deep-research pass 2026-07-22, GM decision):** the outside-gate/gate-suburb PLACEMENT is historically supported, but how MANY cheap inns a settlement held is genuinely unknowable - the ruling class did not count or record peasant lodging (gazetteers foreground official post-stations). The symmetric "1 in + 1 outside each gate" is therefore a deliberate, legible stylization on the generous side of an uncertain range, an intentional demographic choice for a Rokugan that is more peasant-attentive than its historical models, *extrapolated by combining historical precedent with Rokugani demographics*. (Considered and declined: concentrating on only the busiest gate; drawing a distinct animal-yard cart-inn compound.) The **in-wall flophouse is a humble doss-house and belongs in a humble quarter** (`city_flophouse_in_humble_quarter`): the laborer section, or - Tango's case - the agrarian sector, never within ~110px of a temple/merchant/samurai (the nicer neighborhoods) and never within ~150px of (in or beside) the burakumin quarter. **Each city gate gets a CARAVAN transit cluster just inside it** (`city_gate_caravan_facilities`): a town inn can hide its small stables, but a wagon-train arriving at or passing through a city brings **many dozens of draft animals (oxen, packhorses) plus guards, porters, and drivers**, so within ~340px of each gate there must be all THREE of a **flophouse**, a prominent **inn** (`s.inn(x, y)` - a warm building with a red hanging sign), and a **large stables** (`s.stables(x, y)` - stall-division lines), with **open ground around the stables** (the check fails if more than 4 dwellings crowd within ~75px - the animals need room to be tied up or penned; no need to draw the fencing). This caravan cluster is the one place an in-wall flophouse may sit beside an inn/stables rather than alone (the humble-quarter check exempts a flophouse that has both an inn AND a stables within ~170px). There is also a theater stage (`s.theater_stage(...)`, `city_has_theater_stage`), which - like a town's - must sit ADJACENT to a temple (`theater_stage_by_temple`); a **CITY theater stage is bigger than a town's** (`city_theater_stage_larger_than_town`, viewing-ground width >= 185, vs the town baseline ~120-150). Tango's sits in the Temple of Benten's precinct (the two merchant estates that crowded Benten were moved to the freed central ground). Place the theater stage/flophouse BEFORE the dense packs so the packs flow around them.
