(Not ported: the farmer-plurality - a city has zero in-city farmers (but it DOES have caste-count bands of its own, `city_caste_counts_in_band` - see Scale and density above); the monastery clan-patron system - a city has temples; `wall_sections_irregular` - a city wall is a regular defensive ring; the hill and gate-market rules.) **The full lodging program (DECIDED, GM 2026-07-24; research in `flophouse-research.md` "Inn counts, occupancy, and the by-employment household"):** a non-post-station highway seat of ~3,000 runs ~8-15 lodging houses - the 2-4 proper inns + 2-4 flophouses the map already draws as dedicated glyphs, plus **5-8 small family hatago that are DELIBERATELY NOT distinct buildings**: historically these were ordinary shophouses whose back rooms took lodgers (households living on the meal trade, farming, and porterage - lodging was the add-on, and on procession nights the whole town became the billet), so on the map several of the road-market and gate-market `shop` rows are understood to sleep travelers. No check counts the implied hatago; the inn/flophouse floors gate the dedicated glyphs.
- **Cramped city lots push the wealthiest samurai to walled ESTATES OUTSIDE** the wall, which they commute in from - they can afford grander houses than the limited intramural space allows. A city map shows only the nearest **1-3** of them (`city_samurai_estates_outside`, `s.manor(...)` beyond the wall - the rest are dispersed across the rural district, miles out and off-map) and they **vary in size** (`city_samurai_estates_vary_in_size` - the largest at least 1.5x the smallest; some estates are far grander than others). The estates all lie toward the capital (`city_estates_toward_capital`, SE for Tango) and are DISPERSED - each its own compound on its own land, **>= 200px apart**, never a tight cluster (`city_samurai_estates_dispersed`; the dense belt hugging the wall is the commercial gate-suburb, not estates). They must **not overlap each other** (`city_estates_no_overlap`) nor **cross the wall or moat** (`city_estates_clear_of_wall_moat`). **Their gates do NOT all open the same way** (`city_estate_gates_vary`): each scattered country estate fronts its OWN approach lane (not drawn at this scale), so pass `s.manor(..., gate_dir=...)` a MIX - the formal gate favours the auspicious **south**, others face the cityward (NW) approach (west/north) - rather than letting them all fall to the default. (The depicted gate is the formal one; the cityward service gates, like the governor's unshown secondary gates, are omitted at this scale.) Because the view crops tight to the walls, place the estates so **at least two fall (even partly) inside the window** (`city_estates_multiple_shown`) - estates straddling the SE edge, cropped, signal *several* estates rather than one; the same barrier rule applies to the **temples** - all of them sit INSIDE the walls (`city_temples_inside_walls`) and clear of the wall stroke and moat (`city_temples_clear_of_wall_moat`).
- **The surrounding farmland is close, farmhouse-worked, and (if moated) irrigated from the moat.** A city grows up around fertile land, so its outside fields sit **close** to the walls (`city_fields_close_to_city`); every outside field is worked by villagers, so each has **farmhouses ringing it even if it runs off the map edge** (`city_outside_fields_have_farmhouses`, >= 2 houses - build the comb field, then `s.ring(('poly', envelope), n, gap, ["plain"])`; some fields still run off-edge per `city_has_outside_farmland`). **City fields are water-first COMBS like everywhere else** - one `build_comb` call per field (own sluice/seed/fall), NOT the legacy `paddy_field` quilt (45-deg multicolor patchwork with no in-field water - the GM retired it). At 3 ft/px the comb params scale down: `plot_across=26` (~78 ft strips), `row_step=(13,19)` (~40-57 ft cascade rows), canal spans in the 60-260px band, `field_fall` ~90-190 so a city-fringe comb stays the size of the field it replaces (mind the 55,000px^2 bbox floor that makes a field count as "large" for moat irrigation). **Dry crop plots are FOOTPRINT-aware no-build cropland** (`structures_clear_of_dry_plots`, `groves_clear_of_dry_plots`, any map with `dry_plots`): register each hem strip / vegetable-tract plot via `s.dry_polys.append(poly)`, NOT `s.block_polys` - block polys test only a candidate's CENTER, which let a house nudged for its yard (or a ring house at the envelope gap) stand half its footprint on a hem strip, and the grove pass ignored them entirely (GM caught farmsteads and windbreak clumps on Tango's hems, 2026-07). `dry_polys` get a 12px edge margin in `_fits` and a rect test in `_grove_fits` (exactly like the paddy envelopes); the checks allow ABUTTING (footprints shrunk ~6%, clumps at 0.75r) - a hem may run right up to a wall, it just may not be built on. Crucially, the SHOWN portion of each outside field must carry farmhouses at roughly **village density** (`outside_fields_farmhouse_density`, town + city): the check clips the field to the rendered window, measures the **on-map field edge** (the real boundary inside the view, excluding the map-edge cut), and requires **in-view** farmhouses at >= ~7 per 1000px of that edge (village fields run ~4-19, aggregate ~12). A field ringed only around its full, mostly-off-map bbox leaves almost nothing in view (Tango once showed 3) and fails - **ring densely so enough farmhouses land on the on-map edge** (most fall off-map, which is fine). At **city** scale **no farmhouses count toward the city population** (`population_consistent_with_housing` counts only the urban residential kinds for cities - the farmers, surrounding OR in-wall, are not in the documented ~3,000 urban castes, budgets.md), so you can ring as densely as the view needs without touching the figure; at town scale the depicted farmhouses ARE the (partial) county farmer cohort and do count. Fields must not cut across the wall stroke or the moat (`city_fields_clear_of_wall_moat`) - they abut the moat, not overlap it (mind the polygonal wall/moat, which curve in near the gates). A **moated** city always irrigates **>= 3 large fields from the moat** (`city_moat_irrigates_fields`): each comb's SLUICE sits a stride outside the actual moat rim (compute it from the moat polyline - nearest upstream vertex + ~30px outward - so the tap self-corrects), with a short drawn stub bridging moat rim -> sluice and a recorded hairline source channel `[moat rim, sluice, a plot centroid]` - the END must sit INSIDE the field outline (`point_in_poly`; use a plot centroid, never the envelope centroid of a curved fan, which can miss) and downstream of the tap. **The moat GROUNDS the ditch network both ways** (`field_ditches_reach_source_and_sink`): `frm=moat` is a SOURCE (a fed watercourse) and `to=moat` is a SINK (the moat is the city's storm drain) - so a comb's collector may empty INTO the moat (the north field's runoff culvert joins the moat bed's edge) or run off the cropped view (record `frm=drain, to=offmap`). An IN-WALL field's drain records the moat as its sink but its VISIBLE ditch **stops short of the patrol road** - the runoff drops into an implied UNDERGROUND stone conduit beneath the ring road, rampart and moat (GM: never draw a ditch running through the city wall; the water gate is underground). And every drawn channel that MEETS the moat gets the pond treatment (`_clip_to_moat`, the twin of `_clip_to_pond`, applied in `field_channel`): its endpoint snaps onto the moat bed's EDGE with a ~3px inset so the mouth covers the rim stroke - a tap or culvert joins the open water cleanly, never drawing its bed as a colored line across it (taps therefore START from the moat's edge, not the centerline vertex they were computed from). Record these topology channels with a bend (a ruler-straight channel fires `channel_winds_gently`), at hairline width (2.0-3.5px, `irrigation_channels_hairline`), and REGISTER their corridors (`s.corridors.append((poly, 33))`) or the farmstead rings will build on top of them. **The moat has a flow direction, and channels must run WITH it** (`moat_channels_flow_with_current`): the feeder stream enters from one side and that heading, snapped to a cardinal, is the way the moat water flows (Tango's feeder enters from the north, so the moat flows **south**). Tap a moat vertex **upstream** of the field (north of it, for a southward flow) so the channel runs downstream to the field; a channel whose field is upstream of its tap reads as water flowing *from the field into the moat*, backwards. A field that is itself upstream of the whole moat (e.g. NORTH of a north-fed moat) is uphill of the current and **cannot be moat-fed** - run it off the edge with its water implied off-map, or feed it from the source stream, and make up the moat-irrigated count with a downstream (south/east/west) field instead.
- **Neighborhood/zone labels must sit WITH the cluster they name** (`city_labels_placed_with_subject`). A label like `"samurai neighborhood"`, `"merchant district"`, `"burakumin neighborhood"`, or `"samurai estates"` must be (1) **entirely on the same side of the wall** as what it labels (the laborer/burakumin/samurai/merchant/agricultural labels INSIDE the rampart, the extramural-estates label OUTSIDE), (2) **among its buildings** (the nearest of its subject within ~130px for a house cluster, more for sparse manors/temples/fields), and (3) **not floating over a foreign field or compound**. The subject is inferred from the label text (`estates`->the extramural manors, `agricultural`->the IN-WALL fields, `temple`->temples, else the matching building kind). The fix is always to move the `s.label(...)` onto its own cluster - not the quarter's edge over a neighbor, not out over the moat. The label TEXT is recorded in the manifest (`M["labels"][i][5]`) so the gate can match label to subject.
- **The FARM BELT is within reach of wells too** (`farm_wells_within_reach`, town+city; `s.farm_wells()` after `s.farmsteads()`; fixtures: Tango + Hirameki pre-fix). The urban idobata checks scope to commoner dwellings in the core, so the farmsteads ringing the outside fields had NO well coverage at all - Nagahara's interior steadings sat a median ~970 real ft from the nearest well (GM's eye: "too sparse", 2026-07-21). The rule: **no farmhouse stands more than 500 REAL FEET from a well** (a ~2-minute bucket walk; historically a farmstead often dug its own dooryard well, and Rokugan's unusually well-run domains sink wells liberally - the same liberty as the literal urban idobata count). **Map-edge steadings (within 150 real ft of the view edge) are exempt** - their fields already run off-map and their well is presumed just off the edge with the rest of the steading. The placer seats each well in a steading's dooryard or the open margin between steadings (the belt's ground is mostly crop, where a wellhead may not stand); where the only open ground is field-ENVELOPE rim slack, that is a legitimate seat (unplanted margin), tested against the DRAWN plots instead of the smoothed outline.
- **Public WELLS dot the commoner warren** (`city_neighborhoods_have_wells`, `city_wells_in_block_interiors`). Ensuring every commoner could draw water was a defining civic concern of a premodern city; the communal neighborhood well (井戸, the *idobata* social hub) served a courtyard / cluster of ~10-20 households, so the warren is sprinkled with them - one within a short walk of any home. They are the ONLY visible part of the water system: the aqueducts, underground cisterns, and rain barrels that fed the shafts are too small or literally subterranean and stay OFF the map. A wellhead (`s.well(x, y)`) is a stone curb under an open-sided roof, SMALLER than a house, and sits in a block INTERIOR off the lanes. Scatter them with **`s.place_wells(bbox, spacing)`** (a grid that tries a few offsets per cell, dropping any candidate on a lane / compound / the bound via the same `_fits` test the houses use) BEFORE that quarter's `s.pack(...)` so the houses flow around them; for a cramped, lane-laced quarter the grid can't reach (Tango's shallow burakumin lane-strip, the gap-fill band between the alleys), hand-seed a candidate list through **`s.well_at(x, y)`** (places only if the spot is clear). Tango runs ~47 wells (roughly the literal count for ~600 households at ~1 per 10-20, in the same draw-everything spirit as the houses). Two checks enforce this from different angles. **Coverage** (`city_neighborhoods_have_wells`): fires if any commoner dwelling (laborer/burakumin/merchant kinds) INSIDE the walls is more than ~290px from a well - samurai have private wells in their compounds (excluded), servants are interleaved and share the commoners' wells (ride along), and a transient gate market OUTSIDE the wall is not housing (excluded). **Density** (`city_well_density_sufficient`): assigning each commoner dwelling (servants included) to its NEAREST well, fires if any well is the nearest for more than **26** households - because coverage alone can look fine on AVERAGE while the busiest wells in the dense laborer warren are swamped (the 290px reach is satisfied by one well per radius, but a dense warren packs far more than 20 households into that radius). The ceiling is a touch above the historical 20 because the nearest-well split over-counts where two wells are nearly equidistant. The dense laborer/gap-fill quarters therefore need tighter `place_wells` spacing than the merchant quarter. `city_wells_in_block_interiors` is the placement backstop: a wellhead must sit clear of the lanes and not overlap a building/compound. **The SAMURAI/GOVERNMENT quarter has NO public wells** (`city_samurai_quarter_has_no_public_wells`): samurai drew from PRIVATE wells inside their own walled compounds, and gathering at the communal *idobata* was a commoner-district institution (beneath samurai status) - so a public wellhead must not sit among the samurai dwellings. The check is RELATIVE (a well is "in the samurai quarter" if most of its nearest dwellings are samurai), so it correctly ignores a commoner well sitting a block from the quarter across the ward fence rather than relying on a brittle absolute distance. Don't call `place_wells`/`well_at` in the samurai quarter. The drawn wellhead is a **location MARKER under the stroke convention** (GM ruling 2026-07-21, see SKILL.md "to scale": a real curb is ~3-4 ft, sub-glyph at every tier, so the marker denotes the well's to-scale location without claiming its own pixels are to scale) and **scales with the map grain**: `s.well` draws its ~24.8 ft marker footprint through `px()` (city ~8px, town ~25px, village ~12px) and records the drawn radius as `vr` on each well. A fixed-pixel wellhead looked right in a dense city but shrank to a quarter of a house at village/town scale, where buildings are drawn at full size - the well must track the same grain. `wells_sized_to_buildings` enforces this at EVERY scale: mean well diameter over the median dwelling's larger dimension must land in **[0.35, 0.85]** (a well is naturally smaller than a house, but not a dot). The reserved footprint and block-poly also scale with `vr`, so at every scale the well still reserves only a TIGHT courtyard (houses ring it closely) - each well costs roughly its own footprint, not a whole house-plot, so keep that reservation small or a city's worth of wells visibly deflates the population. NOTE wells still displace SOME housing, so re-check the population/caste bands after adding them (to keep Tango's depicted population a little above its declared 3,000 - dwellings x5 - the laborer packs are stepped tight, and the busiest west edge of the warren is given a few extra `well_at` wells so no well exceeds the density ceiling).
- **The RURAL tiers need wells too** (`settlement_has_wells`, `settlement_dwellings_watered`, for `town` / `village` / `hamlet`). Every settlement keeps communal wells - one per ~20-25 households - so `s.place_wells(<dwelling bbox>, spacing=..., near=85)` AFTER the farmhouses. **Pass `near=` for the rural tiers** (the city omits it): the bare grid would scatter wells out into the open fields and countryside between the field-rings, but `near=N` only keeps a candidate that has a dwelling within `N` px, so wells sit AMONG the houses. (A well must serve households around it; `wells_among_dwellings`, below, enforces this at every scale.) A dispersed farm household may instead draw from the **irrigation network it sits beside**, so a dwelling counts as *watered* if a well **OR** a channel / pond / stream / moat is within reach (~380px at the rural grain): the well count makes wells PRESENT, the coverage check makes sure no household is left dry. Tune the spacing per map (the hamlet shares ~1-2, a 60-household village ~6-9, a town ~16) so the worst-served dwelling - usually a far field-ring farmhouse - is within reach; the city tier keeps its own finer suite (density, block-interior placement, the samurai-quarter exemption) instead.
- **A well must sit AMONG the dwellings it serves** (`wells_among_dwellings`, every scale): a communal well is the draw-point for the households around it, so one out in open ground with no building within ~95px is unreal. A city's `s.pack(...)` runs after `place_wells` and fills in around the wells (so they end up surrounded); the rural tiers must use `place_wells(..., near=...)` (their grid runs after the houses and would otherwise drop wells into the fields). This is the bug it caught: Hirameki's wells scattered into the empty countryside.
- **A set-apart SHRINE keeps its OWN WELL close by** (`remote_shrine_has_own_well`, rural tiers). A shrine/temple set sufficiently apart from the village (its nearest dwelling is >150px away) is too far to use the village's shared wells, so it needs its OWN ablution well (*temizu*) right beside it - and specifically a WELL, not just a nearby ditch/pond (those are not ablution sources). A shrine among/near the houses shares theirs (exempt). Place it with **`s.shrine_well(cx, cy)`** AFTER the hall + houses + village wells: it tries widening rings until a well fits clear of the hall/torii/graveyard/lanes, so a large hall pushes its well onto an outer ring; the "close by" test is measured to the hall's EDGE (a big monastery's well sits further from its center), as is `wells_among_dwellings` (a shrine's own well stands beside the shrine, not among houses, so religious halls count as served). **A HILLTOP/mountain shrine is exempt** (it sits on `M['hill']`) - it draws from a spring/basin, and you cannot dig a well on a hill (no current pool map uses a hill-shrine; the exemption stands for any map that does). Both Hoshigaoka's water-mouth shrine and Kikuta's flat-ground Benten sit apart from the houses, so each keeps its own ablution well beside the hall.
- **Wells - research + deliberate liberty** (`wells_sized_to_population`, GM 2026-07-21). *What the research found:* a pre-modern south-China rice village of ~70 households ran **1-3 communal drinking wells total, 2 typical** - drinking water came mostly from SURFACE water (canal/pond/stream, stored in vats, settled, boiled), which is why schistosomiasis was endemic in the Yangtze rice belt for two millennia and why >70% of rural China still drank untreated surface water in the early 1980s; wells were expensive durable capital financed by per-family subscription and dug only as surface quality forced; the classical jingtian "8 families per well" is a Warring-States ideal nobody practiced. Japan corroborates from the other side: valley villages sited on springs/streams needed few or no communal wells, the famous dense pattern (~10-18 households per well, the idobata gossip circle) is URBAN nagaya tenement density, and per-household wells appear only on shallow-water-table plains. Capacity is never the constraint (one open well serves ~400 people by Sphere/UNICEF anchors, and a nucleated village is ~250m across so carrying distance never binds) - digging cost and morning queueing are. *The decision (a DELIBERATE LIBERTY):* Rokugan is deliberately unusually well-run, and generous water infrastructure expresses that - so **villages run ~1 communal well per 8-26 households** (2-3x the historical count) and **hamlets down to per-farmstead wells (2-20 hh/well)**, the shallow-water-table pattern made standard. This is a knowing departure from the historical 1-3-wells baseline, chosen over historical fidelity for the same reason as the Imperial roads: prosperity is part of the setting's thesis. Shrine (temizu) ablution wells are engine-tagged `shrine: true` and excluded from the count.
- **Torii - research + the numerology rule** (`torii_count_canonical`, GM 2026-07-21). *What the research found:* torii were VOTIVE DONATIONS, not shrine construction - a shrine's count records its accumulated patronage (ujiko subscriptions, grateful merchants, the local lord), a culture that boomed in the Edo period. The historical distribution: **1 torii is the overwhelming mode** (~90%+ of true village shrines); **0 is the norm only BELOW the shrine tier** (hokora/wayside god-shelves, which vastly outnumbered real shrines - a proper shrine with none was rare enough that each had a story); **2-3** is the ranked-shrine tier (the numbered ichi/ni/san-no-torii on long approaches, 3 the conventional ceiling); and the **dozens-plus tail is specifically the Inari donation-row cult** (Edo-onward, a handful to a few dozen at a modest rural Inari, hundreds only at famous cult sites, ~10,000 at Fushimi). No scholarly per-shrine census exists - the shape is assembled from normative statements plus attested examples. *The Rokugan rule (a deliberate liberty):* the number 7 is even MORE numerologically potent in Rokugan than in the real world, so every proper religious site - shrine, monastery, temple - carries **exactly 1, 3, or 7 torii**, never another number, unless the hall is explicitly marked `shrine_hall(torii_outlier=True)` (always with a recorded story). Rolled per tier by `settlement.roll_torii_count`: **village 60/30/10**, **town 30/60/10**, **provincial city 30/40/30**, **capital 10/60/30** for 1/3/7 (capital recorded ahead of need - no capital maps exist yet). *The FULL RE-ROLL (GM 2026-07-23):* the GM noticed the city maps carried suspiciously few arches - the table had landed but the town/city gens' hand-placed `torii=[...]` counts predated it and were never re-rolled (Tango + Nagahara sat at four 1s and one 3, a ~1%-likely draw under the city column). Now the roll is wired into `shrine_hall` itself: `torii=[...]` is the avenue GEOMETRY (points marching AWAY from the hall - drawn first-n if the roll is smaller, extended along the avenue's own stride, or at 44px from a single point, if larger), the COUNT is a per-temple seeded roll on the tier column (deterministic in map seed + hall position), pinnable per hall with `torii_count=N` - the per-hall analog of the village path's map-level `torii_count` knob (that path, `roll_village`'s civic shrine, still rolls for itself and records `meta.torii_count`). The resolved target is recorded on the religious rec and gated by `torii_match_roll` (drawn, ATTRIBUTED count == target), so a stale hand count or a misattributed arch can never ship silently. Pinned exemplars, with their stories: Kikuta's dense 7-arch senbon sando and Hikari's ichi/ni/san 3-avenue are GM-approved canon, so they pin rather than re-roll. Post-re-roll counts: Tango 1/1/3 (the dice agreed with the old map), Nagahara Bishamon 1 / Ebisu 7, Hirameki Bishamon 3 / Benten 7, Hoshizora 3, Ueda 3. The re-roll retired the two space-driven completeness checks (`city_temple_torii_fill_approach`, `monastery_torii_scale_with_space`) - avenue completeness is defined by the roll, and the count is PATRONAGE, not street room. `kind="small_shrine"` is the hokora tier: exempt (its glyph carries a miniature token torii) and excluded from torii ATTRIBUTION so a wayside shed can never absorb a temple's gates. This rule superseded and retired `torii_full_avenue_is_seven` (which sanctioned {1,2,7}) the same day it was written.
- **A WELL stands BESIDE a shrine, never ON its hall or UNDER its torii arch** (`wells_clear_of_shrine_and_torii`). A well close to a shrine is REQUIRED (above), but its disc must not overlap the hall footprint or the torii arch's box (`x +/-19, y -10..+18`) - a wellhead painted on the hall or in the gateway reads wrong. The fix is ORDER: place `s.shrine_hall(..., torii=[...])` **BEFORE** `s.place_wells(...)` / `s.shrine_well(...)`, so the hall + torii block-outs already exist and the wells (both the scattered village wells and the shrine's own) are laid clear of them. (This caught Ueda, where `place_wells` ran before the shrine and scattered a wellhead under the torii.) Watch the knock-on: `place_wells`'s fallback pass seats an underserved house's well at `~0.6*near` px, so keep `near` modest (~150, not 210) or that fallback can land in open ground and trip `wells_among_dwellings`.
- **A shrine AND its TORII arch NESTLE in a CLEARING within the sacred grove - never UNDER the trees** (`shrine_clear_of_grove_trees`, `torii_clear_of_grove_trees`). The village fengshui/water-mouth grove often surrounds the shrine (the grove IS the shrine's sacred wood), but the hall and its arch must sit in a cleared opening, not painted over tree canopy (which reads as a building lost in the wood). Mechanism: `village_grove` skips any tree clump within an occupied feature's keep-out (houses, yards, gardens, byres, kura, wells at the ordinary `0.35*clump` reach; **religious halls, shrines, and torii at a LARGER `0.90*clump`** so a full clearing opens around the sacred features) - **provided the shrine + torii are placed BEFORE the grove**. So call `s.shrine_hall(..., torii=[...])` FIRST, then the `village_grove(...)` calls. **Canopy, not nominal clump:** the recorded clump `r` is the nominal footprint, but the DRAWN crowns overhang it, so the visible canopy reaches ~1.7x `r`; both checks use that CANOPY radius (a circle-rect test against the hall footprint and against the torii arch's `x +/-19, y -10..+18` box) so they match what the eye sees. (This caught Ueda's shrine + torii buried under the water-mouth grove: the old occ-skip used `0.35*clump` and the checks used the nominal `r`, so canopy that overhung by ~8px slipped through both. A well record carries a radius, not w/h, so it keeps its own occ branch.)
- **DRAFT-ANIMAL BYRES** (`s.draft_byres(fraction, gap)`; recorded `M['byres']`, a first-class overlap struct). Wet-rice plowing/puddling turns on an ox or water buffalo, but a buffalo was a costly asset that poorer households SHARED or hired - so a village keeps only a MINORITY of byres (~one per 4-5 households, `fraction~0.2`), shared open-fronted sheds standing in the COURTYARDS among the homesteads, NOT one per farm. HOUSE-DRIVEN placement: for the wealthier homesteads (buffalo owners) in turn, spiral out from the house to the nearest clear gap just past its reserved footprint (fits-checked off every other footprint / lane / block / crop, kept `gap` px apart), skipping any homestead boxed in - a grid scatter like the wells finds almost nothing because the nucleated homestead bboxes pack the cluster. Call AFTER `farmsteads()` + `place_wells` and BEFORE the grove (which then skips the byres). The glyph is a small plank-roofed shed with a dark stall mouth, distinct from the solid gray *kura* and the dwellings. **Sizing (1px = 2ft at village scale):** the shed footprint is ~15.5x10.5px = ~31x21ft = **~16 m^2**, right for a single-bay lean-to stalling 1-2 draft animals (an ox/buffalo needs ~6-8 m^2 of stall plus fodder/passage room); it must NOT read as a European multi-stall barn (there are none - see the draft-animals-live-in-the-house rule above), so keep it small.
- **PLANK BRIDGES - two kinds.** (a) A **carried-way crossing** (`s.bridges()`; `roads_bridge_water`): where a road, town street, or village LANE crosses a watercourse (stream, channel, field-ditch, moat) it must be carried over on a railed timber deck oriented ALONG the way; `bridges()` auto-spans every such crossing, on the TOP layer, and the check fails on any unbridged one. (b) **Standalone ditch FOOTBRIDGES** (`s.channel_footbridges(spacing, min_len)`; `long_ditches_have_a_footbridge`, opt-in via `meta.field_footbridges`): the planks field-workers use to cross an irrigation ditch while walking the paddy BUNDS - **NOT tied to any lane** (people reach them along the bunds, so NO path leads to them). Any ditch stretch longer than `min_len` gets a plank about MIDWAY; a long stretch gets one roughly every `spacing` px; each crosses PERPENDICULAR to the ditch. **Deck size (1px=2ft): a *dobashi* footplank is a small single-file crossing, so `plank_w=2.0` (~4ft wide) and the deck spans only the ditch width + a SHORT abutment (`span = w + PLANK_ABUTMENT`, +6px total - GM 2026-07-22: was 2.5 wide and +15, both too large; a footplank over an ~8ft ditch is short, not a long jetty).** It is kept both NARROWER and SHORTER than a cart lane (~5-6px): the wider `bridges()` carried-way deck matches the lane it carries (a road bridge is road-width), a footplank is not, so don't let it read as a road bridge. Because each ditch is a separate manifest entry, the northern trunk (several segments) gets several planks, each branch between two paddy strips gets one, the village-edge channel gets one (Hoshigaoka adds a second on its heavily-trodden northern stretch). **A footplank must reach USEFUL ground on BOTH banks** (`footbridges_reach_useful_ground`; GM 2026-07-22, Hikari no Sato): a standalone plank exists so field-workers can cross to the FIELD, so both banks must land on cultivated ground (wet paddy or dry crop), the village (a dwelling within `PLANK_VILLAGE_REACH`), or a walked dike - never reed marsh, scrub commons, or off-map. The placement slides each plank to a useful, house-clear spot and DROPS it if none is near, so a drain/toe stretch running along the field's OUTER edge (marsh or scrub on the far side) carries no plank; `long_ditches_have_a_footbridge` correspondingly EXEMPTS such a MARGIN ditch (`_ditch_plankable` - nothing to cross TO needs no crossing). *Why it matters:* the useless-plank defect was widespread, not a one-off - the water-first maps' drainage toes AND the diagonal edge-drains along every field's outer boundary all carried planks stepping straight into the swamp or scrub; the check + placement rule cleared them pool-wide (Hikari 13->11, honda/kikuta/akagahara/ikegami/moritono/ueda each lost their toe/edge planks) while keeping every field-to-field, dry-to-wet, and village-to-field crossing. Placement and the check read the SAME cultivation source (the manifest `fields` outlines + `dry_plots`, NOT the blocking-only `field_polys`) so they can never disagree. **A lane must NOT run through the flooded paddy** - the village-to-field spur STOPS at the paddy edge; people cross into the fields on foot along the bunds. Call `channel_footbridges()` AFTER the ditches are placed. **A plank must never sit ON a farmhouse** (`bridges_clear_of_houses`): a bridge is overlap-exempt in general (it deliberately sits on the water it spans) but a rotated-rect SAT of its deck against every house must be clear - so `channel_footbridges` SLIDES each plank along its own ditch (a few arc-length offsets each side of the midpoint) until its deck clears every house, keeping it ON the channel while dodging a home near the village edge.
- **Field-adjacency is TUNABLE by settlement form** (`meta.nucleated`). DISPERSED (default): every farmhouse fronts its own fields, so each must be within ~165px of a field (`all_houses_field_adjacent`). NUCLEATED (`meta(nucleated=True)`): the houses cluster and the fields radiate from the cluster edge, so interior houses are legitimately a cluster-span back - per-house adjacency is wrong. Instead the whole CLUSTER must ABUT its fields (`cluster_abuts_fields`): the nearest house is field-adjacent AND no house is farther than the cluster's own diameter past that edge. Set `nucleated` to pick the invariant.
  - **...and on a dispersed map the field OUTLINE must BE the planting** (`field_outline_matches_planting`, GM 2026-07: *"a single line of farmhouses that stretches much further south than the rice paddies themselves do"* / *"there are still 3 farmhouses south of the paddies"*). A field carries two extents: `outline`/`bbox` is the smoothed ENVELOPE the water net claims, `vis_bbox` is the extent of the plots actually DRAWN. They diverge when a gen declares more field than the comb can fill - `build_comb`'s plots stop where the terrain/drain stops them whatever `field_fall` asks for, and the surplus becomes a **PHANTOM TAIL**: invisible on the rendered map, but fully real to every distance test. Because the adjacency above measures to the OUTLINE, a farmstead hugging that tail reads as "field-adjacent" while standing well out past the last rice. **Akagahara** shipped a 181px tail (`field_fall=1440` against plots that ended ~180px higher), which is precisely how it grew a line of farms hanging south of its paddy - and `all_houses_field_adjacent` PASSED the whole time, because both the gen's placement filter and the gate were measuring the same phantom. The fix was to size `field_fall` to what the comb actually fills (1260), not to nudge the farms. **Scoped to DISPERSED maps**, where the envelope is load-bearing for placement; a NUCLEATED cluster is seeded as a unit and never rides the envelope, so a tail there is inert (**Hoshigaoka** and **Kikuta** both carry ~210px tails harmlessly, and reshaping their GM-tuned fields to satisfy a check that protects nothing would be churn). Tolerance 60px allows the honest rounding of a smoothed rim over irregular plots while staying well under the ~165px band it protects. **The general lesson**: when a check measures distance to a derived outline, something must pin that outline to what is actually drawn - otherwise the check is only as honest as its geometry, and a silently-generous envelope makes a green gate meaningless. Teeth: `test_checks.py::test_field_outline_matches_planting_fires_on_a_phantom_tail`, which asserts BOTH that the new check fires AND that `all_houses_field_adjacent` stays blind on the same manifest.
- **Tax-free (temple/monk glebe) plots are OPTIONAL, not required** (`taxfree_plots_in_range`). Denoting them is a choice - the check only validates the count (~2-3) when a map actually draws some or `meta(taxfree_expected=True)`; a village that does not mark them at all is fine.
- **Every farmhouse-bearing map needs a HARVEST-PROCESSING layer** (`harvest_yards_present`, `harvest_yards_smaller_than_farmhouse`, `harvest_yards_on_sunny_side`, `harvest_yards_clear_of_paddies`, `harvest_yards_clear_of_structures`, for `town` / `village` / `hamlet` AND `city`). A rice settlement does not just grow the crop - it threshes and dries it, and that working landscape is as characteristic as the paddies. Historically Japan processed rice at the **farmstead**, not on a central communal floor: drying happened on *hazakake* racks erected in the fields, and threshing/hulling/winnowing on each household's own packed-earth work yard (the *niwa* / *kadoniwa*). So the model is **per-farmstead, not communal**, and the work yard was **UNIVERSAL** - every farming household processed its own rice, so **every farmhouse gets a yard** (a firm 100%). The yard is **independent** of the ~30% that carry a shed (a farmhouse may have neither, either, or both - the shed/storehouse, by contrast, was NOT universal: a fireproof *kura* was a wealth marker and a simple *naya* was common but not on every plot, so it stays a minority). The yard is a small earthen apron with a straw mat + a little drying rack. **Architecture (important): farmstead drawing is DEFERRED.** `try_place` / `headman` reserve + record a farmhouse but do NOT draw it; the gen then calls **`s.farmsteads()` LAST** (after every other feature) which, for each farmhouse, finds a yard spot, NUDGES the house a little if needed (with every obstacle now known), draws the yard then the house over it, and **drops** any farmhouse that truly cannot host a yard anywhere nearby. This keeps base placement identical to a yard-free map (so population/plurality/household counts are unaffected) while guaranteeing the yard. Wells go AFTER `farmsteads()` so they sit among the final houses; `place_wells` has a coverage pass that guarantees no dwelling is left in a well-gap. Five rules: (1) **present (100%)** - EVERY farmhouse has a yard (`harvest_yards_present`: no house lacks one, matched by the yard's `of` = parent center). Because farmsteads drops the rare un-yardable house, ring counts are set a little generously so enough survive (e.g. plurality/household floors still hold). (2) **smaller than its farmhouse** (`harvest_yards_smaller_than_farmhouse`) - the niwa is a small dry apron, not a second dwelling; it scales with `bscale` so it stays smaller even on a compressed city map. (3) **on the sunny SOUTH/front side** (`harvest_yards_on_sunny_side`) - the yard is the *maeniwa*, the south-facing front work yard: rice must dry in the SUN and minka face south (`houses_face_south`), so the yard sits on the house's south/front side, NEVER the shady north back. (+y is south.) This follows the *sun*, not the field - so when the paddy is to the south the yard falls between house and field, but a northern paddy does NOT pull the yard onto the shady side. (4) **clear of the paddies** (`harvest_yards_clear_of_paddies`) - a DRY floor, footprint out of every flooded field. (5) **clear of every OTHER structure** (`harvest_yards_clear_of_structures`) - the yard abuts only its OWN farmhouse, never another building (placed before OR after it - which is why farmsteads runs last, when all obstacles are known). Applies to the **city** too (its in-wall agricultural district + the outside farm rings); only a map with no farmhouses at all is exempt.
- **Every settlement above a hamlet buries its DEAD - a full funerary geography.** Rokugan always **cremates**, then inters the bones, so a graveyard is a compact field of stone markers, not a body-burial sprawl. Four kinds of site, each with its own setting logic:
  - **Temple graveyards** (`s.cemetery(cx, cy, w, h, label=...)` - rows of *sotoba* markers + a couple of taller memorial stupas). The state merged Shinsei (the Buddhist strand) and Fortune/Shugendo worship, so **ANY temple may host a graveyard** - a temple opts out with `s.shrine_hall(..., graveyard=False)` for a new or special-purpose hall (Tango's Temple of Bishamon, founded in a former samurai estate, keeps none). A graveyard is a parish ground, so it **sits in a temple precinct** (`cemetery_in_temple_precinct`, within ~230px of a `monastery`/`temple`; at city scale only an *intramural* graveyard must - an extramural common ground is exempt). **A village SHRINE hosts its graveyard too - the churchyard rule** (`village_graveyard_by_shrine`). Real-world Shinto shuns death-*kegare*, but **L7R's country shrines are officially Shinseist** (the Buddhist-analog order) even though they house Fortune deities, and their resident **Brother of Shinsei performs the funerary rites** - so the shrine *is* the death-handling institution (the *danka*/*bodaiji* logic), and its graveyard is its churchyard, sitting IN the precinct (within ~250px), NOT held away. So the village graveyard goes BY the shrine - EXCEPT a **hilltop** shrine (`M["hill"]`), which is exempt (graves do not climb the sacred hill; a prominent hill-shrine is not the humble earth-god monk's funerary base). Only the sacred **hall + torii themselves** stay clear of burials (`cemetery_clear_of_shrine` now means "graves fill the yard AROUND them, never ON them" - it fires on a grave/mausoleum overlapping the hall or arch, not on mere proximity). This unifies burial across scales: graves by the monk-run building everywhere (shrine at village, monastery/temple at town/city). **Size the burial grounds to the population they serve** (the core "roughly to scale" principle): a centuries-old settlement's MAIN common ground should read as a substantial, monastery-scale field, not a token patch - and a **town has no ossuary** (city-only) to soak up the poor, so its common ground carries proportionally MORE and should be drawn larger (Hirameki's ~1,200-soul town has a 120x88 extramural common ground that dwarfs its 88x62 intramural parish plot). The intramural parish plot beside a temple is naturally smaller (one parish's families); the extramural common ground is the big one.
  - **Shape of the common ground: ORGANIC, Japan-style - a ruled rectangle is the deliberate exception** (`s.cemetery` `organic` derives from `parish`; GM 2026-07-23, researched + source-verified). The GM caught the city maps drawing the common burial ground as a perfect rectangle and asked whether that was historically accurate. *What the research found - the two reference cultures split.* **Japan** (the organic pole): commoner burial grounds were unplotted and terrain-following everywhere - Kyoto's great burial fields (Toribeno, Adashino, Rendaino) were open hillside/riverbank grounds shaped purely by terrain; a village kept an unsurveyed *sanmai* on waste land at its edge; Edo-period urban burial fragmented into many small temple graveyards packed incrementally (Osaka's excavated "seven graveyards" show crowded overlapping pits, not plots). Premodern Japan offers essentially NO surveyed rectangular commoner cemetery. **China** (the split case): ordinary family graves were scattered organically over unfarmable hillsides by feng shui - no communal commoner cemetery at all - BUT the institutional "common burial ground" for the poor and unclaimed dead genuinely WAS a surveyed rectangle: the Song state pauper cemeteries (*louzeyuan* 漏泽园, empire-wide by edict from 1104, continued as Ming *yizhong* 义冢 charity graveyards) were walled compounds on high barren ground with plots in ordered rows, numbered against the Thousand Character Classic, a drainage ditch every three rows, and a resident caretaker monk. *The decision (GM):* Rokugan follows the **Japanese mode** for its common grounds - like the cremate-then-inter rite, a deliberate exception to China-first - so every NON-parish common burial ground draws as an irregular terrain-hugging earthen plot (`parish=False` -> `organic` defaults True; the recorded bbox and no-build block stay the w x h rectangle, so placement/clearance checks are untouched). A specific city MAY override with `organic=False` to draw a *louzeyuan*-style plotted ground - historically defensible and a real variety axis, but it should be a documented per-map choice, not the default. The cramped *danka* parish plots inside temple precincts stay ruled rectangles (`parish=True` default) - a managed plot inside a walled precinct legitimately squares off.
  - **Clan mausoleum** (`s.mausoleum(cx, cy, w, h, label=..., gate_dir=..., label_below=...)` - a walled crypt precinct with a stone hall + memorial stupas). The ruling clan's ancestral crypts, **inside the walls by the samurai/government quarter** (`city_has_mausoleum` - a prestige monument near the seat of power; ancestor veneration is central to samurai identity). City only. When a wall of such a walled compound **abuts a neighborhood (ward) fence**, the compound *yields* that wall to the fence: `s.mausoleum`/`s.manor` re-stamp the ward fence over the coincident wall so the **fence renders ON TOP and IS that side of the precinct** (the compound's own wall runs underneath) - no doubled, clashing parallel walls. The yielded sides are recorded in `ward_walls`, and `walled_structure_yields_to_ward_wall` gates it: any axis-aligned mausoleum/manor wall inside the city that runs along a ward fence must be recorded as yielded (in Tango the samurai-ward fence IS the mausoleum's north wall).
  - **Cremation ground** (`s.cremation_ground(cx, cy)` - a scorched clearing with a stone pyre platform, a wisp of smoke, and the officiants' shelter). Smoke, fire, and pollution put it **OUTSIDE the walls** (`city_has_cremation_ground`; `town_has_cremation_ground` wants one at a town's edge, clear of the dwellings). It **adjoins an EXTERNAL (outside-the-walls) burial ground** (`cremation_ground_by_external_cemetery`, edge gap <= ~70px): the body is burned and its cremated bones interred next door, so the crematory and the extramural common ground form one funerary complex (an in-wall graveyard does NOT satisfy this - the crematory's neighbor must itself be extramural). And it **stays set back from the main road** (`cremation_ground_set_back_from_main_road`, >= ~130px from `M["road"]`): the pyre is marginal, polluting land reached by a minor funeral path, not high-street frontage. Beyond that floor, it must not sit **between its temple and the road** (`cremation_ground_not_between_temple_and_road`): if a monastery/temple is nearby (within ~400px), the crematory must be at least as far from the road as that temple is (less a ~40px tolerance for "beside, a little away"), so worshippers and funeral-goers don't walk past the pyre to reach the hall - put it BEHIND or beside the temple, never on its road-side approach. (Note the danka split: a temple's own *graveyard* sits beside the temple wherever it is - like a Christian churchyard, and may sit road-side by the temple - but the *cremation ground* is the marginal exception kept apart from the road and off the temple's ceremonial approach; minor town streets don't trigger either rule, only the trunk road.) Monk-run with burakumin assistants - a religious order stands outside the caste system, so handling the dead does not pollute its caste.
  - **Pauper ossuary** (`s.ossuary(cx, cy)` - a low earthen mound with one weathered stupa). The communal bones of the poor and the *muenbotoke* (unconnected dead), **outside the walls by the cremation ground** (`city_has_ossuary`).
- **The scale schedule** (centuries-old settlements): a **CITY** shows **2-4 graveyards** (`city_graveyard_count`), **every non-exempt temple has one in its precinct** (`city_temples_have_graveyards`), plus the mausoleum (inside) and the cremation ground + ossuary (outside) - an extramural funerary complex beyond a gate. A **TOWN** has 1-2 temple graveyards + a cremation ground at the edge. A **VILLAGE** has one burial ground clear of its shrine. A **HAMLET is exempt** (its dead go to the village district's ground, like it has no headman or shrine).
- **Any WALLED settlement (town or city) keeps a graveyard inside AND outside the walls** (`walled_graveyards_inside_and_outside`), **and the exterior common ground is noticeably larger than the cramped intramural one** (`walled_exterior_cemetery_larger`, outside area >= 1.3x the largest inside - there is room beyond the walls, while the intramural temple plots are hemmed in). So a walled town has at least two graveyards (one of each); an unwalled town's graveyards are all parish grounds (no exterior-common-ground exemption). Intramural temple plots are deliberately **small** (Tango's are 46x34 / 56x40, cramped beside their halls), the extramural common ground **large** (104x74).
- **Every solid map feature is a first-class structure for overlap purposes, and a NEW feature must not overlap anything unless the overlap is explicitly declared OK.** This is the governing principle (each new feature historically shipped overlapping streams, channels, fields, walls...), and it is *enforced*, not just documented: `check_village.py` carries a classification registry (`_OVERLAP_STRUCTS` / `_OVERLAP_TARGETS` / `_OVERLAP_LINEAR` / `_OVERLAP_EXEMPT`) and the **`every_feature_classified_for_overlap`** guard, which FAILS when a generator emits a footprint feature whose manifest key is in none of those sets - so a new feature can never silently skip the overlap rules. The DEFAULT is must-not-overlap: a solid feature (houses, civic/urban buildings, the **funerary structures**, wayside shrines, ministries) joins the `structs` set and is automatically caught by `no_structure_overlaps` and every `no_structure_on_*` clearance (building, **wall**, **moat**, **road/street/alley**, **stream**, **channel**, the **pond**, religious hall, gate furniture, torii, and the **ring road** via `ring_road_kept_clear`); every solid feature is normalized to a w/h rect for the test. Overlaps are **opt-in**: a feature that is *meant* to overlap is named in `_OVERLAP_EXEMPT` with its reason - a **label** (text overlay), a **bridge** over water/road, a **guard tower** ON the wall, an **inspection post** at the gate, a **storehouse** annex abutting its shop, a **threshing yard** annex abutting its farmhouse, a **well-head** dropped into a courtyard gap. (`shrines` duplicates the primary religious halls, so it rides with `religious` as a target.) Place solid features AFTER the dwellings (they block placement) in clear pockets; a placement scan must mirror **all** the clearances (wall stroke, moat, ring road, streets, water, fields, torii, gate furniture, and existing structures' *rotated* footprints), and keep extramural funerary sites **outside the wall but inside the cropped view** (Tango clusters its common burial ground + cremation ground + ossuary just west of the wall).
- **Burial grounds sit a SET-BACK from open water that SCALES with the waterway's size** (`funerary_set_back_from_water`, helper `water_setback(width)`) - a burial ground by big water floods out, so the bigger the watercourse the further back the dead must lie - but even narrow open water floods graves, so there is a solid **floor (~75px)**: a stream gets the full ~75px, a **moat** (the heaviest watercourse, ~26px wide) ~130px, a river or canal most (capped ~140px). It applies to the **moat, streams, ponds, and rice-paddy field edges** - a flooded paddy is real standing water (rice grows submerged), a genuine flood hazard, so a burial ground keeps a solid **~50px** margin from any field edge (NOT a token creek distance - graves right against a paddy flood out); thin irrigation channels are not open water and don't trigger it. Two refinements: the **CREMATION ground may sit nearer the water** (a fixed modest ~30px, and exempt from the paddy set-back entirely - fire and ritual want water access, and a fire site is not flood-sensitive like graves), so the graveyard naturally lands *beyond* the cremation ground (Tango's common burial ground sits well back, on the far side of the cremation ground from the moat); and an **INSIDE-wall ground is exempt from the moat term** (the moat is outside the wall, the rampart shields it - streams/ponds still apply on either side). The **walled mausoleum is exempt** entirely (a crypt compound, not a flood-sensitive open plot).
- **A graveyard can be marked NON-parish** (`s.cemetery(..., parish=False)`) - a village-style burial ground not attached to a temple, exempt from the temple-precinct rule. Used for a one-off like **Tango's in-wall agricultural-district burial ground** (a graveyard serving the farm quarter, away from the temples - a Tango-specific extra, not a general rule). bunkotsu (divided remains - a portion at a great head-temple, the rest in the home village) is real but **not drawn** - it isn't visible in this view.
- **A gate market (*guan-xiang*) sits outside EVERY MAIN-ROAD gate** (`city_has_gate_market`, >= 6 extramural shops within ~520px of each gate in `M["gates"]`; floor raised from 3, GM 2026-07-24 - the researched *guan-xiang* ran **10-40 structures per trafficked gate**, so the drawn belt is a SLICE like the samurai estates and the farmland: string the shops along the approach road and let the outermost run off the frame, the truncation itself saying "the suburb continues") - the same extramural *guan-xiang* commerce as a town's, here beyond the moat, at every main gate rather than just one (GM decision + research 2026-07-22, `flophouse-research.md`). **WHY at every main-road gate:** the *guan-xiang* is a road-driven extramural suburb that formed along the approach road at each *trafficked* gate - historically Beijing's gates all carried one, varying in scale (大关厢 vs. small). A city's MAIN gates each sit on a main/through road (the Imperial road or the river route), so **each earns a market; the scale may differ** - Tango's south gate opens onto the wider southern approach and carries the bigger market, its north gate a smaller stall row; Nagahara's river gate has the whole WHARF suburb, its north (highway) gate a small cluster. Mirrors `city_flophouse_outside_each_gate`. **A purely military SALLY gate is exempt** (traffic-free - it opens onto empty field for siege sorties, with no road, market, flophouse, or caravan cluster): the current pool cities have none, and `M["gates"]` holds only the main road/river gates, so "every gate in `gates`" already means "every main-road gate." Were a sally-gate knob added, its gates would live in their own structure and the market/flophouse/caravan checks (which iterate `gates`) would skip them automatically.
- **Fire defense ports up too, at city scale.** A city's quarters each need a **fire-watch tower** (`s.fire_tower(...)`, `city_has_fire_towers` >= 2; `fire_tower_in_commoner_quarter` keeps each in a commoner quarter, not the samurai ward; `fire_towers_dispersed` keeps any two towers at least one watch radius apart, and `fire_tower_amid_its_district` makes each tower stand amid the rooftop district it is nearest-tower for - so the towers actually spread across the commoner quarters instead of bunching in one quadrant). Because the commoner warren packs wall-to-wall, a tower stands where it actually has SIGHTLINES: a cleared block or an open seam between building clusters. Because the towers annotate existing gaps, place them **LAST, after the packs and `farmsteads()`**. `meta(fire_tower=False)` to suppress. See the "Fire towers" grounding below.
- **A BELL-AND-DRUM TOWER stands at the main street crossing of every WALLED seat** (`s.drum_tower(x, y)`, `walled_settlement_has_drum_tower`, town + city scope) - the timekeeping/curfew institution: morning bell, evening drum, the dusk gate-closing, the five night watches. Exactly one combined tower (the paired towers are capital grammar), on a corner of the central crossing within ~80px of two non-parallel road/street segments, ~70 ft at city tier / ~60 ft at town tier, heavier-built than the skeletal fire towers (fire watch is a separate institution and does not satisfy this). An unwalled town is exempt - its time signal is the monastery's bell, implied. Full research record under "The bell-and-drum tower" in Historical grounding below.
- **Extensive farmland lies OUTSIDE the walls** (`city_has_outside_farmland`, >= 1 field running off the map edge - the rest implied off-map). The in-city farmers are zero, so these fields are worked from the surrounding villages; draw them mostly running off the edge rather than ringing them with city farmhouses.
- **By default a city has NO farms inside the walls** (`city_no_inwall_farms`). Tango is *uncharacteristic* in having an **agricultural district** (its NW quarter): in-wall water sources plus dimensions that made it save ~nothing to wall the farms out. Opt in with `meta(agricultural_district=True)`; that quarter also holds the city's in-wall burakumin. **Most cities will NOT set this.** When a city DOES farm inside its walls, those fields are **real farmland**. Unlike a surrounding field - mostly off the cropped map, so only a sparse FLOOR is enforceable on its shown sliver - an in-wall field sits **entirely in view**, so its **whole perimeter must read as worked**: ring it **densely all the way round**, not a sparse few on one side that leaves long bare edges. `city_interior_fields_farmhouse_density` holds in-wall fields to a much higher floor than the extramural `outside_fields_farmhouse_density` - **16 houses per 1000px of edge** (the dense end of village ringing) vs the outside floor of 7. Ring with a tight inner row plus one or two denser outer bands at finer spacing (Tango lands ~24-37/1000px). **The in-wall paddy is a comb too, and the pocket geometry drives its design:** the ring road leaves an elliptical crescent that narrows toward the high corner, and `build_comb`'s fan is CHIRAL (canal A swings clockwise of the fall at -42 deg, the wide canal-B flank counterclockwise at +58 deg, drifting ~1.6x the fall) - the default hand throws the wide flank into the narrowing crescent. Real combs came in both hands, so the gen computes the comb in a y-MIRRORED frame and maps it back (`comb_field(..., mirror_ym=...)` in `tango.gen.py`): sluice and fall direction mirror in, every polygon/channel/bead mirrors out, furrow angles negate. The pond sits at the quarter's HIGH corner (water enters the city from the high north, like the moat feeder - a tameike is embanked on high ground) and the fan fills the crescent downhill of it. Sweep seeds/falls against the ACTUAL ring-road polyline (its chords cut inside the ideal ellipse) - at Tango's scale only ~1 in 8 seed/fall combinations fits the pocket. The district's SECOND block is a `kind="vegetable"` garden tract on the road flank (the comb's 100-deg fan + fixed 90px head-race simply do not fit twice in a ~220px-deep crescent, and the tract is the documented urban form anyway). Two wrinkles: (1) placement uses a single seeded RNG, so adding ring calls early in the gen shifts every later draw; if your samurai/laborer packs are tuned near a threshold, **append the extra interior-field rings at the END of the gen** so they perturb nothing upstream. (2) These in-wall farmhouses do **NOT** count toward the city population (city farmers are never in the ~3,000 - see the population rule above), so ring as densely as the field wants without watching the figure.
- **City commoner housing goes down as CONTIGUOUS TERRACES - the row-packing doctrine** (`s.rowpack(bbox, kinds)`; gated by `city_row_housing_touches` >= 55% of row-class dwellings touching a neighbor, and `city_row_housing_gap` median nearest-neighbor edge gap <= 2px). Lay each quarter's laborer/servant/burakumin/merchant_house stock with `rowpack`, NOT `pack`: E-W rows of touching units (a 0.4px hairline seam keeps the SAT overlap gate honest), the real ~3-6 ft eave gap between rows, an idobata court every 2 rows, and the caller's roji/alleys (draw them FIRST) fronted tightly while real streets keep a frontage band for the shops. Wells go down BEFORE the rows so the terraces break into courts around them. The SAMURAI quarter is the exception - bushi kept detached compounds with yards, so it stays `pack` (its scatter is the deliberate contrast that makes the terraces read). See "Historical grounding" below for the why.
- **Walled-compound gates, walls, and the funerary features are TO SCALE** (GM 2026-07-19; gates `compound_gates_to_scale`, `cremation_ground_to_scale`, `ossuary_to_scale`, `burial_grounds_sized_to_population`). The walled compounds (manors/estates, the governor's yamen, merchant estates, the mausoleum) draw walls + gate + a **deliberately blank court** - the interior is the subject of its own Mode A diagram when the PCs visit - so the wall and gate ARE the feature and must be honest. *Anchors (researched 2026-07-19, full memo below):* a samurai residence gate (nagayamon/yakuimon) opens ~9-12 real ft, a grand yamen gatehouse ~18-24 ft (the old fixed +-34px gap drew a 204 ft opening at city scale - most of a wall missing); walls (dobei/tsuijibei) ~1.5-2 ft thick, drawn true-width-or-floored at 2px; gate posts ~2 ft squares floored ~3px. Funerary: a sanmai cremation ground's cleared core is 30-80 ft (village/town) to ~80-160 ft (city) - even the Yoyogi crematory serving metropolitan Edo was ~900 tsubo (~180 ft square) - with a ~15x10 ft pyre platform; a muenzuka pauper bone mound is 10-30 ft (Kyoto's monumental Mimizuka ~50 ft base; cremated bone takes almost no volume - Kozukappara's 100k+ dead never made a great mound), drawn ~22 ft mid-band with a 4.5px visibility floor (tightened 2026-07-21: the earlier ~40 ft glyph carried a 9px floor that rendered 54 real ft at city scale - the legibility-size license is retired, and the `ossuary_to_scale` band is now [8, 32] ft); burial grounds size to the population served at ~10-20 sq ft per packed urn-grave with ~1 generation of active plots before reuse (village ~0.15-0.30 ac for the WHOLE ~800-person district it buries - see 'District catchment' below; town ~0.25-0.75, city ~0.75-2 split across yards; Chinese full-body burial runs ~4-6x - Rokugan follows the Japanese cremate-then-inter mode), and the ladder stays MONOTONE with population served - the old village glyphs drew 0.5-0.65 ac, dwarfing the towns'. Sources: Edo hatamoto yashiki schedules, Fukui sanmai survey, Shinpen Musashi Fudoki-ko (Yoyogi), Tanigawa's Edo cemetery excavations (JJRS 1992), Chinese Deathscape (yizhong).
  - **District catchment - the village ground buries the WHOLE ~800-person district, and hamlets bury nowhere visible (GM asked 2026-07-23; researched + source-verified).** The presence rules always said it (`settlement_has_cemetery`: "a hamlet's dead go to the village district's burial ground, just as it has no shrine or headman") but the sizing was anchored to the central village's own ~350 (the 2026-07-19 resize comments read "a ~350-person village ground") - an internal contradiction the GM caught. *What the research found:* Edo Japan actually buried PER-SETTLEMENT - hamlet burial patches (*shuraku bochi*, today's grandfathered *minashi bochi*) at the fringe of even 12-15-household hamlets were ubiquitous - while the RITUAL center was central (*danka* temple registration, funerals, and stone markers at the main village's temple; the *ryobosei* two-grave regions formalized the split: the corpse in the local *ume-baka*, the venerated stone at the center). Ming/Qing China is the deliberate contrast: scattered fengshui-sited family graves through the farmland (Buck's 1929-33 farm survey: ~2% of ALL farm area under graves), communal grounds only as pauper charity (*yizhong*) - so the discrete communal ground we draw is the Japanese surface convention, correctly per the China-geography/Japan-surface split. TWO things make the one-central-ground convention MORE defensible in Rokugan than in historical Japan: (1) the cremate-then-inter canon - an urn is carried to the district ground in a way a corpse-procession is not; (2) a hamlet's own burial patch is TINY (~750-2,450 sq ft full-body, less for urns - a ~15-20px blob at 2 ft/px), legitimately below map resolution, so hamlets drawing nothing stays honest even where local patches exist in-fiction. *The decision:* the drawn village ground is the marked, ritually active DISTRICT ground, sized to the district: ~800 inhabitants x ~25-30 deaths/1,000/yr x ~30-yr plot reuse = ~600-720 active urn plots x 10-20 sq ft = **~0.15-0.30 acre** (cross-checked against the excavated Umeda-haka commoner ground, ~15-17 sq ft per body including paths). The four village grounds were resized 2026-07-23 from ~0.14 ac (the ~350 anchor) to ~0.24-0.26 ac, and `BURIAL_AC_BAND["village"]` re-anchored from [0.04, 0.30] to **[0.12, 0.38]** (the district band + glyph-rounding slack both ways), so a village-only-sized ground now FAILS `burial_grounds_sized_to_population`. Monotone with population served survives: the district's ~800 still sits below a town's ~1,200, and 0.15-0.30 nests under the town's 0.25-0.75.
- **Samurai country estates: the drawn belt is a SLICE, and the count is free** (GM ruling 2026-07-19). budgets.md supports ~560 estate samurai domain-wide (~110 households) - roughly 8-15 in a provincial city's orbit - but the map never claims a census: draw **at least 2** (to show there are several), **at the map edge with some cut by the frame** - exactly like the farm fields the frame cuts, the truncation says "this continues beyond the map." Any count >=2 is fine; `city_estates_multiple_shown` + `city_estates_toward_capital` gate the doctrine. Estate-dwellers are tallied in the surrounding village districts per budgets.md, not the city's 3,000.
- **A merchant estate's wall stands on dry, private ground - off the streets** (GM doctrine 2026-07-19; gates `merchant_estate_wall_clear_of_water` + `merchant_estate_wall_clear_of_fire_towers` + `merchant_estate_wall_clear_of_streets`, town+city scope). The walled compound of a very-rich urban merchant must not run its perimeter through WATER - canal, dock basin, moat, river, pond - or through a FIRE TOWER (nor wall one INSIDE the court: the watch reaches its tower from public ground), or stand IN the cleared band of any STREET, alley, road, or the ring road (a compound wall may LINE a street - that is what a walled compound on a block looks like - but the public way stays open). *The why:* a wall footed in water is undermined, and the canal/dock edge is WORKING waterfront (boats, porters, the towpath that makes the merchant rich) - a private wall may approach the quay but never stand in it; the fire watch is municipal infrastructure needing its own footing, daylight round the braced frame, and watch access - it cannot be embedded in a private compound wall. The whole perimeter is walked, gate gap included (a courtyard gate opening straight onto water or into the tower frame is the same siting error). Placement enforces it too: `s.merchant_estate` slides through a small candidate fan to the nearest clear seat when the requested spot violates (draw water + towers BEFORE the estate), and raises rather than drawing a wall the gate will reject. Both checks landed red-first against the shipped Nagahara (its estate wall clipped the dock basin AND the labeled fire tower - pinned as `pool/regressions/merchant_estate_wall_fires_on_dock_and_tower_nagahara.json`).
- **Doors face OUTWARD; rows stack at most TWO deep** (GM doctrine 2026-07-18; gates `city_house_doors_unblocked` + `city_rows_max_two_deep`, town+city scope). A FARMHOUSE always faces SOUTH - its dooryard garden and threshing ground need the sunlight, so its orientation is canon and it is exempt everywhere. A CITY house has no sun constraint; what it must have is an **unblocked entrance**: the door (drawn on the building's local +h/2 side, so facing derives from `rot` in the manifest) opens onto walkable ground - street, roji, court - never into the back of another house an eave-gap (~3-6 ft) away. The pair rule follows: terrace rows come in **back-to-back pairs, both fronts outward** (`rowpack` places the first row of each pair at rot 180, the second at rot 0; between pairs a walkable roji of ~12 ft, widening to the idobata court), because the middle row of a 3-deep stack is walled on both faces - those households would be trapped. `frontage(rows=2)` flips its rear row 180 (the street row faces the street, the back row faces the back lane - the ura-dana pattern); scattered `pack` houses pick the open cardinal via `s.open_face_rot`. The check boundary is `DOOR_CLEAR_FT = 7` real ft - between the eave band (<= ~6 ft, drainage not entrance) and the walkable band (>= ~10 ft) at every map scale. *Historical grounding:* an ura-nagaya unit had exactly ONE entrance, opening onto the roji its row fronted (Edo tenement rows were laid out around lane access; machiya opened to the street they taxed frontage on); back-to-back pairs sharing a rear wall were the densest honest pattern - three-deep does not occur because the middle row has no lane, and a household with no door to a lane cannot exist.
- **At the declared 3 ft/px city scale the freed ground goes to the agricultural district** (GM density canon): Tango has an AVERAGE provincial-city population with ABOVE-average in-wall space per capita *because of* its agricultural district - rare but not unheard of. So when the contiguous terraces vacate ground the old scatter filled, absorb it with more farmland, NOT more houses (the caste bands pin the dwelling count). In-wall fields east of the Imperial road cannot show a water source (a channel cannot cross the road), so they go down as **`kind="vegetable"` garden tracts** - exempt from `fields_show_water_source`, `field_ringed`, and the in-wall farmstead-ring density (see grounding below).
- **Tango's quarters** (a specific layout, not a universal rule): the road + E-W axis split it into NW (agricultural district + in-wall burakumin + a pond), NE (laborer terraces + garden tracts), SW (merchant district + the temple neighborhood with the Rites ministry), SE (governor's mansion + the other five ministries + the samurai neighborhood, with the samurai estates just outside the SE wall). Other cities arrange their quarters differently; the gate checks the *contents*, not which quarter holds them.

### The validator (`check_village.py`)

The generator emits a manifest the validator asserts against; it must pass before a settlement map is presented. It works for **any** village/hamlet, not just Kikuta: the UNIVERSAL invariants are always checked, while the VILLAGE-SPECIFIC expectations are read from `manifest["meta"]` and from each channel's `frm`/`to` anchors.

- **Universal (always):** no farmhouse overlaps (rotated-rect SAT); nothing on a lane / **irrigation channel** (`no_structure_on_channel`, same footprint test as streams) / **road** (`no_structure_on_road`) / **stream** (`no_structure_on_stream`) / manor / **wall** (`no_structure_on_wall`) / **moat** (`no_structure_on_moat`) / **town street** (`no_structure_on_street`) / **religious hall** (`no_structure_on_religious`) / **gate guard station + tower** (`no_structure_on_gate`) / **torii arch** (`no_structure_on_torii`) - and **every solid feature (the funerary structures, wayside shrines, ministries) is checked by all of these exactly like a building** (see the overlap-classification principle above; `every_feature_classified_for_overlap` fails if a new feature is left unclassified; the per-farmstead **threshing yards** are the exception - an annex abutting their own farmhouse, so overlap-exempt against it, but still kept off the paddies) - the manor, hall, gate structures, and each torii block a rect plus a building-half margin, because an ellipse undershoots their corners; all houses field-adjacent; every (on-map) field ringed; no cultivation on a hill; houses face south; the headman's house is the largest; no two body labels overlap; the per-farmstead threshing yards keep their footprint out of the flooded paddies (`harvest_yards_clear_of_paddies`); each channel is anchored at both ends, winds gently, and is reasonably direct; any torii are clear of the shrine and spread out; fields stay clear of any road or town street, incl. the road running out the gate (`fields_clear_of_road`) and never cross a wall (`fields_clear_of_wall` - abut only); every fully-on-map field shows a water source - a channel feeding it or the field abutting a stream/pond (`fields_show_water_source`); streams never run through fields (`streams_avoid_fields`); roads/streams/large terrain run off the map edge (`edge_features_run_off_map`); the religious building matches the settlement scale (`religious_matches_scale`); roads/streets are a ground layer drawn UNDER anything that legitimately sits on them - a gatehouse or a label (`roads_drawn_under_overlays`); in a town, businesses front the streets (`businesses_front_streets`), street-fronting buildings face the street they line (`buildings_face_street`), and dwellings stay off the main commercial frontage (`housing_off_main_street`).
- **Meta-driven (per settlement):** a village must have a headman / a hamlet must not (`village_has_headman` / `hamlet_has_no_headman`, from `meta.scale`); occupied-house count consistent with `meta.households` (~0.7 houses/household), or a `meta.target_houses` band, else the `meta.scale` default (village 40-80 / hamlet 10-30); tax-free plots 2-3 (villages); fallow fields ring abandoned houses ONLY if `meta.fallow_implies_abandoned`; the two largest common fields differ in orientation ONLY when there are two; shrine-on-summit + torii-on-hill ONLY if `meta.shrine_on_hill`; torii count == `meta.torii_expected`; pond checks ONLY if a pond exists; channel source anchored to pond / off-map edge / stream / field per its declared `frm`; channels run downhill ONLY if `meta.downhill` is declared (`channels_flow_downhill` - source uphill of the field along the slope).
- **Town-scale (`meta.scale=="town"`):** each non-farmer caste's building count falls in its `budgets.md`-derived band (`town_caste_count[merchant|laborer|servant|burakumin|samurai]` - merchant ~24, laborer ~29, servant ~5 standalone, burakumin ~12, samurai 5-10; shops are additional and ungated); farmers are the plurality (`town_farmers_plurality`); a magistrate's walled manor exists (`town_has_magistrate_manor`); at least one field runs off the edge (`town_has_field_off_edge`); a theater stage exists unless `meta(theater_stage=False)` (`town_has_theater_stage`), sited adjacent to a temple/monastery (`theater_stage_by_temple`); the magistrate's manor gate faces the town it administers OR the road it fronts, not a blind default (`manor_gate_faces_town`); the town declares its monasteries via `meta.clan` or `meta.monastery_fortunes` (`town_declares_monasteries`) and has the right count and dedications (`town_monastery_count`, `town_monasteries_dedicated`); a noticeable minority of merchant houses keep an attached storehouse (`town_has_merchant_storehouses`, >= 3 kura); a market-day flophouse exists (`town_has_flophouse`, default 1; `meta(flophouses=N)` for more, `0` to opt out); a rice-transit town declaring `meta(granary=True)` draws a distinct granary (`town_has_granary`). **Walled (`meta.walled`):** a wall + gate exist (`walled_town_has_wall`) and the wall is irregular (`wall_sections_irregular`: >= 5 sections, length CoV >= 0.25); no structure overlaps the rampart (`no_structure_on_wall`); a main street runs inward from the gate (`walled_town_has_main_street`); every inside-the-walls street has buildings along it - no "street to nowhere" (`streets_have_buildings`); the rampart hugs the built area rather than enclosing empty corner space, terrain and a modest gate forecourt excepted (`wall_hugs_the_town`); each monastery's torii avenue fills its approach space - several arches for a long clear run to the street, a single arch for a cramped corner (`monastery_torii_scale_with_space`); a small extramural gate market of a few shophouses sits outside the gate unless `meta(gate_market=False)` (`walled_town_has_gate_market`); the theater stage sits inside the walls unless `meta(theater_stage="outside")` (`theater_stage_inside_wall`); and a WALLED town, unless suppressed, stands a fire-watch tower in its commoner core (`walled_town_has_fire_tower`, `fire_tower_in_commoner_quarter`) - an unwalled town gets none (see "Fire towers").
- **City-scale (`meta.scale=="city"`):** the interior carries the provincial government - the governor's mansion (`city_has_governor_mansion`), the six ministry offices one of which is Rites (`city_has_six_ministries`, `city_has_ministry_of_rites`), and a samurai neighborhood sized to the ~10% samurai cohort with many houses fronting its streets (`city_has_samurai_neighborhood`, `city_samurai_housing_sufficient`, `city_samurai_partly_front_streets`); a merchant district (its housing varied by wealth band - walled estates, large and small houses - and spread out, unlike the dense uniform laborers; the estate courts clear of the wall/moat and of any building, and each estate gate opening onto open ground not into a compound) and laborer neighborhoods are present (`city_has_merchant_district`, `city_merchant_housing_varied`, `city_merchant_housing_spread`, `city_merchant_estates_clear_of_wall_moat`, `city_merchant_estates_clear_of_buildings`, `city_merchant_estate_gate_clear`, `city_has_laborer_neighborhoods`, `city_laborer_housing_varied`); the population is dwellings x5 not total buildings (and its caste MIX - ~40% laborer / 20% servant / 25% merchant / 10% samurai / 5% burakumin - is within +/-30% of budgets.md, servants interleaved not starved), shops front the streets, and poor housing fills the interior (`population_consistent_with_housing`, `city_caste_counts_in_band`, `businesses_front_streets`, `poor_housing_mostly_interior`); a city with an Imperial road running through it (walled or not) lines that road with a commercial ribbon of shops/inns (`city_imperial_road_has_commerce`); extensive farmland runs off the edge outside the walls (`city_has_outside_farmland`); religious buildings are temples (`religious_matches_scale`); the commoner warren is dotted with public wells, each in a block interior off the lanes, enough that no neighborhood lacks water access AND none is over-burdened (~1 per 10-20 households), while the samurai/government quarter has none (its water is private, inside the compounds) (`city_neighborhoods_have_wells`, `city_well_density_sufficient`, `city_wells_in_block_interiors`, `city_samurai_quarter_has_no_public_wells`); and the civic amenities ported from the town tier are present - merchant-house kura, a flophouse, a theater stage (`city_has_merchant_storehouses`, `city_has_flophouse`, `city_has_theater_stage`); fire defense ports up too - >= 2 fire-watch towers over the commoner quarters (`city_has_fire_towers`, `fire_tower_in_commoner_quarter`). **Walled (`meta.walled`):** a closed wall + >= 2 gates (`walled_city_has_wall_and_gates`); a guard house + attached inspection station + guard tower at each gate (the guard house + inspection station rotated square to the wall/ring road, like the towers), plus guard towers spaced around the whole rampart and rotated square to the wall - every tower NUDGED INWARD so only ~8px of its outer face projects past the wall centerline (the horse-face bastion's stride: a tower centered on the wall line would stand its footing in a close-set moat's bed; the gateposts likewise stop ~5px past the wall line on the moat side, and are recorded as `gate_structs` kind="gatepost" so the gate sees them), all gated by `city_wall_furniture_clear_of_moat` (wall towers + gate furniture footprints clear of the moat bed; bridges exempt - they span it by design). **And the ward gates keep their ground against the towers** (`kido_clear_of_wall_towers`): a kido hangs where a lane or the ring road crosses the ward fence - a FIXED crossing - and the fence ends abut the rampart, so the last kido can land against a mural tower's footprint (its guard box reads as a stray "small square building" inside the tower; both classes are overlap-exempt, so no generic pass catches the pair). The TOWER yields: pass the kido spots as `city_wall(..., tower_skip=[(x, y), ...])` - a mural tower whose vertex falls within ~62px **SLIDES a short way along the wall** (growing arcs, both directions, shortest clear slide wins - a full vertex jump left a ~360px bare stretch of rampart, a defensive hole on the attack side; dropped entirely only when boxed in both ways, which the 75-deg spacing check tolerates once), and a GATE tower walks further along the wall until clear. **The kido's own ground must be RESERVED before any pack runs** (`kido_clear_of_buildings`): the gates hold fixed crossings but `s.ward` draws them near the END of the gen, long after the quarters are built - so the gen block_polys each kido spot up front (~17px margin, a `samurai_large` half-diagonal, since block polys test only placement centers; the guard box hangs W of a vertical kido, N of a horizontal one).
