Note the ordering trap both rules solve: `city_wall` and the packs run long before `s.ward`, so neither can see the kido - the gen must declare the spots once, up front, and feed them to both. - plus guard towers spaced for INTERLOCKING flanking fire at a density set by the city's DEFENSE TIER (`meta(wall_defense="siege"|"garrison"|"peaceful")`) - `>= 2` towers cover every curtain point within the tier's arrow range (siege = aimed-lethal 197 ft, garrison = full war-bow 328 ft, peaceful = `>= 1` within 197 ft), the gate barbican and water-gate openings exempt (`city_wall_tower_coverage`; `city_wall_towers_spaced` remains the coarse floor); and a ring road in the wall-clear patrol zone just inside it, kept clear of buildings/civic compounds/fields (only gate guard houses, inspection stations, towers and gated ward fences may sit on it), which the streets meet cleanly (reaching its bed, neither short nor poking past) - as they do the Imperial road (`city_inspection_station_at_each_gate`, `city_gate_has_guardhouse`, `city_gate_furniture_aligned`, `city_wall_towers_spaced`, `city_wall_tower_coverage`, `city_wall_towers_aligned`, `city_has_ring_road`, `ring_road_kept_clear`, `city_streets_meet_through_lanes`); >= 1 burakumin neighborhood inside the walls (`walled_city_has_burakumin_inside`); the samurai/government quarter sealed off the commoner streets by a kido-gated ward fence whose ends meet SOLID wall (no walk-around gap, clear of gate openings) and run UNDER the rampart, with commoner lanes that approach the fence reaching it and ending at a kido gate (`city_samurai_quarter_gated`, `city_samurai_ward_sealed`, `city_ward_fence_meets_wall`, `city_ward_fence_under_wall`, `city_ward_cap_flush_to_wall`, `city_lanes_reach_ward_gates`); 1-3 dispersed walled samurai estates of varying size toward the capital (SE), spread >= 200px apart, not overlapping each other or the wall/moat (`city_samurai_estates_outside`, `city_samurai_estates_dispersed`, `city_samurai_estates_vary_in_size`, `city_estates_toward_capital`, `city_estates_no_overlap`, `city_estates_clear_of_wall_moat`); the governor's mansion is the grandest compound and the ministries cluster around it and front its avenues, each office standing clear of its neighbors (not abutting) (`city_governor_mansion_large`, `city_ministries_cluster_at_government`, `city_ministries_front_a_street`, `city_government_offices_dont_abut`); all temples inside the walls and clear of the wall/moat, with a torii in front of any a street runs up to, and torii drawn OVER the streets they span (`city_temples_inside_walls`, `city_temples_clear_of_wall_moat`, `city_temple_approach_has_torii`, `city_torii_over_streets`); the governor's mansion + ministries clear of the wall/moat (`city_government_clear_of_wall_moat`); the farm fields and the in-wall pond clear of the wall/moat (`city_fields_clear_of_wall_moat`, `city_pond_clear_of_wall_moat`); the streets AND alleys stay inside the wall, clear of the moat, off the buildings, and streets never run through a civic compound (`city_streets_clear_of_wall`, `city_streets_clear_of_moat`, `no_structure_on_street`, `city_civic_clear_of_streets`), are lined with buildings - the larger ones closely lined with roadside frontage (only narrow alleys and the ministry-fronted government avenue excepted) - form one connected network whose beds actually reach the road, and neither near-miss nor leave intersection stubs, and any two lanes (streets/alleys) heading straight at each other with a clear gap connect rather than stop short (`city_streets_have_buildings`, `city_larger_streets_lined`, `city_streets_connected`, `city_streets_no_near_miss`, `city_streets_no_intersection_stub`, `city_lanes_meet_when_aligned`); the wider lane renders over the narrower where they cross and lanes meet as clean crossroads (beds merging, no edge line across a junction), and every lane that runs into a wall - the city rampart or a ward fence - renders UNDER it (showing through only at a gate opening) (`city_lanes_layered_by_width`, `intersections_are_crossroads`, `city_lane_under_wall`, `city_lanes_under_ward_fences`); every neighborhood/zone label sits WITH the cluster it names - entirely on that cluster's side of the wall, among its buildings, not over a foreign field, and every label renders on top of everything so its text is never covered, no label sits on a building it does not name, and no named civic label drifts onto a sibling civic building (`city_labels_placed_with_subject`, `labels_render_on_top`, `labels_clear_of_other_buildings`, `city_civic_label_on_its_own_building`); the in-wall flophouse sits in a humble quarter, not beside the temples/merchants/samurai or burakumin (`city_flophouse_in_humble_quarter`); no deep block of housing is cut off from streets+alleys (`no_isolated_dwelling_cluster`); the wall holds the city with no large empty swath inside (`city_no_large_empty_space`); the Imperial road runs N-S off both edges through the gates (`city_imperial_road_through`); a gate market sits outside EVERY gate (`city_has_gate_market`); a flophouse sits inside the walls and outside every gate (`city_flophouse_inside_walls`, `city_flophouse_outside_each_gate`); several estates fall inside the cropped window (`city_estates_multiple_shown`); the Imperial-road label sits outside a gate (`city_road_label_outside_walls`); the surrounding fields sit close, are farmhouse-ringed even off-edge with the SHOWN portion at village density, and (if moated) >= 3 large ones are moat-irrigated (`city_fields_close_to_city`, `city_outside_fields_have_farmhouses`, `outside_fields_farmhouse_density`, `city_moat_irrigates_fields`); no in-wall farms unless `meta(agricultural_district=True)`, and any in-wall fields ringed densely with farmhouses all the way round (`city_no_inwall_farms`, `city_interior_fields_farmhouse_density`); and where a moat is drawn it encircles the wall and is fed from off-map (`city_moat_surrounds_wall`, `city_moat_fed_offmap`).

**Three disciplines this gate has taught us:**

1. **Any rule that can be machine-checked belongs in `check_village.py`, not only in this prose.** When a new Mode B rule emerges, add it as an assertion.
2. **The manifest must record what is actually RENDERED, not the generator's pre-render inputs.** The fields render as a smoothed (Catmull-Rom) curve that bows inward of the raw outline vertices; recording the vertices let a channel "connect" in the manifest while visually stopping in the gap. The generator now records the *sampled smoothed boundary* (`smooth_points`). A check is only as honest as the geometry it asserts against - sample the drawn shape, and still eyeball a crop, because a green check on the wrong geometry is worse than no check. **The checks run against the JSON manifest, never the rendered SVG/PNG** - `s.finish()` writes the picture and the manifest from one in-memory model so they cannot drift, and the gate does pure geometry over coordinates (exact and fast) rather than re-deriving objects from pixels (lossy and ambiguous). The PNG is the human deliverable; the manifest is the machine-checkable truth.
3. **Test the checks themselves, with negative fixtures, and enforce 100% coverage.** `gate(M)` takes a manifest dict and returns the failed-check names (`main(path)` wraps it for the CLI). The suite has **four** legs: **`test_villages.py`** proves the real maps PASS the whole gate (integration, running the gens in-process so they count toward coverage); **`test_checks.py`** proves each check FIRES on a deliberately-broken synthetic manifest (unit); **`test_settlement.py`** reaches the generator branches the maps don't; and **`test_regressions.py`** replays the captured-failure corpus in **`pool/regressions/*.json`** - actual bad manifests, each tagged with a `_regression.fires` list of the checks it MUST still trip. The integration/unit pair is not redundant: if a refactor silently neuters a check, every real map still passes and `test_villages` stays green while the check sits dead - only a negative fixture catches that. **Coverage is gated at 100%** (`pyproject.toml`: `[tool.coverage.report] fail_under = 100`), so this isn't aspirational - the suite *fails* below 100%. Run the **whole** suite (`python3 -m pytest` from the skill dir; needs `pytest-cov`); a subset under-reports and trips the gate. The few genuinely-unreachable defensive fallbacks carry an explained `# pragma: no cover`. **When you add a check or a generator branch, add the test that exercises it** - the gate will fail until you do. Writing "here is a map that SHOULD fail this" also forces you to enumerate the ways the thing can be wrong, which is how *logic gaps* (not just regressions) surface - the streets-to-nowhere miss was such a gap.

   **STANDING REQUIREMENT - capture every "bad" map as a regression fixture.** 100% line coverage does NOT prove a check has teeth: a check whose condition is silently always-true still runs its `check(...)` line on every passing map, so coverage stays green while the check is dead. The cure is a manifest that actually *trips* it. So: **whenever you add OR refine a check - or you eyeball a generated map and find a flaw the gate let through - save the manifest of that bad map into `pool/regressions/<name>.json` with a `_regression` block** (`{"fires": ["the_check_that_should_catch_it"], "source": "..."}`), then make the check catch it. The maps we generate while iterating toward one we're happy with are exactly this corpus: each "oh, that one wasn't good enough" is a free, real negative fixture - don't throw it away, drop its `.json` (manifest only; the PNG re-renders from it) into `pool/regressions/`. `test_regressions.py` globs the directory, so a new file is picked up with no wiring. The backfill of the existing in-test fixtures into this corpus was produced by `make_regressions.py` (re-run it to regenerate the auto-captured set); going forward the discipline needs no tooling - just save the manifest. Note the corpus currently pins the ~80 checks that have a negative fixture; the remaining checks are still only exercised on their PASS path (real maps), so prefer adding a captured failure for any check you touch that lacks one.

## Historical grounding: the "why" behind the realism checks

**Requirement (project rule, restated here):** whenever historical research drives a check, a generation rule, or a magic number, record the *reasoning* here next to the rule - not just the rule. The check is the "what"; this section is the "why," so a future reader (or a future us, after the research has fallen out of memory / context) can revisit a decision without redoing the legwork. Source citations are optional; the reasoning is mandatory. Each entry: what the research found, the decision it drove, and any deliberate departure from literal scale (we draw small features oversized for legibility - see "Core principle: roughly to scale" in [`SKILL.md`](SKILL.md) - but keep *relative* sizes roughly honest).

- **ONE NAME per river, end to end - a deliberate anti-historical liberty (naming research 2026-07-24).** *What the research found:* one-river-many-names was the NORM in the pre-modern world, in both reference cultures. China: the Yangtze never had a single pre-modern name - its course ran Tuotuo He / Tongtian He / Jinsha Jiang, then regionally Chuan Jiang (Sichuan) / Jing Jiang (Hubei) / Xunyang Jiang / Yangzi Jiang (originally only the Nanjing-Shanghai reach; modern standardization settled on Chang Jiang). Japan: per-stretch renaming was standard practice - the Chikuma-gawa becomes the Shinano-gawa at the Shinano/Echigo provincial border, the Seta/Uji/Yodo system renames at each confluence, and within Edo itself one river carried different names neighborhood by neighborhood (Asakusa-gawa / Ryogoku-gawa / Okawa / Sumida-gawa, all the same water). The mechanism: pre-modern river names were LOCAL - people named the reach they lived on and used, and nobody needed a whole-course name because nobody administered or traveled the whole course; names broke at both political borders and confluences. One-name-per-river is a modern bureaucratic artifact (national mapping agencies, Japan's 1896/1964 River Laws, the PRC settling on Chang Jiang). *The decision it drove:* Rokugan rivers keep ONE name along their whole course, across every province and clan territory - the same "limit the number of place names" liberty as the capital-naming rule in l7r.md's "Place Names" section (the provincial city of Nagahara seats Nagahara province; the capital of the Reiji domain is Shiro Reiji, even though the capital of Virginia is not Virginia City), and made for the same reason: forcing players to remember more names is bad game design even when the extra names are historically accurate. So when a river crosses provinces (e.g. the river that runs through Nagahara and continues into the Fox Clan's Minami province), every map and note uses the same name for it, and no map invents a local variant. Map-label doctrine is unchanged (rivers rarely get labels at all); this governs prose, titles, and notes whenever a river IS named.
- **The bell-and-drum tower - one per WALLED seat, at the main crossing** (drives `s.drum_tower`, `walled_settlement_has_drum_tower`, the citybudget "bell-and-drum tower" line; GM decision 2026-07-24; fixtures: pre-tower Tango + pre-tower Hirameki). *What the research found:* the "morning bell, evening drum" institution (dawn gate-opening, the dusk gate-closing that began the street curfew, the five night watches, alarm and ceremony) was part of the standard Ming county-seat kit alongside the yamen, the Confucian temple, and the City God temple - common approaching standard in walled northern seats. A county seat had ONE tower - a drum tower, a combined bell-and-drum tower, or a market tower straddling the main street; the paired gulou + zhonglou on an axis is CAPITAL grammar (Beijing, Xi'an), and Pingyao, a wealthy county seat, has exactly one (the ~60 ft Market Tower on South Street). County-tier form: a masonry platform ~60-80 ft square carrying a 2-3 story timber pavilion, at the central crossroads near (not inside) the yamen; poorer seats made do with a *qiaolou* - a drum tower over the yamen's own gate (a recognized cheaper variant, not drawn here). Critically, FIRE WATCH WAS A SEPARATE INSTITUTION in both reference cultures - Song Kaifeng ran 20+ dedicated *wanghuolou* fire-lookout towers with a standing brigade, and Edo split the licensed *toki no kane* time bell from the *hinomi-yagura* fire towers - so the fire towers do not cover the timekeeping/curfew niche. *The decision it drove:* every walled seat (provincial city or walled town) draws exactly ONE combined bell-and-drum tower at its main street crossing (a corner of the crossing, not straddling the street), 70 ft at city tier, ~60 ft at town tier, visibly heavier-built than the skeletal fire towers; the capital tier may take the full paired gulou/zhonglou when it exists. **An UNWALLED town is exempt**: it has no gates to close, and its time signal is the monastery's bell - the Edo pattern, where most towns contracted a temple bell rather than building a tower - implied within the precinct, no glyph (Hoshizora). The tower follows the WALL, not the population. *Audibility - one central tower covers the whole seat with enormous margin (GM sanity check 2026-07-24, researched).* The geometry: Tango's farthest in-wall resident stands ~1,640 ft (500 m) from its tower and the farthest drawn gate-suburb structure ~790 m; Nagahara ~435 m / ~920 m. The attested anchors dwarf those distances: Edo's Kokucho time bell BILLED ~400-410 blocks of households "within earshot" (*kane-yaku-sen*, 4 mon per month per house - an effective fee radius of ~1.2-1.4 km in a far denser, noisier city, and a conservative figure, since only admitted hearers were billed); Basho casually heard the Ueno/Asakusa bells ~3-4 km away across the river; Beijing's single drum tower timed the watches for an inner city ~6.5 x 5.3 km. Acoustically, a large bell or great drum runs ~110-130 dB near the tower; at a 500-730 m city edge that arrives ~40 dB above a premodern NIGHT noise floor (~25-35 dBA, when the watches matter most) - loud, not merely detectable, everywhere inside the walls and suburbs, and the low frequencies diffract over one-story rooflines. One tower stops sufficing only past a ~2-3 km radius of daytime urban din, so even the future ~12,000-pop capital tier (~1 mi across) needs no second tower on audibility grounds: the historical scaling answers are Edo's multiplied fee-district bells vs the China-first pattern of ONE monumental tower whose watches ward night-watchmen relay through the streets with clappers and gongs - the capital tier should take the latter (grander tower, implied watchmen, still exactly one).
- **Every comb paddy fan has a FIELD FLOOR under its plots** (drives `paddy_fan_has_floor`, `s.comb_base_fill(net, name)` recording `M['comb_floors'][name]`; fixtures `paddy_fan_has_floor_fires_on_tangos_floorless_fans` + `..._on_uedas_floorless_village_comb`). The comb carve tessellates its paddy and dry plots but cannot fill the odd triangles at the canal JUNCTIONS - the head-race fork where it splits into the two supply canals, the outfall corner where a supply canal dies at the drain, the confluence wedges. With nothing drawn under the plots those triangles show the bare parchment LAND background - the "blank bits on the paddies" the GM circled repeatedly across three days (2026-07-22), on cities AND (less obviously, under the scrub matrix) villages and hamlets. Reasoning about the carve GEOMETRY to patch them (command-area fillers, hem bands) kept missing, because the junctions sit above the supply canal / past the outfall, exactly where those fillers are bounded OUT. The robust fix is architectural: draw a base-fill polygon under the plots first, so every gap - junction, inter-plot sliver, rim slack - reads as field ground, not a hole. `s.comb_base_fill` does it and records the floor. Two extents: **cities** fill the FULL envelope in soil-tan (`#CDB78C`, `full_envelope=True`) - a tight-cropped city has no surrounding scrub, so the edge junctions must be covered too; **villages/hamlets/towns** fill paddy-green clipped to the PLOTS' union bbox (feature 012), which covers the interior junctions while leaving the nucleated map's harmless phantom tail and the homestead-cluster ground unpainted (the scrub matrix covers those). This is why the shared `draw_comb_field` maps were already fine (they had the fill since feature 012) and only the inline-drawing gens (the old city comb_field, plus hikari/hoshigaoka/ueda/ikegami/moritono/akagahara) showed the blanks - they lacked it. `paddy_fan_gapless`'s 2% tolerance let the small junction triangles slip; `paddy_fan_has_floor` requires every irrigated fan (a paddy field with recorded `field_ditches`) to have a floor, so a floorless comb fires at any scale.
- **A comb's HEAD ground is quilted with dry crops** (drives `city_fan_heads_quilted`, the village-real `dry_band` values in the city gens, the fork-triangle b-side hem band, and the grain-scaled hem berm; fixture: `city_fan_heads_quilted_fires_on_tangos_bare_heads`).
  - *What the GM's circled screenshot showed (2026-07-21).* Bare parchment at every city fan's head - along the supply canals and in the triangle between the two arms at the head-race fork. That ground is uncommanded by gravity (it sits at or above its canals), so the paddy carve correctly never plants rice there; historically it is prime DRY-crop ground (barley, millet, buckwheat beside the head-race), and on the village maps it reads full because the hem quilts it and the scrub matrix textures the rest. The city gens invoked hems at village px values unscaled for 3 ft/px (42-78 real ft instead of 140-264) on maps with no scrub - the fill system existed and was simply under-invoked, a regression against the pre-`.clones`-era fill work.
  - *Dry parcels are to REAL scale too* (`dry_plots_to_scale`, fixture `dry_plots_to_scale_fires_on_tangos_oversized_hem_parcels`): a hem parcel is a smallholder's strip - Buck's surveys put the mean Chinese dry parcel near 1 mu (~0.17 acre), and the village maps land right there (0.16-0.17 mean; the hamlet's garden-scale strips at ~0.04). `_dry_fields`' tiling constants (46px parcel width, 36px row depth) are real-feet quantities at the 2 ft/px tuning grain and now scale by `grain`; unscaled at 3 ft/px they doubled every parcel's area to ~0.34-0.38 acre - dry cells visibly dwarfing the ~78 ft rice plots beside them ("like we set a number of pixels and not a number of feet" - the GM's exact catch, 2026-07-21). The gate holds the map-wide MEAN under 0.25 real acres. The `dry_plot_furrows_vary` adjacency radius is likewise 100 REAL feet now, not 50px.
  - *The check's shape.* Sample both flanks of every recorded MAIN channel beyond the hem berm (offsets 20/34/48 real ft), skipping the sluice mouth (90 ft) and the moat/ring corridors; a sample is covered by any paddy plot, dry plot, or channel. Map-wide bare fraction must stay under 20% - calibrated with the pre-fix manifest at ~25% and the quilted maps at ~13-16%. Only fields recording `plot_polys` are gated (cities); villages read full via scrub and can opt in by recording them.
- **A comb fan wastes no commanded ground - the carve's minimum sizes are REAL FEET, and awkward wedges get terraced** (drives `build_comb(grain=2/ftpx)`, the `_fill_wedges` post-pass, and the `paddy_fan_gapless` check; the frozen fixture is Tango's holey combs, 2026-07-21).
  - *What happened.* The white-spots bug - bare parchment wedges inside a paddy fan - was fixed for villages once (canal-side closers, the closing rank onto the drain, the zero-width-row anchor at ditch forks), then re-appeared on the provincial-city maps. The carve's "too small to plant" thresholds (minimum sector/row/plot widths, canal berms, drain set-backs, closer margins) are pixel constants tuned at the village grain of 1px = 2ft; at the city grain of 1px = 3ft the same pixels mean 1.5x the real feet, so the carve silently dropped sectors, head plots, and closers a village would have planted. `grain` scales them so the thresholds mean the same real-world size at every scale.
  - *Why the filler pass and why it tiles.* Even scale-correct, the carve leaves slivers where ditch threads diverge - and historically a cascade fan wasted nothing: irrigable land was too valuable, so fork wedges were terraced into small irregular paddies. `_fill_wedges` plants the leftover bare clusters with fan-aligned (u,f-frame) plots, tiled at ~plot_across x row_step so no filler dwarfs the ~0.08-acre plots around it (relative-size doctrine), overlapping neighbors by at most ~12 real ft (fillers draw last, so a lap reads as the shared bund). Gated to `grain != 1` purely for byte-stability of the visually-vetted village pool.
  - *Why the ditch net draws in a LATE water block - on EVERY comb map, not just cities (GM 2026-07-21, Hoshizora's "canals rendering below the rice paddies").* All watercourses composite in one shared-opacity block spliced at the FIRST water call's document position - a single-comb village reaches water after drawing its field, so its ditches paint OVER the fan, but any map that draws water BEFORE a field hides that field's net UNDER the later plots (an invisible network, plus parchment pinstripes on the uncovered ditch corridors): a city's moat/river anchors the block early (the case caught first, patched per-gen with `field_channel(late=True)` in the city comb wrappers), a TOWN's water-first stream/road layout does exactly the same (Hoshizora/Hirameki - the GM's catch), and even village-scale maps hit it when a SECOND comb's plots draw over the first comb's net (Hikari-no-sato). So the engine now routes every comb net late automatically (`field()` passes `late=True` unconditionally), and the late block **RE-ANCHORS at every late call** rather than pinning at its first - a multi-comb map emits plots-then-channels per field, so a first-call anchor would still sit under every LATER field's plots (the residual hole Tango/Nagahara's per-gen patch had on their 2nd+ fans; abandoned placeholders are empty strings, inert). Ratcheted by an SVG-level audit in `test_villages` (`_channels_under_plots`: no channel midpoint may lie inside a plot polygon that appears later in the document) - deliberately an SVG test, not a manifest check, because paint order is not manifest-recorded, same as the per-tuft scatter skips. Late ends are clipped to abut other water, so the blocks never double-composite. Channel widths also scale by `grain`, so a supply canal or tapering ditch is the same REAL feet at every map scale. The in-wall exception stands: an in-city drain may STOP short of the patrol road, implying an underground stone culvert to the moat (the GM's rule - never draw a ditch running through the rampart).
  - *Why the check's tolerance is bund-scale and ditches count as cover.* Anything wider than a bund (~6 real ft) inside the command area must be planted or be WATER; the recorded field ditches draw over the fan, so crediting them lets the tolerance stay tight without flagging the delivery-ditch strips between plot columns. Only fields that record their drawn `plots` are gated - the city gens do; a village gen opts in by recording them.
- **Swept ground around sacred + funerary features** (drives the `self.clearings` keep-out that `commons` scrub + `marsh` reed scatter skip, added by `_clear_ground` from `shrine_hall` (hall + each torii) and `cemetery`). **Gated by `scatter_respects_swept_clearings`** (since 2026-07-20): every clearing and every cover draw records an ordinal (`seq`) in the manifest, and the check fires when a commons/marsh poly overlapping a clearing drew BEFORE the clearing existed - unless a pre-cover `reserve_clearing` guard already protected that ground (the documented duplicate-registration pattern is recognized).
  - **The verge outline is ORGANIC, never the padded rectangle (GM 2026-07-23: "such clearage rarely conforms to precise geometric shapes").** The old collar was the feature footprint grown by `extra` as an axis-aligned rectangle, and the scatter skip made that rectangle visible: a crisp bare box in the scrub around every shrine and graveyard. *The why:* swept ground is PRODUCED by tending - brooms, feet, the sando's traffic - radiating outward from the feature, and its edge sits wherever the tending peters out into the scrub that season; nobody surveys it. Straight ruled edges belong to things that ARE surveyed or built - walls, paddy bunds, house plots (the same reasoning as the perimeter-dike and organic-burial-ground rules: geometric precision is earned by construction, not by maintenance). *The mechanics:* `_clear_ground` carves irregular INWARD-ONLY bays into the padded rect (16 edge samples, bay depth up to ~55% of the collar, damped at corners, tangential jitter) under a footprint-seeded, state-restored RNG - identical args always yield the identical blob (render-sync determinism) and the map's own RNG stream never shifts, so ONLY collar shapes changed pool-wide. *Why bays-only, no outward lobes:* a collar is a maintenance CLAIM - making it irregular means the sweeping falls short of the surveyed ideal, it never annexes ground - and an outward lobe can newly overlap a cover that legitimately predates the clearing, flipping `scatter_respects_swept_clearings` on a previously-clean map (the first lobed draft did exactly that on Ueda: the graveyard collar's lobe reached the toe marsh, cover seq 3, which draws before the stage-3b reserve). Bays-only means every blob is a subset of the old rectangle, so the change is pool-safe by construction. *Same-center dedupe:* a duplicate registration within 4px of an existing clearing's center (the documented reserve_clearing-then-feature pattern - the torii's internal collar even sits 2px off its reserve) REUSES the first blob verbatim, so guard and late collar can never disagree about the swept outline. The `scatter_respects_swept_clearings` sampling was tightened to match: exposure now tests the exact clearing/guard POLYS, not their bboxes (a bbox guard would credit a blob with ground its bays never swept; a bbox clearing would claim exposure on ground outside the blob). Tests: `test_settlement.py::test_clearings_keep_scrub_off_sacred_and_funerary_ground` (blob shape + containment-in-rect + feature containment), `::test_clear_ground_is_deterministic_and_preserves_the_rng_stream`, `::test_clear_ground_dedupes_same_center_registrations`.
  - *What the research found (China-first, Japan corroborating; GM asked, 2026-07-19).* The ground immediately around these was kept CLEAR of wild scrub, while the surrounding waste stayed scrubby - a tended verge, not a big bald radius. **Shrine precinct**: the keidai / forecourt was a swept, raked-gravel or flagged surface (purity), and in the Chinese case a village earth-god shrine or ancestral hall fronted a hard swept plaza (grain-drying, market, opera). **Torii + sando**: the approach path and the ground under the arch were kept clear and maintained the length of the sando, never overgrown. **Graves**: PARTIAL - graves sat on marginal scrubby back-slope/waste ground, but grave-tending (Chinese Qingming tomb-sweeping, Japanese haka-mairi) clears weeds off the mound plus a modest collar; the waste even a short way out stays scrubby. So: clear AT the graves, wild BETWEEN them.
  - *The decision.* A small swept collar around the shrine (extra ~58px pre-bscale), each torii + its sando footing (~30px), and the grave plot (~30px), keeping the loose hinterland scatter off it. Deliberately modest ("a little bit of clearance") - the surrounding scrub commons is unchanged a stride out.
  - *The one nuance that shaped the design.* A Japanese shrine's setting is a DELIBERATELY-PRESERVED grove (chinju no mori) - swept precinct set INSIDE preserved trees, the opposite of cleared. So the clearing keep-out affects ONLY the loose scrub/marsh scatter, never the grove (a separate drawn feature) and never building placement - a shrine's fengshui back-grove stands untouched right up to the swept precinct, exactly as in reality.
  - *ORDERING GOTCHA (this bit us once).* The scatter only skips clearings that EXIST when it runs, so a precinct placed AFTER `hinterland()` / the `commons`/`marsh` scatter reads UNCLEARED (the scrub is already down). Two fixes: (a) `s.roll_village(..., lay_hinterland=False)` then call `s.hinterland()` yourself AFTER the precinct (Kikuta), or (b) `s.reserve_clearing(x, y, w, h, extra)` with the precinct's footprints BEFORE the scatter, then draw the precinct wherever (Hoshigaoka, Hikari, Ueda - for a precinct dropped in post-crop or whose coords are known early). Do NOT assume a precinct sits on ground no scatter will ever touch: Ueda's graveyard was safely on open ground until the satoyama ring was completed under it (2026-07-20), and the pre-existing cemetery silently lost its collar to the new S band - the bit-us-twice that made this a gated check (`scatter_respects_swept_clearings`) instead of a doc note.
- **Stable yard - the gate caravan yard reads as IN ACTIVE USE, not empty** (drives `stables_have_yards`, city scale; `s._stable_yard`, drawn automatically by `s.stables(yard=True)`; fixture `stables_have_yards_fires_on_a_blank_gate_yard`). A gate stables keeps an open ~85px berth (the pack keeps dwellings out), but drawn as blank parchment it read as forgotten emptiness (GM asked, 2026-07-22).
  - *What the research found (China-first, Song/Ming-Qing; Edo Japan secondary; sources incl. the Qingming Shanghe Tu 清明上河図 gate scene, the caravanserai court, the Chinese hitching post 拴马桩, the yizhan 驿站 / shukuba post-station).* A city-gate cart/animal yard was **beaten tamped earth** - NO grass (trampled hard, and the animals were **hay-fed at mangers, not grazed** there) - and, crucially, **NOT a fenced paddock** (the least authentic option; a rail fence belongs to an inn's private back-yard or a walled caravanserai). Its edges are the wall + flanking buildings; its "in active use" signal is **carts, animals tethered at hitching rails / picket lines, and littered ground** (the Qingming convention: clustered carts and pack animals, no fence, no lawn). WELL-ATTESTED: the hitching post as a Chinese fixture, the Qingming gate scene, the caravanserai court. INFERRED (reasoned from those norms - no source describes an ordinary gate cart-yard's ground directly): the no-grass beaten-earth surface and the open-not-fenced edge.
  - *The decision.* Draw the yard as a feathered SCATTER (house style, no solid fill - a filled polygon reads as a crisp rhombus) of beaten-earth scuff + straw litter, **two or three hitching rails with tethered draft animals** (a wagon-train ties up many animals - the authentic answer to the fence instinct), a stone trough, and a dung heap or two. NO parked-wagon icons (tried 2026-07-22, removed as clutter). The FIRST rail is **road-parallel, set back from the nearest road/street**, its animals facing into the yard (rumps to the roadbed) - the road-side barrier keeping stock off the through-road (the GM's insight); the rest sit at clear interior spots. The scatter auto-avoids the stables/inn/flophouse/funerary footprints, the road/streets, fields, and water (filling only the genuinely open pocket) and does NOT avoid `block_polys` (those RESERVED the pocket for exactly this). Glyphs are legibility-tuned for city ftpx=3 (the wellhead-marker doctrine; a true ~10 ft cart would be ~3 px).
  - *Furniture keeps off the ROADS and the WALL - and the yard draws at CROP time (GM 2026-07-24; `stable_yard_furniture_clear_of_roads_walls`).* Hitching rails and dung heaps must not overlap any way tread (road, ring road, street, alley) or the rampart's clearance: the road-side rail's whole purpose is keeping tethered stock OFF the through-road, so a rail whose tip lands on the tread defeats itself, and a heap on the tread or against the wall fouls the public way / the patrol strip. Two mechanisms deliver it. (1) *Full-extent probes:* the old placement tested only each glyph's CENTER, so an 18px rail could lay its tip (len/2 + 2.4px post reach) on a road - candidates now probe the rail's tips and the heap's ellipse edge, and `_corridor_buffers` gained the alleys + the ring road (a rail tip on an alley is the same defect). (2) *Flush-late:* the yard used to draw at stables() time and could not see streets drawn AFTER it - Nagahara's wharf-yard heap sat on a later-laid NE-quarter street (the pinned real fixture). stables()/animal_ground() now QUEUE their yards and `flush_stable_yards()` (auto-run by `crop_city`) draws them when the map is complete - the placement-and-check-read-the-same-data doctrine (see PLANK BRIDGES). Ripple-free: the scatter runs on its own seeded RNG, and a bonus of late drawing is that the watering point sees every real well, so the dig-your-own fallback fires only when the neighborhood genuinely lacks one (the dug wellhead also probes the well checks' own way margins). Rails and heaps are recorded per yard (`rails` / `dung_heaps` on `M['stable_yards']`) so the check tests the drawn geometry; legacy pinned manifests without those keys are skipped, never retro-failed.
  - *Placement - no move needed (GM asked whether it belongs against the wall).* The yard sits a little INSIDE the wall behind the defensive wall-base setback (Tango's intramural ring road), near the gate, fronting the road where carts pull in - NOT flush against the masonry (the wall base was kept clear for defense/circulation) and NOT on the rampart. The flophouse stays OUTSIDE the gate (the extramural gate-suburb / *guanxiang* is where cheap lodging historically clustered - convenience lodging for arriving peasants/carters, NOT the old dusk-curfew rationale; see `flophouse-research.md`); the inn + stables + yard sit INSIDE (secure overnight animal holding). Place the stables AFTER its cluster's inn + flophouse so the scatter skips them. City-scoped for now - a town's single caravan stables keeps plain open ground until the yard geometry is made scale-aware.
  - *Watering - a WELL-ANCHORED TROUGH CLUSTER, not one token trough (GM 2026-07-23, researched + source-verified).* The GM asked whether caravan grounds should show water troughs big enough to read at map scale. They should, and the original single ~6 ft trough glyph was functionally undersized. *What the research found:* a working ox drinks ~10 gal/day (range 3-30 by heat/work), a pack horse 5-18, a water buffalo 40-60+ L and it barely sweats (it wants a WALLOW, not just a trough) - so a 20-40 head wagon-train arriving thirsty needs ~300-600 gallons, drunk in one or two big sessions. Historical practice waters BY RELAY at a fixed point: Silk Road caravanserais watered whole trains from a courtyard well/cistern; Chinese inn yards drew by bucket from a well into troughs (wells, not channels, are the in-town norm); traditional stone stock troughs run ~8 ft x 2 ft (London's high-traffic granite street troughs ~9.5 ft - one busy trough served 1,800 horses/day, throughput by turnover), with ~2 ft of trough edge per drinking head and both sides of a freestanding trough usable. Animals are LED to the water in relays - you water at the well, not at the hitching rail. *The decision:* `_stable_yard` draws a WATERING POINT - 2 troughs for a plain stables yard, 3 for a caravan-scale ground (`r >= 76`), ~14 ft long each - clustered BESIDE the nearest recorded well within `r + 40`: offset from the wellhead by only its visual radius + half a trough (~bucket-pour distance, GM 2026-07-23 - "otherwise you'd have to carry the water a long way"), on the yard side, even when the well stands at or just past the yard rim; recorded as `troughs` + the cluster center `troughs_at` on the `M['stable_yards']` entry. **A yard with NO reachable well - or every flank of the near wellhead blocked - DIGS ITS OWN courtyard well** and clusters the troughs beside that (GM 2026-07-23, promoted from a silent random-spot fallback to a placement rule + check after Nagahara: both its yards had fallen back, leaving 100/241 ft bucket-carries that Tango happened not to have). The historical form supports the dig: the Silk Road caravanserai and the yizhan post-yard watered whole trains from their OWN courtyard well/cistern - "no well nearby" is a reason to sink one, never to carry 300-600 gallons across a city block. Gated by `stable_troughs_beside_well`: every yard with `troughs > 0` must record `troughs_at` within **40 real ft** of a well (the placement's own ~24 ft worst case + slack; a genuine carry blows far past it) - fixtures `stable_troughs_far_from_any_well_nagahara` (the real pre-fix capture) plus the two synthetic `stable_troughs_beside_well_fires_*`. **The cluster BOX draws on open ground** (GM 2026-07-23, same day): the hug offset is **direction-aware** - the minimal center distance at which the cluster box (t_len x t_total) clears the well-house roof square along the chosen ray, + the 1.5 px step - because a fixed `vr + t_len/2` only guarantees HORIZONTAL clearance and the 2-3-trough stack is TALLER than it is wide, so a near-vertical ray clipped the roof corner (Tango's caravan ground, the motivating defect). The box is also corner-checked against everything the yard's `clear()` knows (buildings incl. houses, roads, fields, water, the wall) and kept off every other wellhead roof; placement records the drawn extent as `troughs_box`. Gated by `stable_troughs_clear_of_buildings` (rotation-exact SAT against every solid footprint + every roof square; an unrecorded box fails) - fixtures `stable_troughs_clip_the_well_house_roof_tango` (the real pre-fix capture) plus the three synthetic `stable_troughs_clear_of_buildings_fires_*`. *Departures:* trough width is floored at the 2px cartographic minimum (true ~2.5 ft would be sub-pixel at 3 ft/px - the wellhead-marker legibility doctrine), and the buffalo WALLOW (a 15-30 ft mud pond, very China-first) is deliberately NOT auto-drawn - it is an available flourish for a specific map's gen where ground and water fit, not a default.
  - *Capacity - why 2-3 troughs absorb several dozen oxen, and why MORE troughs is the wrong lever (GM asked, 2026-07-23: "there might be several dozen oxen passing through at a time... 2 troughs doesn't feel like enough").* It is enough, and the reason is worth keeping because the naive fix (add troughs) does nothing. **Edge capacity:** each drawn trough is ~14 ft at ~2 ft of edge per drinking head, both sides of a freestanding trough usable - so one trough serves ~14 head at once (call it 7 where the wellhead crowds one side); the caravan ground's 3 troughs are ~20-40 simultaneous stations, a plain yard's 2 are ~14-28. **Turnover:** cattle drink ~1-2 gal/min, so a working ox's 5-8 gal session is over in ~5 minutes - even read one-sided, the caravan cluster waters ~20 head every ~6 minutes, and several dozen oxen clear in two or three relays (~20-30 min). That fits how a stage stop worked: animals were unyoked and rested for HOURS, so watering was a leisurely relay chore for a couple of teamsters, not a race - the London figure (one 9.5 ft trough, 1,800 horses/day) is the throughput-by-turnover anchor. **The binding constraint is the WELL, not the trough edge:** a hand bucket-draw sustains maybe 5-10 gal/min, so a train's 300-600 gallons is 1-2 hours of steady drawing NO MATTER how many troughs stand there. Extra troughs would not water anyone faster; they would just hold more standing water. What the troughs actually do is BUFFER - filled between arrivals so the first relay drinks instantly while the drawing continues - which is exactly why caravanserais centralized on one courtyard well/cistern instead of multiplying basins, and why coaching-inn yards typically show a SINGLE trough (our 2-3 is already the generous end). **The right lever if a specific map ever needs more watering throughput** (a border city where two trains overlap) is a second WELL or a cistern, never a fourth trough.
- **Gate structures are TO SCALE, not fixed-pixel markers** (GM asked whether they were scaled, 2026-07-22; the true-feet footprints in `city_wall`'s guard house / inspection / gatepost and `_tower`'s mamian bastion + gate tower; overlap-classified, no dedicated new check - the to-scale doctrine covers them).
  - *The bug.* These were authored as FIXED-PIXEL glyphs (guard house 66x44, inspection 60x44, gatepost 14x31, tower 38-40 px SQUARE) that ignored `ftpx`, so at the city's 3 ft/px they implied a ~198x132 ft guard house, ~180x132 ft inspection, ~114 ft towers - a gate duty-room drawn LARGER than the 130-ft Temple of Bishamon. Exactly the torii's old fixed-38-px-rail (114 ft) error, fixed the same way.
  - *What the research found (China first: Xi'an / Pingyao / Beijing walls; Edo sekisho secondary).* A gate guard duty room is a small 1-3 bay building (~15-35 ft); a gate inspection hall (sekisho/lijin bansho) ~25-45 ft; the wall's MAMIAN bastion (马面 - the projecting spur that carries the enemy-tower) is ~65x40 ft (Xi'an's are ~20 m wide projecting ~12 m), the tower building on it ~30-40 ft; a provincial GATE tower (城楼) ~52x30 ft (reserve the 120-130 ft towers for a capital); a corner tower ~50-66 ft. Well-attested: the mamian and the provincial gate-tower footprints; approximate (bay-count estimates): the guard/inspection buildings.
  - *The decision.* Footprints in real feet via `s.px()`: guard house 34x20, inspection 44x22, gatepost 15x24, gate tower 52x30 - and the wall tower REDRAWN as a mamian bastion 62x40 (a rectangle PROJECTING from the wall, longer along it than deep, with the enemy-tower building inset) instead of a fixed square. Sizes sit at the legible upper end of each attested range - a real value, never inflated past it. Strokes keep their legibility floor (the stroke convention, SKILL.md 'to scale'); the footprint takes no license. The town `wall()`'s single "guard station" (96x46 px) uses its own path and is left for a follow-up.
  - *Knock-on (the reflow tax).* The smaller furniture freed N-gate ground on Nagahara, re-packing the warren denser: two idobata draw-points went over the 26-household ceiling (split with a denser court grid) and the burakumin caste floor dropped to 20 (its top-up was inside the dwelling-total-capped loop, which the freed room reached first - promoted to an unconditional floor ahead of the cap). Tango absorbed the reflow with no change.
- **Gate guard house + inspection sit AT THE THROAT, flanking the road** (GM asked whether they looked too far from the gate, 2026-07-22; drives the short-arc opposite-flank placement in `city_wall` and the `city_gate_furniture_at_throat` check; fixture `city_gate_furniture_at_throat_fires_when_walked_back_along_the_wall`).
  - *The bug.* Once the furniture went TO SCALE (small ~14x7 px), the pair still used their old placement: BOTH stacked on one flank and WALKED 80/144 px (240/432 ft) ALONG the wall from the gate vertex, then radially inset to the ring road. That read as two little buildings pushed far off along the rampart, plainly detached from the gate - and the caption, centered on the inspection station, painted over the guard house (Tango's guard house nearly invisible under the label).
  - *What the research found (China first: wengcheng 甕城 barbican + lijin 厘金 / chaoguan 鈔關 tax barriers; Japan's Hakone/Arai sekisho as the best-preserved architectural proof).* An inspection/tax barrier only works where traffic is forced single-file, and a walled city's gate passage is the ONE such chokepoint in the whole wall - set the station back and arrivals disperse into the street grid before ever reaching it, defeating its purpose. So guard + inspection cluster AT the gate opening, ~20-100 ft inside, flanking the road as it enters. Hakone is decisive: just inside each gomon the *Obansho* (papers/goods inspection office) and the *ashigaru* guardhouse stand OPPOSITE each other across the road, and nobody reaches the town beyond without passing between them. In a wengcheng the whole cluster reads most authentically inside the urn-courtyard between the two misaligned gates. "Set back a few hundred feet along the wall" is historically wrong.
  - *The decision.* Each building walks a SHORT arc to its OWN flank (guard house one side, inspection the other, `guard_east` picks which), just past the road verge (road half-width + its own half-length + a 6 px gap), then radial-insets to the ring road - so the two face each other across the road at the throat, the road passing between them (the Hakone pattern), each still square to the local wall tangent. Built distance from the opening lands ~35-45 px (~110-135 ft), right at the inner mouth. ONE caption, "guard / inspection stations", is centered on the road and pushed far enough inward (along the gate radial) to clear BOTH footprints, then reserves its own ground (a `block_polys` box) because `city_wall` runs BEFORE the quarters pack - a post-pack auto-placement is impossible, so the label must claim its box up front or a crowding quarter drops a house under the text (Nagahara's N-gate laborer terraces). The furniture's own keep-clear apron dropped from the old 30 px (sized for the 66x44 glyph) to 12 px for the now-tiny buildings, since the road corridor already fends packs off one flank - the oversized apron had squeezed Nagahara's E-gate merchant blocks (`city_merchant_housing_spread`).
  - *The check with teeth.* `city_gate_furniture_at_throat` requires a guard house AND an inspection within 70 px of every gate vertex. The pre-existing `city_inspection_station_at_each_gate` (160 px) and `city_gate_has_guardhouse` (2 structs within 180 px) have deliberate barbican slack and would wave the old 85/145 px far placement straight through - the negative fixture (Tango with the pair walked back to 80/144 px) proves the new check catches exactly what the loose radii miss.
- **A fed CLOSED moat must also DRAIN - the ring flushes, it is not a terminal pond** (GM asked whether Tango's moat, fed by a stream but with nowhere to go, needed an outlet, 2026-07-22; drives Tango's SE outfall stream and the `city_moat_has_outfall` check; fixture `city_moat_has_outfall_fires_when_a_fed_closed_moat_cannot_drain`).
  - *The bug.* Tango's moat had a full-flow feeder off the high NW but no outfall - a closed ring taking water in with nowhere for it to leave. It read (correctly, to the GM's eye) as water with a source and no sink.
  - *The physics (the load-bearing "why").* Water balance at a stable level: `outflow = inflow + rain - evaporation - seepage`. With NO outlet, `outflow = 0` forces `inflow = evaporation + seepage`; a real perennial stream delivers far more than a moat's surface can evaporate or its bed can seep, so storage climbs and the moat **overtops its banks** - "the level just keeps rising" is not a steady state, it is flooding. (A stream's upstream profile is set by its own bed slope, not the pond it enters - raising the moat only backs water up a short distance at the mouth, it cannot lift the whole feeder, so you cannot absorb continuous inflow by "raising the stream too.") The terminal-pond regime is real but belongs to a **spring/rain-fed** moat in an **arid** climate where small diffuse input is balanced by evaporation; a wet rice climate (modest evaporation; a high water table and puddled paddies that seal seepage) cannot absorb a live stream, so a stream-fed moat there MUST shed the surplus through a channel.
  - *What the research found (China first: Beijing's gated water-passes + the Forbidden City moat; Japan agreeing: Edo/Matsue jokamachi moats).* Flow-through was the standard, engineered deliberately. **Beijing** admitted water through gated wall passes, branched it into through-city rivers, and discharged SE to the Tonghui/Grand Canal; the **Forbidden City** moat is fed from the Jade Spring and "flows in from the NORTHWEST and discharges to the SE" - inlet one corner, outfall the diagonal. Flushing mattered for sanitation (a stagnant moat stank and bred summer fevers; the remedy was flow-through + annual dredging), for **storm drainage** (a city moat doubled as the flood sluice - a drain with no outfall is not a drain), for a fire-water reserve, and for irrigation offtake. The pond-like look is legitimately achieved by an **overflow weir/sluice** that holds a set level and sheds only the surplus (Beijing's gated behavior) - placid surface, real outlet underneath. A closed moat with a live feeder and no outlet is historically wrong.
  - *The decision.* Tango drains off the LOW, downstream rim (SE - N is the high ground, `capital_dir=southeast`), diagonally opposite the NW feeder so the current flushes the ring corner-to-corner (the Forbidden City pattern). The outfall is a `s.stream(moat rim -> off-map)` as wide as the feeder (conservation of flow), threaded S between the Imperial road and the westernmost samurai estate. The existing irrigation taps to the surrounding farms stay as a legitimate SECONDARY, seasonal offtake - not a substitute for the main outfall (a 7 px summer tap cannot balance a 22 px year-round feeder). Nagahara (a river-bank city) already drains correctly: its open moat taps the river upstream and returns downstream, covered by `city_moat_joins_river`.
  - *The diverted-stream moat is itself a historical type (GM asked whether Tango's arrangement - a stream seemingly turned into the moat, then resuming its course - was real, 2026-07-23).* It is, and commonly so: a dry-site Chinese seat dug its *hucheng he* by turning a nearby stream through the ring (the Forbidden City's NW-in / SE-out flush is the model Tango already encodes), and Japanese castle towns fed moats by the same river diversions (Edo turned the Hirakawa into its moat spiral). Two honesty notes, both deliberate: (1) **no relic of the stream's pre-diversion bed is drawn through the city** - after centuries of urban buildup the abandoned course is built over, so its absence is realistic, not an omission (do not "fix" this by threading an old channel through the blocks); (2) the ring splits the feeder's flow into two live arcs (west-about and east-about) that rejoin at the outfall, which is why irrigation taps on BOTH flanks can legitimately draw "with the current" (`moat_channels_flow_with_current`).
  - *The check with teeth.* `city_moat_has_outfall` fires when a fed CLOSED (non-river) moat has no second off-map stream on the OPPOSITE face (centroid-radials pointing apart) - i.e. a feeder with no outfall, or two inlets crowding one arc. Gated on `not river` (the river-moat's inlet/outlet is already enforced by `city_moat_joins_river`) and on `moat_is_fed` (an unfed spring/rain pond-moat is legitimately exempt - no inflow to shed). The negative fixture is Tango with the SE outfall removed.
- **The gate's own tower sits AT its gate, flanking the opening - never marooned mid-curtain** (GM spotted a small gate tower stranded among the mural bastions on Tango's S gate, 2026-07-22; drives the flank-flip placement in `city_wall` and the `city_gate_tower_at_its_gate` check; fixture `city_gate_tower_at_its_gate_fires_when_the_gate_tower_is_marooned`).
  - *The bug.* Each gate carries one distinct, SMALLER tower (52x30 vs the mamian's 62x40 - see the TO SCALE bullet above). It started ~78 px along the wall on ONE flank and WALKED further out whenever that spot was blocked. On Tango's S gate a ward-gate kido's ~62 px keep-out sat right there, so the tower walked to arc ~118 - stranded among the 62x40 mamian bastions while a mamian seated closer to the gate. A smaller tower reads as "the gate's tower" only AT the gate; marooned mid-curtain it just looks like one tower randomly shrank. (The N gate, where the same tower stayed at the opening, read as intentional - which is how the GM caught the S gate as wrong.)
  - *The decision.* The tower now tries the near-gate spot on its PRIMARY flank, then the OTHER flank at the SAME short arc, and only steps outward if BOTH near-gate flanks are blocked. A kido or the gate furniture on one side sends it to the gate's OTHER side (still at the opening), not out along the curtain. Normal gates are unchanged (primary flank, arc 78); only a blocked gate flips instead of walking. Tango's S gate now sits at arc 78 on the west flank, mirroring the N gate.
  - *The check with teeth.* `city_gate_tower_at_its_gate` fires when a mural bastion sits meaningfully closer (>12 px) to a gate than that gate's own tower - i.e. the gate tower is not the closest tower to its opening. The pre-existing tower checks (`city_wall_tower_coverage`, `city_wall_towers_aligned`) say nothing about which tower is nearest the gate, so they wave the marooned placement through. The negative fixture is Tango's pre-fix manifest (S gate tower at arc 118, a mamian at 86).
- **Wall towers give INTERLOCKING flanking fire - density is a TUNABLE defense tier** (GM asked whether "every attacker is within arrow range of >= 2 towers" is accurate and whether our maps reflected it, 2026-07-22; drives `meta(wall_defense=...)`, `WALL_DEFENSE`, `settlement.wall_tower_spacing_px`, the tier-driven densification + coverage-remediation in `s.city_wall`, and the `city_wall_tower_coverage` check; fixtures in `test_checks.py`).
  - *What the research found (China first: the mamian 马面 wall-tower system; Warring-States through Ming).* The rule of thumb IS accurate, and it is the ORIGINAL design purpose of the projecting wall tower. Adjacent mamian bastions are spaced so their fields of **flanking fire (侧射) overlap** - an attacker at the curtain base between two towers is shot at from BOTH (Shen Kuo's 11th-c. Mengxi Bitan describes it as 矢石相及, "arrows and stones reach each other"). The spacing that achieves ">= 2 towers everywhere" therefore equals the effective **arrow range**: put towers a bowshot apart and every curtain point has two within a bowshot. Real spacings bracket the effective ranges: **Pingyao** ~50-60 m (>= 2 everywhere, an aimed-lethal bowshot), **Xi'an** ~120 m (= 2 x 60 m; the crossfire covers the curtain but the base near a tower has only that one at full reach - the sparser, peacetime-affordable ring). Effective bow ranges: **aimed-lethal ~60 m** (a war arrow kills reliably), **full war-bow reach ~100-150 m** (harassing fire).
  - *The decision - three tiers, because fortification tracked THREAT, not a universal constant.* A city that has repelled sieges was towered as densely as it could afford; one at peace for centuries was not. So the density is a per-city knob (`meta(wall_defense=...)`), asked at city-generation time alongside "Imperial road?" and "river?":
    - **`siege`** = `>= 2` towers within **aimed-lethal 60 m / 197 ft** (spacing == range, the Pingyao standard). Border / besieged cities. **Tango and Nagahara both use this** (border location + siege history - GM's call).
    - **`garrison`** (default) = `>= 2` within **full war-bow 100 m / 328 ft** (the looser interior-garrison ring).
    - **`peaceful`** = `>= 1` flanking tower within aimed-lethal range (curtain midpoints still get 2) - the Xi'an ~120 m spacing, a long-peaceful city.
  - *The check's shape and its keep-outs.* `city_wall_tower_coverage` samples the curtain every ~18px and requires the tier's min-count within (range + 12px). The **+12px is a mamian half-footprint** - an archer shoots from the bastion's parapet SPAN, not its center point, so a tower reaches ~12px past its recorded center; the placement code adds the same 12px, so the two agree. **Barbican and water-gate exemptions** matter as much as the coverage rule: the gate is the most-fortified point (gate tower + guard house + inspection + gateposts), and a water gate is a grated opening flanked by its own two towers - so points within 130px of a gate, 55px of its guard furniture, or 45px of a water gate are skipped. These check keep-outs deliberately **mirror the placement keep-outs** in `s.city_wall`: `_seat_mural` will not put a tower inside a barbican or on a water-gate opening, so a point the placement structurally cannot tower must not be one the check demands - otherwise the map can never pass. (This alignment is what finally cleared Nagahara's last near-gate and water-gate coverage points, 2026-07-22.) The older `city_wall_towers_spaced` (>= 6 towers, no bare arc > ~75 deg) stays as a coarse floor - cheap, and it still catches a wall with almost no towers.
  - *Deliberate departure / legibility.* Towers draw at the legible upper end of the mamian footprint (see the gate-structures entry above); the SPACING is honest to the tier, but a real 60 m bowshot at 3 ft/px is ~66px, so a siege ring is a dense necklace of bastions - which is the correct read for a border fortress and matches Pingyao's actual tower count per length.
  - *Tower SHAPE - rectangular, never round (GM asked, 2026-07-22).* Every wall/gate tower draws as a RECTANGLE - the mamian spur wider along the wall than deep (62x40 px ~ Xi'an's ~20 x 12 m, a ~1.7:1 spur); the enemy-tower block on it and the corner/gate towers run nearer square, which is also authentic (don't force a ratio there). CIRCULAR towers are deliberately absent: round towers are a EUROPEAN medieval signature (a round front resists sapping and later deflects cannon), and Chinese/Japanese fortification is rectilinear top to bottom. The "why" is an inversion of the European logic worth keeping straight - Europe shaped its towers against the ATTACKER's siege engineering; China/Japan shaped them for the DEFENDER's flanking-fire VOLUME: a rectangular tower's flat faces let more archers line up and shoot straight down the wall base, with LESS dead zone than a round one. Same problem, opposite answer. The only genuine round bastions are archaic pre-rebuild survivals (Xi'an's SW-corner roundel) - reserve a round tower ONLY to signal "an older fragment of the wall", never as the default. Japanese yagura/tenshu are likewise square/rectangular timber on stone bases; the one place Japan curves is the ishigaki WALL batter, not the towers.

- **Samurai country estates are DISPERSED, not a wall-hugging cluster** (GM asked whether the tight cluster of estates just outside the wall was accurate, 2026-07-22; drives the reduced-count + spread placement in the city gens and the `city_samurai_estates_outside` (now 1-3) + `city_samurai_estates_dispersed` checks; fixture `city_samurai_estates_fire_on_a_tight_wall_cluster`).
  - *The bug.* Both cities ringed one stretch of wall with ~5-6 walled estates packed together just beyond the moat (~400-1300 ft out) - reading as a genteel estate suburb hugging the gate.
  - *What the research found (China-first: the Ming-Qing gentry as urbanized absentee landlords + the dispersed fortified manor; Japan agreeing).* Three forces all push AGAINST a wall-cluster. **(1) Land:** elite holdings were fragmented, scattered parcels and lineages were rooted in specific ancestral villages, so the rural big-house sits among its OWN fields / at the home village, dispersed across the district (the single live-on manor was an earlier Tang-Song form). **(2) Security:** a row of rich, undefended compounds outside the wall is a bandit magnet that negates the wall - the rural estates that existed were each individually fortified (the Sengoku *yakata*, walled lineage compounds) precisely because they stood ALONE beyond the city's protection, which spreads them apart. **(3) Amenity:** the seat's exam/office/social life pulled the gentry INWARD through the gate to live in town as absentee landlords (in an Edo reading they don't commute - they're resident inside). And the belt hugging the gates was the COMMERCIAL commoner suburb (*guanxiang*), not a genteel quarter - "close to the gate" describes the wrong land use. So: the bulk of well-off samurai live INSIDE the walls (the samurai ward); the immediate wall-shadow is the commercial suburb (gate markets / flophouses, already drawn); the country estates proper are dispersed ~2-15 miles out, each an isolated fortified compound by its own land; at most a few near-city retreats sit within a mile or few, spread apart, never clustered.
  - *The decision (map-scale reality).* A city view is under a mile across (~3,800 ft), so the real country estates (miles out) are entirely OFF-MAP. The map shows only the NEAREST 1-3, SPREAD APART (>= 200 px / ~600 ft) on the open, capital-facing approaches (the fields fill the other exteriors), each on its own drive out to the district road - the rest implied off-map. `city_samurai_estates_outside` caps the shown count at 1-3 (was 5-15); `city_samurai_estates_dispersed` forbids a tight clump (the negative fixture is the old 6-estate cluster). The capital-direction lean (`city_estates_toward_capital`) is kept as a deliberate setting choice (a samurai builds his country seat on the capital-facing side); the dispersal happens WITHIN that open arc, since the field-crowded exterior leaves only the E-to-SE open.
  - *Deferred - where the full pattern would show (the district-scale map).* The genuinely dispersed pattern - estates strewn across the whole countryside, each beside its OWN fields / ancestral village, out to ~15 miles, most nowhere near the city - only becomes visible at a **district / county-seat-hinterland scale**, a separate future mode (cf. the domain-capital tier, a `separate future mode` too). At city scale the honest depiction stays "the nearest 1-3 at the frame edge, the rest off-map." Captured here per the deferred-note convention (see the sally/postern-gate note) so the idea is not lost.
- **A delivery ditch takes off DOWNSTREAM of the head fork, never AT it** (GM asked why some fields' channels come together in an intersection instead of feeding into the next, 2026-07-22; drives the 40px fork-clearance skip in `build_comb` and the `channels_join_not_cross_at_fork` check; fixture `channels_join_not_cross_at_fork_fires_on_a_delivery_at_the_division`).
  - *The bug.* The comb's sluice head-race forks at the **bunsuiguchi** division into two supply canals (a clean 3-way Y - one water feeding two, historically correct). But where canal B was SHORT (Tango's in-wall nw1, Hoshizora's west field), its single offtake landed ~0-1px from the fork, so a delivery ditch sprouted AT the division - a **4-way star** that reads as a crossroads, not directed flow. (No ditches actually cross; it is the coincident takeoff that reads as an intersection.)
  - *The fix.* `build_comb` skips DRAWING any delivery whose takeoff is within 40px of the fork - the plots it shapes keep their bunds, only the blue ditch clutter at the division goes, leaving the clean 3-way Y (matching Kikuta's accepted head). Skipping the draw (not the carve) keeps every plot byte-stable. The measured gap - the two offenders sat 0-1px out, the nearest legitimate delivery 76px - makes 40 a safe cut at every scale. `channels_join_not_cross_at_fork` gates it (a `role="branch"` ditch taking off < 40px from a >= 3-way `role="main"` node fires).
- **A paddy tiles COMPLETELY - a green base fills the gaps** (feature 012, `draw_comb_field`; `specs/012-in-field-paddy-features/research.md` D5).
  - *What was wrong.* The field drew its plot polygons straight onto the parchment background with no base fill, so imperfect plot tessellation left bare cream "white" gaps showing through (GM read them as infertile ground, 2026-07-20). Flat, flooded valley-bottom paddy is the most valuable, most intensively worked land - it tiles completely; bare islands in the wet center are not a thing (the genuine unfarmable pockets are WET - reed marsh / lotus - which we draw blue-green, not bare). So the gaps are artifacts, filled, not dressed up.
  - *The fix.* A paddy-green (`_RICE_GREEN`) wash under the plots, clipped to the PLOTS' bbox (not the raw envelope) so a nucleated map's harmless phantom tail - the over-declared `field_fall` the checks let a nucleated cluster carry, see `field_outline_matches_planting` - stays invisible instead of being painted green. Deliberate non-rice features (ponds, rock, graves, knolls) are placed as their own glyphs where the archetype matrix allows; they do NOT explain the gaps.

- **In-field paddy features are ARCHETYPE-GATED, and margin/slope-biased** (feature 012; `_paddy_features` + the glyph helpers; gated by `paddy_features_match_archetype` + `field_ponds_on_low_ground`; `specs/012-in-field-paddy-features/research.md`).
  - *What the research found.* Flat, flooded valley-bottom paddy is the archetype that hosts non-rice obstacles LEAST - it is the most valuable, most intensively worked, and wet. Grave mounds and feng-shui knolls are MARGIN/slope features in the rice south (feng-shui wants a backing hill + downslope water view, so the dead go on the slope, not the wet center); rock outcrops are a TERRACE feature (bedrock the risers wrap around) and are absent on alluvial valley/polder and delta dike-pond; small OPEN-WATER ponds (a low pocket / header tameike / half-moon by a hall) are the one thing that genuinely belongs in the wet middle. The per-archetype matrix (research.md) is encoded in `_PADDY_POND_KINDS` / `_PADDY_ROCK_KINDS` / `_PADDY_GRAVE_KINDS` and enforced by `paddy_features_match_archetype`.
  - *What we DON'T redraw.* The matrix's MARGIN graves + feng-shui knolls are already the village **burial ground** (`cemetery`) + **back-grove** (`village_grove`) every village draws - the research explicitly warns a standalone knoll usually IS the back-grove - so we do NOT draw a second, redundant set. The only genuinely new glyphs are the in-field POND, the bedrock ROCK outcrop, and a rare in-field GRAVE island.
  - *CALIBRATED LIBERTY (GM 2026-07-20, disclosed).* The in-field grave ISLAND (the "graves among the paddy" look) is a north-China-dry-plain / Japanese-corroborated signature, NOT the rice-south default (which is margin/slope). The GM approved "both", so it is drawn rarely (~30% on valley/terraces/ribbon) as a deliberate departure, recorded here and in research.md D1, not an oversight.
  - *Honest limits.* Ponds sit on the `low`-flagged ground (the low pocket), checked against `wet_plots` for teeth; a pond is size-capped so a wide terrace band gives a POND, not a field-spanning lake. Frequencies (pond ~55% of eligible fields, rock 1-3 on terraces, grave island ~30%) are legibility-driven estimates within the research's plausible ranges - every rice-south frequency in research.md is flagged interpolated (only the Japanese tameike count is hard data). dike-pond gets NONE (open water is its fabric).

- **A nucleated cluster is a COMPACT FABRIC, not a wide hollow arc** (drives `village_cluster_compact`; the crescent seed shape in `cluster_seeds`).
  - *What was wrong.* Kikuta's rolled `crescent` strung its 55 houses over a wide, hollow hull they filled only ~20%, stranding the NE horn ~350-410px (~700-825 ft) from any cropland across bare ground (GM caught it, 2026-07). A nucleated farming village exists to keep houses CLOSE to the fields they work; a household walking that far over empty unused ground is not how these settlements functioned, and the void served nothing.
  - *The root cause (non-obvious).* The seed SHAPE barely matters: `_place_bundle_nucleated` pulls every house to hug the paddy edge and then packs ALONG it, drifting each house up to ~400px from its seed. WIDTH is what that pull amplifies, so an over-wide seed cloud (the old crescent spread `t*ex*1.15`, the widest of the four shapes) strings houses into a stranded arc. A NARROW seed cloud (like `elongated`, the tightest-packing shape) stays compact. So the fix narrows the crescent's lateral reach (`t*ex*0.5`) and lets DEPTH carry the frontage - a deep narrow blob packs far better than a wide shallow ribbon.
  - *The check + its calibration.* `village_cluster_compact` measures the BUILT coverage (houses + gardens + yards + farmstead groves) of the house convex hull - the thing `cluster_abuts_fields` misses, because that check allows each house a cluster-span from the field, so a big hollow cluster passes. Measured coverage: the pathological arc ~0.20; the `roll_village` placer's healthy nucleated villages ~0.28-0.31; the tightly hand-placed villages (Hoshigaoka, Hikari, Ueda) ~0.40. Floor **0.25** sits clear below the healthy band and above the pathology. Village scale + >=12 houses only (a hamlet is legitimately loose; a tiny hull is degenerate). The pre-fix Kikuta manifest is frozen as `pool/regressions/kikuta-hollow-crescent.json` so the check keeps its teeth.
  - *Honest limit.* The `roll_village` nucleated placer tops out around 0.31 (the hug-and-pack-along design is looser than hand placement), so this is a floor that catches the pathology, not a demand for hand-placed density. The fix improved Kikuta's coverage 0.20 -> 0.31 and halved its span (948 -> 533px); a few back-row houses still sit ~350px from the crops, which reads as the honest back of a compact village rather than a stranded arc.

- **Threshing / drying yards are PER-FARMSTEAD and UNIVERSAL** (drives `harvest_yards_present` = 100%, `harvest_yards_on_sunny_side`, `_smaller_than_farmhouse`, `_clear_of_paddies`, `_clear_of_structures`; the near-square irregular footprint also feeds `garden_plots_are_quads`).
  - *Per-farmstead, not communal.* Japan processed rice at the individual farmstead, on the household's own packed-earth work yard - the *niwa* / *kadoniwa* / *maeniwa* (front yard). This is a real divergence from **many European farming villages, which shared a common threshing floor / threshing green**, and from the Mediterranean/Chinese communal threshing floor. So we do NOT draw one big village threshing ground; every farm has its own.
  - *Universal.* Every farming household had to thresh, hull, and winnow its own crop (hand tools: *senba-koki* threshing comb, *tōmi* winnower, *dō-usu* hulling mill), so a work yard was an operational necessity, not a luxury - hence 100% of farmhouses, density permitting (the generator drops only a farmhouse too boxed-in to host a yard at all).
  - *Sun, not the field, sets its side.* Rice must dry in the sun and *minka* faced south, so the yard is the south-facing FRONT yard. When the paddy is south it lands between house and field (the classic gradient); a northern paddy does NOT pull the yard onto the shady back.
  - *Relative size.* A household's real work yard was small - on the order of ~100-300 m² against a ~1-*chō* (~1 ha = 10,000 m²) holding, i.e. **~1-3% of the cultivated area** - so a threshing yard is much smaller than the paddies, never larger. On the map we draw it a touch smaller than the farmhouse, and the audit of 2026-07-21 VERIFIED this honest end to end: the drawn yard (~60 m² at village scale) is actually below the real 100-300 m² yard range and inside the true 1-3%-of-holding band, and the farmhouse itself is true-scale (an earlier version of this note claimed a "legibility exaggeration" that the current code does not perform). Drying *racks* (*hazakake* / *inagi*) historically stood in the fields; we fold a small indicative rack into the yard glyph rather than tracking field racks separately.
  - *Size varies (DOWN from a maximum), shape stays near-square.* The base yard dims are the household's MAXIMUM apron (sized to the harvest it must dry), so they jitter DOWN (a smaller holding needs less drying floor) - the inverse of the garden, whose base is its minimum and jitters up. The footprint is a slightly-irregular inscribed quad like the garden but with **LESS** corner jitter: a threshing floor is a deliberately-swept, tamped work surface kept roughly rectangular for flailing and mat-drying, not a hand-dug bed, so it reads near-square (`garden_plots_are_quads` validates both). At 1 px = 2 ft the generator lands ~40-255 m² per yard (the largest is the headman's capped apron), squarely in the ~100-300 m² band.
- **Dooryard kitchen gardens (*saien*) are PER-FARMSTEAD and UNIVERSAL** (drives `gardens_present` = 100%, `gardens_on_sunny_side`, `gardens_smaller_than_farmhouse`, `gardens_clear_of_paddies`, `gardens_clear_of_channels`, `gardens_clear_of_structures`, `gardens_clear_of_sheds`, `garden_plots_are_quads`, `garden_area_within_norms`; placed by `farmsteads()` alongside the yard).
  - *Universal, and a SIDE feature - not the south front.* Every farmstead kept a small intensive vegetable plot (*saien*) for the household's daily greens (*daikon*, onions, beans, herbs), so it is drawn on 100% of farmhouses (the generator drops only a farmhouse too boxed-in to host BOTH a yard and a garden). Crucially it does NOT sit on the south front: that ground is the threshing/drying **work apron** (the *niwa*, which must stay clear hard-packed earth for flailing and sun-drying rice). The garden takes a **sunny SIDE** instead - we prefer the **east**, the *doma*/kitchen end where the cook steps out to it, then the sunny **SE/SW corners** (each tried flush AND a little further out, to slip the garden past the south yard into the corner), and the **windward WALL itself LAST** (the west, for the default NW wind) so that wall stays free for the homestead grove's belt; **never the shady north back**. The windward CORNER (SW) is fine - it tucks below the grove's arm - it is only the windward *wall* the garden yields. This matters most for a farm whose EAST faces the paddy: its garden can't go east, so it takes the SW corner rather than the west wall, leaving the west for the grove (a west garden vetoing the west grove arm was the #1 reason a windward arm went missing). (So the historical homestead reads: grove on the windward N/W, house, garden on a lee side, work yard on the S front, paddy beyond - all four drawn, and the homestead SOLVER shifts the whole farm to a nearby spot where they all fit without overlapping rather than stacking the garden under the grove.)
  - *And clear EASTERN sky where a small nudge buys it (`gardens_unshaded_from_east`, GM 2026-07).* The garden goes on the lee/EAST side, but a NEIGHBOR's windward grove arm sits on that neighbor's W wall - i.e. just EAST of our garden - and would block its MORNING sun (the sun rises in the E). Two levers keep the east open: (1) the communal COPSE keep-out gained an EAST sun-lane beside its south one, so a scattered clump never sits directly east of a garden; (2) once every per-house grove is drawn, `_relax_gardens_south` nudges an east-shaded garden **a little SOUTH** - into open ground, so the tree falls to its NE and the eastern sky opens (the GM's "move it a bit south" remedy). It is BEST-EFFORT and an OPTION, not a hard slot: most farms keep the plain east garden; only the shaded, movable ones shift, and a garden boxed in to the south (paddy/lane/neighbor) stays put - so the check fires only on an AVOIDABLE case (still east-shaded though a clear south-shift existed). Two subtleties the implementation had to get right: the nudge clears EVERY east arm in one move (a small shift can otherwise slip a garden out of one arm's shade and straight INTO a taller arm just south - a 1-D interval fit, not "dodge the nearest tree"); and it tests REAL footprints, so a garden may drift into a neighbor's empty reserved-bbox MARGIN, it just may not touch a drawn house/yard/garden/grove. WHY: morning light matters for a kitchen bed, and the fix is placement (move the garden) - not felling the neighbor's windbreak.
  - *Three appurtenances, three sides - they never collide.* The farmstead's yard (south front), its **storehouse/*kura*** (WEST wall for a dispersed farm, the shaded NORTH wall for a nucleated-cluster house, on the ~30% of plain farms that have one - see the kura bullet above), and its garden must sit on DIFFERENT sides of the house. The garden yields whichever wall the kura holds (`gardens_clear_of_sheds` enforces no overlap). The kura is a **recorded annex** (`M['farm_sheds']`) reserved in the homestead bundle, so the check reads its footprint straight from the manifest.
  - *Off the water, too (`gardens_clear_of_channels`).* A raised-bed *saien* is dry-ground - it must not sit in a running irrigation line (a feeder CHANNEL, an in-field/drain DITCH, or a stream). `gardens_clear_of_paddies` covers the flooded basin, but the **drain outfall and feeder channels thread the DRY village margin** where the gardens are, so they were the gap this check closes. The fix is in the SOLVER, not just the check: `_rect_blocked` now treats every water polyline as a keep-out for the SOLID bundle parts (house/yard/garden/kura), so the homestead self-heals off a ditch (the grove stays exempt - it may hug a bund). Found on Ueda, where two field-edge gardens sat on the SW drain.
  - *Why a side and not the front.* The south apron is occupied by the work yard and must stay open; a kitchen garden tolerates partial sun better than grain-drying needs full sun, so it can take an east/west side. This is the historically dominant *nōka yashiki* layout (idealized - real plots bent to terrain/wealth), which is why the generator encodes *preferences* (sunny sides, east first) and places "where there's room," not fixed slots.
  - *Relative size.* Small - smaller than the threshing yard and well under the farmhouse (a kitchen plot, not a second field); drawn as a tilled bed with tidy planted rows, distinct from the tan work yard and the blue-green paddy quilt.
  - *Size varies, and is held to a HISTORICAL AREA band (`garden_area_within_norms`).* No two households worked an identical plot, so the garden's base dims (its MINIMUM - the least ground that feeds a household's daily greens) jitter UP, by a different fraction in each dimension (which also varies its proportions).
