The band spans ~7.7x because a commoner warren runs ~4-6x denser than a samurai/official ward (Edo land-vs-population inversion); the dead-zone guard applies only to PURE residential (a mixed quarter legitimately holds a civic forecourt).
  - `city_commoner_dwellings_inside_walls` - HARD ZERO commoner dwellings (laborer/servant/burakumin/merchant) outside the wall. Only samurai country estates, farmhouses, the wharf SHOPS, and gate-market shops are legitimately extramural (the guan-xiang/wharf/villa/farm categories); a lone commoner house outside defeats the wall and has no economic anchor. `population_consistent_with_housing` also counts IN-WALL dwellings only, so a generator cannot hit its target by spilling.
  - `city_civic_quarter_not_mostly_open` - a `civic` quarter may be up to `CIVIC_OPEN_TOL` = 70% open (a yamen/temple precinct is majority courtyard/garden) but must actually HOLD its compounds; open-and-structureless reads as merely empty.
  - `city_reserve_within_cap` - total `reserve` ground <= `RESERVE_CAP_FRAC` = 20% of the interior. Civic buildings alone are only ~3-6% of a Chinese county seat; the big open consumer is the drill ground plus under-built garden/farm, and ~20% (drill ground + gardens + an agricultural district) is historically conservative. Beyond it the wall encloses more open ground than a provincial seat justifies -> shrink.
- **The reworked verdict** (`city_capacity`, surfaced by `city_wall_sized_to_population` + `--capacity`): `enlarge` (can't hold target even packed), `shrink` (far more room than needed, OR only fillable via over-cap reserve - emptiness cannot be laundered as reserve), `densify` (wall right, placed below the population floor), `sized_and_packed` (done). `placed` counts in-wall only; `--capacity` prints the per-quarter density table so you see WHICH quarter is under-built. The `densify` boundary tracks `population_tol` so the capacity verdict and the population check never disagree.
- **Anti-trap discipline:** the pre-feature broken Nagahara is pinned as `pool/regressions/city_density_broken_nagahara.json` and MUST keep firing the new checks (a known-bad map that has to fail - the discipline the earlier aggregate model skipped). The band was calibrated against BOTH Tango (good, must pass) and that fixture (bad, must fail).

**Worked examples:** *Tango* declares 4 wedges (NE laborer residential; SE government mixed; SW merchant+temple mixed; NW split into an agricultural-district reserve above + a burakumin residential quarter below) and, per the GM's call, was enlarged a hair (uniform x1.015, RX/RY 480/450 -> 487/457) so its honest inside figure meets 3,000 rather than trimming the declared population - the earlier "hugged" ring had been faking ~12 dwellings past the wall. *Nagahara* declares 4 mixed/residential wedges; its formerly-empty NW temple quarter is filled by a MONZEN-MACHI commoner pocket (temple-town housing - historically a temple neighborhood was dense), which fixed both the emptiness and the population without enlarging the wall. Both cities: zero extramural commoners, every residential quarter in band, `sized_and_packed`.

  - *Known WIP (none).* Both worked cities (Tango, Nagahara) pass clean, per-quarter. Capitals are the next tier (a later task).

### Budget-first wall sizing (feature 009, `citybudget.py`)

Every settlement mode grows from a first principle - villages from water flow, manors from a declared square footage - and the city's is the **space budget**. The old order (guess a wall, place everything, iterate on the `city_capacity` verdict) converged on maps the checks accepted but the GM did not: the shipped Nagahara read fully green while ~17% of its interior (~116k px^2, five pockets >= 35k px^2) was unaccounted open ground, because every aggregate measure treats open ground as "fillable" rather than "unjustified". So the order is inverted: **compute the budget FIRST, derive the wall from it, and hold the drawn map to the promise.**

**The workflow** (see `specs/009-city-area-budget/` for the full feature):

1. `budget = plan_city(CityProgram(population=..., river=..., agricultural_district=..., aspect=..., nring=...), canvas=(W, H))` - BEFORE anything is drawn. Audit it with `python3 citybudget.py --plan --population 3000 --river`.
2. Take the wall from `budget.wall.rx/.ry` (never hand-pick RX/RY) and record the promise: `s.meta(budget=budget_to_manifest(budget))`.
3. Render order as ever (river -> walls -> roads -> ring -> ... -> packs), with the budget's `dwelling_target` feeding the same population/caste floors as always.
4. `city_wall_matches_budget` (walled-city gate) compares the wall's enclosed area against `budget.required_interior_px2`: over +8% = the empty-space defect (shrink, or declare+draw the ground as an itemized line); under -5% = the program cannot fit (enlarge, or trim the program). `city_capacity` must read `sized_and_packed` on the FIRST derivation - if it wants a resize, the budget model (not the wall) is what needs fixing.

**The model**: `required interior = (packed + spaced + civic + water + extras) / (1 - circulation% - agri%)`, then the wall is the ellipse **N-gon** enclosing exactly that (`0.5*N*sin(2pi/N)*rx*ry` - the drawn 20-22-gon's polygon area, NOT the smooth ellipse's `pi*rx*ry`, which would systematically undersize every wall).

**Historical grounding / the why behind each constant** (research: `specs/009-city-area-budget/research.md`; China first, jokamachi tiebreaker):

- **Inventory** from the budgets.md Provincial city caste table (600 families at pop 3,000: servants 120 / laborers 240 / merchants 150 / burakumin 30 / samurai 60; zero farmers unless an agricultural district overrides). ~2/3 of samurai families live in-wall (measured: Tango 33, Nagahara 41 of 60; the rest hold extramural estates per the estate doctrine).
- **Gross ground costs at DRAWN footprints** (legibility floors included - budgeting real-world square footage would undersize the wall): packed row dwelling ~690 px^2 gross (Tango healthy-quarter range 448-822), samurai house ~2,480 px^2 gross (measured samurai-ward ~2,915; the pair solves Tango's back-prediction to +0.2% while keeping the measured ~3.6x packed:spaced ratio).
- **Civic program is a FLOOR, not per-capita** - a pop-2,000 seat still carries the yamen, 6 ministries, temples, theater, gate furniture. Itemized at Tango's measured compounds (~64k px^2 total ~ 9% of interior; the historical civic share of a county seat is ~10%, range 5-15% - yamen 3-5% + temples/school 3-5% + granary/drill 2-4%, per Chang in Skinner's *The City in Late Imperial China*). The program also carries a small **adept-monk housing** line (5 x C_PACKED; GM 2026-07-24): 2-3 ordinary homes per temple precinct for the married adepts among its monks, real households OUTSIDE the lay caste table's 600 families (see "City temples" above).
- **Circulation 7% of interior at drawn widths** (measured 6.8-7.0% on both shipped cities). The historical envelope is 10-20% of ground (Chinese county seats ran deliberately sparse nets - Pingyao's "4 big streets, 8 small streets, 72 lanes"; Edo machi-wari grids compute to 13-18%) - but no source states the Chinese figure outright, so it is a triangulated envelope, and the MAP-calibrated constant wins because the budget must price what the maps actually draw (deep blocks + alley warrens sit at the sparse end).
- **Deliberate open ground must be DECLARED and DRAWN, never ambient.** The Chinese norm was 25-30% of the enclosure unbuilt (walls sized to administrative rank and growth expectation; intramural fields/ponds as siege insurance and flood refuge - Quanzhou still 1/4 vacant in 1945, Suzhou enclosed farmland into the Republican era). On a diagram that roominess reads as emptiness unless drawn as its kind, so the budget credits open ground only as itemized lines: the **agricultural-district toggle** (+15% of interior, Tango's measured declared reserve; inside the feature-006 20% reserve cap) or explicit `extras` lines (drill ground, gardens). A future city that wants the roomier historical character opts in legibly; it can never launder slack.
- **Tolerances (+8%/-5%)** are pinned by the two anchors: shipped Tango encloses ~0.25% under its budget (must pass); the pre-feature Nagahara encloses ~+21% (must fail - pinned at `pool/regressions/city_budget_fires_on_the_too_empty_nagahara.json`). Under is tighter than over because an undersized wall breaks packing immediately.

**Calibration provenance**: constants measured 2026-07 from `pool/provincial-cities/tango.json` (GM-accepted) and the pre-feature `pool/provincial-cities/nagahara.json` (GM-rejected); the back-prediction test in `test_citybudget.py` re-derives Tango's shipped 487x457 ring to +0.1% and is the regression guard on the whole constant set.
